601 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Sells v. Metropolitan Plan Com.


No. 30,901


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


248 Ind. 92; 223 N.E.2d 349; 1967 Ind. LEXIS 403



February 8, 1967, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 6, Mercer M. Mance, Judge.

Appellant, Dallas Sells, appeals from the denial of an injunction against the Metropolitan Plan Commission.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which denied his prayer for an injunction against appellee, the Metropolitan Plan Commission, that was sought on the grounds that An Act for the Development Through Planning and Zoning of Metropolitan Areas, Ind. Code Ann. § 53-902 et seq. (Supp. 1964), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant brought an action seeking to enjoin the Metropolitan Plan Commission, which had been established by An Act for the Development Through Planning and Zoning of Metropolitan Areas, Ind. Code Ann. § 53-902 et seq. (Supp. 1964). Appellant claimed that the Act was in conflict with Ind. Const. art. 4, § 19, which required that every act had to embrace but one subject and matters properly connected therewith and that an Act's failure to express a subject in its title rendered that subject not expressed void. The trial court entered judgment denying the injunction. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the title to the Act was sufficient to inform anyone reading the same that the Act related to the planning and zoning of metropolitan areas which zoning would, of necessity, be effectuated through local boards, which had to have authority to make appropriate rules and regulations, and to administer and adjudicate the same subject to appeal to the courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

602 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Phillips v. State


No. 30,849


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


248 Ind. 150; 222 N.E.2d 821; 1967 Ind. LEXIS 416



January 24, 1967, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 29, 1967.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Greene Circuit Court, Edwin B. Long, Judge.

Appellant, Francis Ernest Phillips, appeals from his conviction of sodomy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Greene Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of the crime of sodomy. The trial court overruled a motion to quash an affidavit.


OVERVIEW: The memorandum for the motion to quash argued that the charge was too indefinite and uncertain and did not point out with sufficient detail the particular act of sodomy with which defendant was charged in either count. Defendant also argued that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the verdict. In affirming the decision, the court found that the charge was sufficient. The meaning of the boy's testimony was left to the jury. The jury found defendant guilty. The evidence showed without question that defendant did entice, allure, and instigate the boy, age 14, to commit the act of masturbation. The evidence fully sustained the verdict that found a violation of Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-4221 (1956). Additionally, there was no showing that the prosecuting attorney knowingly used any perjured testimony. There also was no showing that defendant was in any way prejudiced by the time granted pursuant to Ind. Sup. Ct. R. 1-15 to the prosecuting attorney to file counter-affidavits to the charge that he was guilty of misconduct by using alleged perjured testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Williams v. State


No. 30,712


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


248 Ind. 66; 222 N.E.2d 397; 1966 Ind. LEXIS 443



December 29, 1966, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Vanderburgh Circuit Court, Robert J. Hayes, Special Judge.

Defendant appeals conviction of robbery.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction for robbery in the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which admitted evidence found in defendant's car after his arrest.


OVERVIEW: State troopers stopped defendant to check his operators' license when the troopers noticed a large wad of money in the vehicle. Defendant was arrested, and a search of his effects revealed currency wrappers from a bank. Defendant confessed to robbery, was convicted, and sought review. On appeal, the court was equally divided, and therefore the decision of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The equally divided court affirmed defendant's conviction and upheld the validity of the search of defendant's vehicle.

 

604 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Thorpe v. King


No. 30,899


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


248 Ind. 275; 221 N.E.2d 895; 1966 Ind. LEXIS 449



December 22, 1966, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted June 13, 1967.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens sought review of a judgment of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which denied their petition for an injunction to prevent appellees, officials of the Town of Cedar Lake, Indiana, from taking any action in their official capacities.


OVERVIEW: A petition to incorporate the Town was filed pursuant to Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 48-101 to 48-109 (1963), but certain residents did not receive notice by mail as provided by § 48-106. The citizens filed a petition with the Commissioners of Lake County to reject the incorporation petition, but the Commissioners adopted an ordinance incorporating the Town. The citizens filed suit challenging the ordinance, which was declared to be void because of the notice defect. The General Assembly then passed 1965 Ind. Acts 283, p. 779, which declared the Town's incorporation to be valid. The citizens filed the instant action for an injunction, but the trial court found that the Act cured the defects in the incorporation. On appeal, the court rejected the citizens' contention that the notice provision of Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-106 was "jurisdictional." The court expressly overruled Strosser v. The City of Fort Wayne, 100 Ind. 443 (1885), insofar as it was in conflict. The Act was a valid curative statute that did not unconstitutionally interfere with the earlier judgment or constitute special legislation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

605 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Carlson v. State


No. 30,840


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 631; 220 N.E.2d 532; 1966 Ind. LEXIS 418



October 18, 1966, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Lake Superior Court, Room No. 5, Newell A. Lamb, Special Judge.

Appellee, The State of Indiana on the relation of Frank A. J. Stodola, Judge of Hammond City Court, brought this action against appellant, George Carlson et al., as members of the Common Council of the City of Hammond, to mandate them to provide the funds requested by the judge for the operation of his court. From an adverse judgment appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city judge filed an action to mandate appellants, members of a city council, to provide the funds requested by the judge for the operation of his court. The Lake Superior Court (Indiana) entered a judgment for the judge, and the council members appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city judge prepared a yearly budget for the city court and its staff and submitted it to the council members for approval. The council members reduced the amount submitted, and the city judge filed an action to mandate the council members to provide the funds requested. The trial court granted the requested relief. On appeal, the court held that the statutes relating to the salaries of certain city court employees had to yield to the constitutional provision in Ind. Const. art. 1, § 12 that the courts shall be free and independent and able to function properly in administering justice. The court also held that the trial court properly ordered the council members to provide the requested funds because the city judge had authority to provide for the payment of expenses necessary for the city court's proper functioning and there was no showing that he abused his discretion in preparing the budget.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State ex rel. Board of Sanitary Comm'rs v. Superior Court of Vigo County


No. 30,975


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 617; 220 N.E.2d 336; 1966 Ind. LEXIS 415



October 11, 1966, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] This is an original action for writ of prohibition to prevent trial court from hearing and determining action for injunction against relators.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State, on relation of the Board of Sanitary Commissioners of The City of Terre Haute, Indiana, brought an action against respondent trial court seeking a writ of prohibition to prevent the trial court from hearing and determining an action for injunctive relief against the Board.


OVERVIEW: The Board sought to offer bonds for sale. Although they had adequate administrative remedies, various plaintiffs chose to wait until the day before the bond offer to file suit to enjoin such sale. The lawsuit rendered the Board unable to sell and deliver the bonds because the cloud cast on their validity by the refusal of counsel for a bonding house to approve the issue. The Board brought an action against the trial court seeking a writ of prohibition preventing it from hearing the injunction suit. The court held that, even assuming that plaintiffs in the case below had an adequate administrative remedy, the Board's proper remedy was to seek relief from the trial court, not to attempt to prevent it from exercising its authority in a case over which it had general jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court denied the Board's petition for a writ of prohibition.

608 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gilbert


No. 30,600


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 544; 219 N.E.2d 892; 1966 Ind. LEXIS 399



September 23, 1966, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion County Municipal Court Room No. 5, John A. Christ, Judge.

State brings question reserved pursuant to Section 9-2304, Fourth, Burns' 1956 Replacement, upon decision of trial court holding penalty provision of Section 47-2602b of Burns' 1965 Replacement unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Marion County Municipal Court (Indiana), which sustained defendant's motion for discharge on the grounds that the statute under which defendant had been charged, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 47-2602b (1965), violated Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with registering a motor vehicle without submitting a valid receipt from the county treasurer in violation of 1961 Ind. Act ch. 345, § 15, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 47-2602b (1965). When defendant filed a motion for discharge, the trial court granted the motion on the grounds that § 47-2602b was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the statute violated Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1, which provided for a uniform and equal rate of assessment and taxation. In reaching that conclusion, the court noted that it had previously declared invalid a portion of the Act of 1961, which provided for a tax of two per cent on the value of motor vehicles and mobile homes in lieu of the ad valorem property tax. Although statutes were to be construed so as to modify them where constitutional objections were presented, the court was required to declare the entire statute invalid. Because § 47-2602b expressly provided a penalty for the failure to pay the excise tax and it could not be severed from the remainder of the Act, it was invalid and defendant could not be prosecuted for the failure to comply with its terms.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

610 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


No. 30,784


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 490; 217 N.E.2d 588; 1966 Ind. LEXIS 386



June 22, 1966, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Hamilton Circuit Court, Edward F. New, Jr., Judge.

Appellee, Teddy Ray Clark, had his motion to quash two affidavits filed against him sustained. Appellant, State of Indiana, appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State challenged the judgment of the Hamilton Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained defendant's motions to quash the affidavits that charged him with violations of the Offenses Against Property Act, Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 10-3028 to 10-3041 (1965).


OVERVIEW: After defendant was charged with violating the Offenses Against Property Act by uttering a forged instrument, theft, and obtaining unauthorized control of property, the trial court suggested that defendant's attorney file a motion to quash on the grounds that the Act was unconstitutional. Although defendant's counsel was apparently confused as to the reason and procedure for the motion, he complied, and the trial court sustained the motion to quash. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that defendant was not entitled to relief because he failed to show that he had standing to contest the constitutionality of the Act. Specifically, defendant failed to show he was harmed or was about to be harmed by any unconstitutional provision contained in the Act. Further, legislation was presumed constitutional and the Indiana General Assembly had the power to define crimes and to specify the punishment to be imposed. After applying the ordinary meanings to the words within the title of the Act, the court noted that the offenses charged in the two affidavits came within the purview of the title to the Act and that the Act was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the action for further proceedings.

 

611 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Public Service Com. v. New York C. R. Co.


No. 30,733


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 411; 216 N.E.2d 716; 1966 Ind. LEXIS 374; 63 L.R.R.M. 2276; 53 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P51,491



May 19, 1966, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room 3, Glenn W. Funk, Judge.

Defendants appeal issuing of temporary injunction enjoining enforcement of 1937 Full Crew Law.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Public Service Commission of Indiana, its members, and other parties, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which granted a temporary injunction to appellee railroads enjoining enforcement of the Indiana Full Crew Law, Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 55-1326 to -1338 (1951).


OVERVIEW: The railroads sought to enjoin enforcement of the Indiana Full Crew Law. They alleged that the United States Congress's adoption of Pub. L. No. 88-108, 77 Stat. 132 (1963), preempted the field in which the Full Crew Law was designed to operate. The trial court granted the railroads a temporary injunction. The court took judicial notice of the fact that the United States Supreme Court, having determined that Pub. L. No. 88-108 did not supersede state laws and that classification according to mileage in state laws similar to the Full Crew Law did not constitute discrimination against interstate commerce, had decided those issues adversely to the railroads. The court held that the Full Crew Law was constitutionally valid. Even if the railroads' allegations of changed conditions such as the changeover from steam to diesel power, less-than-carload lots of freight, decrease in switching and flagging difficulties, and the use of longer trains and fewer stops, were true, the changes had existed for such a long time as to conclusively negate the railroads' ability to show either an emergency or irreparable injury. The trial court abused its discretion in granting the temporary injunction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and decree, vacated the temporary injunction, and remanded the cause with directions to the trial court to deny the railroads the relief sought.

 

612 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Zellers v. St. Joseph Circuit Court


No. 30,502


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 394; 216 N.E.2d 548; 1966 Ind. LEXIS 370



May 13, 1966, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by the State of Indiana on the relation of Donald E. Zellers, against respondents, St. Joseph Circuit Court and Joseph W. Nyikos as judge thereof, seeking to vacate an order dismissing relator's cause of action.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator malpractice claimant, through the State, filed for an alternative writ of mandate and prohibition against respondents, a circuit court and its judge, challenging the dismissal of the suit by the claimant as a plaintiff for malpractice. After dismissal, the claimant filed a motion to reinstate, which was overruled, followed by a motion to reconsider opposed by a motion to strike by the defendants in the underlying action.


OVERVIEW: The claimant filed the underlying suit based on malpractice involving the claimant's son. Well over a year passed after service. The circuit court then struck the case from the docket. The claimant then filed his motions seeking to have the suit reestablished. The claimant argued that the judge acted outside of his jurisdiction and dismissed the case pursuant to an unconstitutional local rule, St. Joseph County, Ind., Cir. Ct. R. IX. On appeal, the court favored the claimant. Dismissals had to be made pursuant to 1961 Ind. Acts ch. 224, § 1, p. 535, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 2-901 (Cum. Supp. 1964) or when there was a total lack of jurisdiction. A court had no inherent power to establish rules affected substantive rights and dismissing a suit for other reasons than those specifically in the statute or when there was a lack of jurisdiction. Because there was jurisdiction, the statute had to be followed. Further, an excusable neglect law did not apply. While not specifically declaring the local rule invalid, the court did find that it conflicted with the statute and failed to protect the rights of litigants.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ. The circuit court and its judge were ordered to vacate the order of dismissal, reverse and vacate the overruling of the motion to reinstate, and reverse and vacate a second order overruling the motion to reinstate. They were also ordered to reinstate the cause. The circuit court and its judge were prohibited from any further attempts to dismiss.

 

613 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Steers v. Miller


Nos. 30,606, 30,607


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 326; 216 N.E.2d 354; 1966 Ind. LEXIS 355



April 14, 1966, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Porter Circuit Court, Alfred J. Pivarnik, Judge.

State on the relation of Edwin K. Steers, Attorney General, appeals decision of lower court sustaining demurrer to complaint on grounds that statute is unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State, on the relation of the Indiana Attorney General, challenged the decisions of the Porter Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted the demurrers by appellee justices of the peace to the complaints by the State that the justices were unlawfully retaining fees. The justices challenged the constitutionality of 1957 Ind. Acts. ch. 322, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 5-130 (Supp. 1965). The two actions were consolidated for appeal.


OVERVIEW: The statute set forth the rules regarding the retention of fees of justices of the peace based on the population of a township. The justices argued that the statute was unconstitutional because it violated the rule against local or special laws because it created separate standards of compensation based on townships with less than 20,000 residents and depending on the number of justices in the township. The court on appeal held that the statute was not unconstitutional. However, the statute was applied in an unconstitutional manner. That was based on the fact that townships that had more than two justices would not have their income limited until the end of their terms of offices while justices in townships with two or less, as in the case at bar, would be immediately limited. Thus, justices elected at the same time in townships of the same size were treated differently. However, once the date in the statute was met, all justices were treated equally. The different standards thus became moot after that date, and the statute was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments below.

Callahan v. State


No. 30,807


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 350; 214 N.E.2d 648; 1966 Ind. LEXIS 361



March 9, 1966, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 27, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Criminal Court of Marion County, Division One, Eugene Fife, Jr., Judge.

Petitioner filed verified petition for writ of certiorari to review trial court's denial of belated motion for new trial.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a verified petition for a writ of certiorari challenging the denial of a belated motion for a new trial after defendant was convicted of murder in the first degree. An earlier motion for a new trial was overruled, which was affirmed on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot a police officer after his arrest for fleeing from a burglary. Defendant's claims in his petition included ineffective assistance of counsel, a violation of his speedy trial rights, the failure to consider an alibi, and general errors in the trial. On appeal, the court denied relief. The court first found that almost every issue raised by defendant was raised in the prior appeal. Further, he failed to object and preserve certain errors, including one that excluded the public generally from the courtroom and a challenge to the convicting statute as unconstitutional. Essentially, defendant was unhappy for losing rather than presenting viable issues. Defendant hired his own counsel at trial, and defendant was attempting to second-guess trial strategy. Defendant also failed to preserve the speedy trial issue. On the merits, an 11-month delay was not done to prejudice defendant. Defendant failed to file an alibi defense at trial.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition.

616 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Sexton v. Dunlap


No. 30,414


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 343; 213 N.E.2d 807; 1966 Ind. LEXIS 358



February 9, 1966, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 25, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Monroe Circuit Court, Paul R. Schnaitter, Special Judge.

Petitioners for injunction against Redevelopment Commission appeal denial of injunctive relief against redevelopment of certain area in Bloomington.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant class litigants challenged the decision of the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied injunctive relief requested against appellees, the city's mayor and the city's redevelopment commissioners, to enjoin them from continuing with a specific project for the redevelopment of a certain area in the city undertaken pursuant to the Redevelopment of Cities and Towns Act of 1953, as amended.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found in favor of the class litigants in their action challenging the urban renewal program that involved the acquisition of the named plaintiff's property and the property of others similarly situated. On appeal, the court dismissed, holding that not only had the Act been determined constitutional by the court in past cases, but that the class litigants had failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. The court ruled that failure to resort to the remedy provided by statute, and the attempted resort to the extraordinary remedy of injunction in lieu of the direct appeal provided by the Act, constituted a collateral attack on the actions of the redevelopment commission that could have been maintained only in the event that all other avenues of relief were forever closed or the commission had no jurisdiction in the first instance. The court found that nowhere had it appeared or had there been any allegation that the class litigants had resorted to the required procedure. The court concluded that the required procedure was to have appealed from the actions of the redevelopment commission under the Administrative Adjudication Act § 63-3001, et seq.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed in favor of appellees in the class litigants' action that sought to enjoin appellees from continuing with a specific project for redevelopment of a certain area in the city.

State ex rel. Red Spot Paint & Varnish Co. v. Vanderburgh Circuit Court


No. 30,794


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 296; 211 N.E.2d 181; 1965 Ind. LEXIS 328



November 4, 1965, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 7, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original action by the State of Indiana on the relation of Red Spot Paint and Varnish Co., Inc., and Anchor Supply Company, Inc., seeking to compel the Vanderburgh Circuit Court and Addison Beavers, Special Judge thereof, to permit relators to inspect books and records necessary to the preparation of their cause of action.



DISPOSITION: Petition granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State, on behalf of relator property owners, petitioned for a writ of mandate to compel respondents, a circuit court and a circuit court judge, to permit the property owners to inspect books and records necessary to the preparation of their cause of action against defendants, a city and a city redevelopment commission, to prohibit a proposed renewal area.


OVERVIEW: The commission approved an urban renewal project, which would result in the demolition of certain property. The property owners held real estate in the designated area and brought an action to prohibit the project. The property owners claimed that the property was not a menace, making the project inappropriate. The property owners petitioned the judge for discovery of the commission's books and records, and the judge ordered the discovery. However, when the commission and the city answered and objected, the trial judge overruled the order. The court held that 1965 Ind. Acts 140, § 1 amended Ind. Code Ann. § 2-1644 (1946) to make it mandatory that a judge allow the discovery of books and other papers that were not privileged. Because the discovery was not discretionary, the court found that it was error for the trial judge to refuse to order the city and the commission to hand over the commission's books. The court determined that the judge was prohibited from proceeding on the matter until such discovery took place.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition.

 

618 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hashfield v. State


No. 30,360


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 95; 210 N.E.2d 429; 1965 Ind. LEXIS 316



October 6, 1965, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 8, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Monroe Circuit Court, Nat U. Hill, Judge.

Defendant, Emmet O. Hashfield, appeals conviction of murder and death sentence.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied his plea of insanity, convicted him of murder, sentenced him to death, and denied his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who had three times previously been convicted of sex offenses, raped, killed, and dismembered an 11-year-old girl. Defendant alleged that the trial court's failure to grant his motion for a continuance violated his rights under the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments to the U.S. Constitution and Ind. Const. art. 1, §§ 12, 13. Specifically, he alleged that because he was not given an opportunity to examine the report of court-appointed doctors or interrogate them, he was unprepared to rebut their testimony that he was legally sane. Defendant also alleged that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury that criminal intent was willful intentional conduct to commit an act prohibited and made punishable by the Indiana Legislature. Affirming, the court held that defendant's claim of surprise could have been based on the testimony of only one doctor. However, since there was no inconsistency in the testimony of that doctor and that of defendant's doctors, defendant could not have been surprised by the doctor's testimony. Also, the court held that the proposed jury instruction was properly refused because it misstated the law and would have been confusing to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

619 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hammond City Court v. State


No. 30,601


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


247 Ind. 300; 208 N.E.2d 682; 1965 Ind. LEXIS 329



June 30, 1965, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 7, 1966.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Lake Circuit Court, Felix A. Kaul, Judge.

Appellants, Hammond City Court and Frank A. J. Stodola, Judge, bring action for review of order of Lake Circuit Court mandating appellants to grant appellee change of venue.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a city court and a city court judge, appealed from a judgment of the Lake Circuit Court (Indiana), which mandated that they grant appellee individual a change of venue. The individual had been charged with the violation of a city ordinance in the city court. He filed a timely motion for change of venue from the county, which motion was denied. Thereafter, he filed an action in the circuit court and obtained the order at issue.


OVERVIEW: The parties agreed that 1905 Ind. Acts ch. 129, § 215 (Ind. Stat. Ann. § 4-2401 (1946)), which originally provided for the establishment of city courts, provided that there be no change of venue therefrom except a change of venue from the judge. By 1951 Ind. Acts ch. 165, § 4 (Ind. Stat. Ann. § 4-2704 (1946)), the legislature authorized a change of venue from any city court to the circuit or superior court of an adjoining county. The circuit court rested its judgment on the authority of this statute. Appellants contended the judgment was contrary to law because the legislature in 1961 reenacted 1905 Ind. Acts ch. 129, § 215 which prohibited changes of venue from the city court, thereby repealing by implication the 1951 amendment. The court agreed. As a general rule, the mere reenactment of a general law did not repeal a law enacted in the interim that dealt solely with a specific aspect of a general law. However, the 1951 act was not a special law. The court found that the 1961 act expressly covered the subject of changes of venue from all city courts. Thus by implication it repealed the 1951 amendment and the individual was not entitled to a change of venue to another county.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment.

 

620 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


East Lake Lot Owners Asso. v. Prince's Lakes


No. 30,509


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


246 Ind. 333; 205 N.E.2d 821; 1965 Ind. LEXIS 357



April 12, 1965, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appellants, East Lake Lot Owners Association, Inc., have filed a "Petition to Reconsider" the Supreme Court's action in dismissing their case as moot.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant association filed a petition for the court to reconsider its dismissal of their action against appellee city as moot. The association had challenged a city ordinance regulating the speed of boats.


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance regulating the speed of boats on waterways. Several association members were arrested under the ordinance, which was later repealed. The court had dismissed the association's action against the city as moot since the challenged ordinance had been repealed. The association petitioned the court for reconsideration. The court denied the petition, holding that if, during the progress of a prosecution, the ordinance on which it was based was repealed, the prosecution had to fail, unless the repealing ordinance contained express provisions whereby all pending prosecutions were saved from its operation. The proceedings referred to by the association would have been be terminated by the city's own repealing ordinance. The association's fears of the lower court judgment becoming res adjudicata were not well founded as such judgment depended on an ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court denied the association's petition for reconsideration.

 

621 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Earle v. Indiana Nat'l Bank


No. 30,719


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


246 Ind. 251; 204 N.E.2d 652; 1965 Ind. LEXIS 347



March 3, 1965, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Hamilton Circuit Court, Charles W. Ardery, Jr., Judge.

Appellant, Cecil A. Earle, filed a petition to determine heirship in the estate of Everett W. Conn, deceased. The trial court entered judgment holding that the appellant as an adopted child could not inherit from his natural blood brother. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adopted child sought review of the judgment of the Hamilton Circuit Court (Indiana) holding that pursuant to the Indiana Probate Act, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 6-208(a) (1964), the adopted child could not inherit from his natural brother upon his petition to determine heirship filed against appellee administrator.


OVERVIEW: The adopted child was adopted by his aunt and uncle while he was a minor. The adopted child inherited property from them as their adopted child. Subsequently, the adopted child's natural brother died, and he filed a petition to determine heirship. The trial court entered judgment for the administrator, holding that the adopted child could not inherit from his natural brother. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court ruled that, under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 6-208(a) (1964), a child adopted as a minor was to be treated as if he were the natural child of his adopting parents and was to cease being treated as the child of his natural parents. The court ruled that the Indiana Probate Act did not violate the privileges and immunities clauses of Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23 or U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court stated that to treat the adopted child as his natural brother's sibling would be to treat him as the child of his natural parents in violation of the statute. Thus, the court concluded that the statute applied to collateral relatives as well as to descent and that the adopted child was precluded from inheriting from his natural brother.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment holding that the adopted child could not inherit from his natural brother.

 

622 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


In re Sobieski


No. 0-709


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


246 Ind. 222; 204 N.E.2d 353; 1965 Ind. LEXIS 344



February 17, 1965, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action filed by petitioner, pro se, entitled "Petition for Issuance of Citation to Public Defender".



DISPOSITION: Petition Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a pro se petition requesting that the public defender be cited to show cause for his refusal to represent the inmate in post-conviction proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The public defender filed a return stating that his refusal to represent the inmate was based upon the lack of merit upon which to predicate an appeal. The inmate asserted that his trial counsel was inadequate or incompetent in that he failed to assert the errors by filing a motion for new trial. The inmate urged that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 47-2001(b) (1952) was unconstitutional, that allegations of prior convictions for driving under the influence prejudiced the jury and deprived him of a fair trial, that a jury instruction was erroneous and prejudicial, that the trial court failed to instruct the jury that it was required to fix the penalty if it found that the inmate was guilty of the misdemeanor portion of the charge, and that the jury verdict indicated only a fine to which the trial court erroneously added an indeterminate sentence. The court concluded that none of the inmate's allegations constituted grounds for a new trial; therefore, counsel was not required to prosecute an appeal. The court concluded that the lack of merit in the petition sustained the public defender's refusal to represent the inmate.


OUTCOME: The court denied the inmate's petition.

 

623 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Levitt


No. 30,611


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


246 Ind. 275; 203 N.E.2d 821; 1965 Ind. LEXIS 350



January 25, 1965, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 15, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Monroe Circuit Court, Nat U. Hill, Judge.

Appellees, Ralph Levitt, James Bingham, and Tom Morgan, were indicted by a grand jury for the alleged violation of Section 5 of the Indiana Anti-Communism Statute. The appellees filed a motion to quash which was sustained by the trial court. From this judgment appellant, The State of Indiana, appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions to overrule the motion to quash.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision and an order by the Monroe Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained defendants' motion to quash after defendants were indicted by a grand jury for the alleged violation of § 5 of the Indiana Anti-Communism Statute, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-5205 (Repl. 1956). The trial court found that § 10-5205 was unconstitutional and that the objection could not be avoided by a new indictment and discharged defendants.


OVERVIEW: Defendants filed a motion to quash the indictment, based on the theory that § 10-5205 was invalid, primarily on the grounds that § 10-5205 had been superseded by federal legislation, namely, the Smith Act of 1940, 54 Stat. 670, as amended in 18 U.S.C.S. § 2385, and that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-5205 (Repl. 1956) violated defendants' freedom of speech and assembly. The court concluded that the United States Supreme Court's did not hold that the doctrine of preemption was applicable to Indiana's attempt to protect itself against subversive activities directed towards the violent overthrow of the state government. This was also the conclusion of most law writers on the subject. The court found that the "clear and present" doctrine had no place as a test of constitutionality. The most that could be said for the "idea" was that it was a principle applicable to the sufficiency of the evidence to sustain a conviction under the Subversive Acts. The court held that § 10-5205 was not defective because it failed to specifically state the prohibited act required to be done with guilty knowledge and intent. Such condition was to be inferred and it was thus not vague and uncertain in that respect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and the order of the trial court sustaining the motion to quash the indictment and discharging defendants. The court directed the trial court to overrule the motion to quash. The court remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion of the court.

 

624 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Metropolitan Thoroughfare Authority of Marion County v. Nutting


No. 30,640


Supreme Court of Indiana


246 Ind. 105; 203 N.E.2d 192; 1964 Ind. LEXIS 280



December 23, 1964, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 3, John F. Linder, Special Judge.

State of Indiana, appellant, appeals from an adverse judgment in a mandamus action, the subject of which was to compel continuing collection of Thoroughfare Tax on all motor vehicles in Marion County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged an order of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which entered a judgment for appellees, Indiana Commissioner of Motor Vehicles and Indiana Bureau of Motor Vehicles, in a mandamus action to compel appellees to collect a statutory tax and registration fee from owners of passenger motor vehicles.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a mandamus action to compel appellees to collect the Thoroughfare Tax from owners of passenger motor vehicles pursuant to 1945 Ind. Acts 304, § 64, amended by 1955 Ind. Acts 273, § 10. The trial court entered a judgment for appellees. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that in order for any provision of a repealed act to be adopted by reference, a clear legislative intent to do so was required. The court ruled that 1945 Ind. Acts 304, § 64, amended by 1955 Ind. Acts 273, § 10, was repealed by 1961 Ind. Acts 345, § 11 because § 11 set a contrary schedule of taxes and registration fees for all motor vehicles and it contained no provision for passenger motor vehicles. The court determined that there was no clear legislative intent to adopt by reference the former schedule for passenger motor vehicles. Therefore, the court held that appellees had no statutory authority to impose the tax and registration fee upon passenger motor vehicles pursuant to § 11. The court ruled that § 11 did not violate Ind. Const. art. 4, § 19.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for appellees in the state's mandamus action to compel appellees to collect the tax and registration fee from owners of passenger motor vehicles.

 

625 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Nott v. Bender


No. 30,697


Supreme Court of Indiana


246 Ind. 186; 202 N.E.2d 745; 1964 Ind. LEXIS 281



December 8, 1964, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 10, 1965.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the DeKalb Circuit Court, Harold D. Stump, Judge.

Appellant, Thomas W. Nott, in a paternity proceeding was adjudged to be the father of a child born to appellee, Eleanor Jean Bender. Appellant appeals.

Transferred from the Appellate Court pursuant to Rule 2-23 of the Supreme Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of a judgment of the DeKalb Circuit Court (Indiana), which, following a jury trial, adjudged him to be the father of a child born to appellee mother in a paternity proceeding brought under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 3-638 (1946) and refused his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that the trial court erred in refusing to grant him a new trial upon the ground of newly discovered evidence and erred in overruling his motion to exclude the child from the courtroom. The court affirmed. The court found that the two affidavits attached to the father's motion for a new trial were insufficient. Both affiants alleged only "personal relations" of others with the mother and the court did not know what that meant. The court stated that an affidavit alleging newly discovered evidence was required to set forth specifically the exact testimony or evidence that would be elicited at a new hearing from the witness or witnesses in question and should not have stated the same ambiguously or in a manner requiring inferences to be drawn from it to give it probative force. The court held that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 3-638 (1946) specifically stated that the trial court could admit those persons directly interested in the case. The court stated that it was difficult to imagine a person more directly interested in the case than the child for whose benefit the action for care, support, and maintenance was brought.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Steiner v. Ft. Wayne Community Schools


No. 30,484


Supreme Court of Indiana


245 Ind. 410; 199 N.E.2d 340; 1964 Ind. LEXIS 221



June 16, 1964, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the DeKalb Circuit Court, Harold D. Stump, Judge.

Appellants, Russell Steiner and others, were adjudged in contempt of court for violating a restraining order issued on behalf of appellees, Fort Wayne Community Schools and others. Appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, members of an original county committee for the reorganization of schools, sought review of the judgment of the DeKalb Circuit Court (Indiana), adjudging them to be in contempt for violating a restraining order that was issued without notice and without bond in the action filed by appellees, residents and taxpayers, to enjoin and restrain appellants from dividing a county school into two school corporations.


OVERVIEW: Claiming that appellants would make use of public funds, facilities, and services to divide the schools, appellees alleged that they would suffer irreparable damage and harm thereby in that they would be deprived of their property without due process of law. In conformance with appellees' request, the trial court on its own motion restrained appellants or anyone or anything else from in any way affecting the proposed plan until a special judge could be appointed. However, within the same order, the trial court refused to rule on appellees' application for a restraining order and disqualified himself due to his strong opinions on the subject. Subsequently, while awaiting a change of venue, appellants recognized a certification as to the proposed new school creation, adopted a motion to publish it, and authorized their attorney to publish it. These actions, appellees contended, warranted punishment for contempt of court. Ruling otherwise, the court held that the trial court's order was utterly void and a nullity for a lack of jurisdiction because no reason was provided for enjoining the provisions of the School Reorganization Act, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 28-6101 et seq.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

627 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Cottongim v. Congleton


No. 30,448


Supreme Court of Indiana


245 Ind. 387; 199 N.E.2d 96; 1964 Ind. LEXIS 219



June 11, 1964, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Washington Circuit Court, John M. Lewis, Special Judge.

Appellants, Ralph Cottongim and others, brought action against appellees, Elmer Congleton and others, alleging unconstitutionality of certain statutes involving School Reorganization Act. Judgment for appellees and appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, citizens, residents, and taxpayers of a township (taxpayers), challenged a judgment entered in the Washington Circuit Court (Indiana) in favor of appellees, the appointed members of a school corporation, in the taxpayers action alleging the unconstitutionality of the School Corporation Reorganization Act of 1959, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 28-6101 et seq. (1948), which established the school corporation.


OVERVIEW: Under the Act, a committee for the reorganization of the township's school districts was established. The plan was submitted to the county voters who approved it. The taxpayers filed an action alleging that the plan violated the Act and that the Act violated Ind. Const. art. 4, § 1, Ind. Const. art. 1, § 25, and Ind. Const. art. 1, § 24, in that it was an unlawful delegation of legislative powers, its "taking effect" was dependent upon a condition, and it was an ex post facto act which impaired the taxpayers' obligation of contracts. On appeal, the court held that there was no unlawful delegation of legislative power with reference to the administration of the school systems. The legislature had the discretion to determine how to organize and administrate the district. The fact that the plan was subject to the vote of the residents involved also did not render the Act unconstitutional. The court held that the Act was not an ex post facto law impairing the taxpayers' contractual rights by forcing upon them the contractual obligations previously executed by the other townships because the taxpayers were not parties to the contract and had no contractual interest therein.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of appellees.

 

628 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Lurie v. Indianapolis


No. 30,488


Supreme Court of Indiana


245 Ind. 457; 198 N.E.2d 755; 1964 Ind. LEXIS 226



May 26, 1964, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Dissent Filed July 1, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 4, Frank A. Symmes, Jr., Judge.

Action by appellant, Betti K. Lurie, for herself and on behalf of all others similarily situated, to enjoin appellees, City of Indianapolis, and others, from levying certain taxes. Judgment for appellees and appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer, on her own behalf and other similarly situated, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which entered judgment in favor of appellees, city and others. The taxpayer brought the action to enjoin the levying of taxes on her property pursuant to the Acts of 1919, 1919 Ind. Laws 144 (as amended).


OVERVIEW: The city council levied taxes on property outside the city to help provide for a county-wide park system. The taxpayer brought an action to enjoin appellees from levying the tax on her property, arguing that the statutes involved were unconstitutional. The trial court entered judgment for the appellees, and the taxpayer appealed. The court affirmed, holding that it was true that the city council could not levy taxes on property outside the city for general city purposes that in no way benefited the outside property, but when the taxes were for the benefit of the entire district, were levied on an equal basis throughout the district, and the money was expended by a board in which all the taxpayers of the district had representation, there was no discrimination. The statutes expanded the area of operations of the park districts to all the territory within the county, so it merely extended the boundaries of the city's Park District, and the power to levy taxes was continued in the city council, acting as an administrative agency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a decision which denied injunctive relief to a taxpayer in an action brought after the city levied taxes on her property that was outside the city.

 

629 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Harris v. Superior Court of Marion County


No. 30,478


Supreme Court of Indiana


245 Ind. 339; 197 N.E.2d 634; 1964 Ind. LEXIS 216



April 17, 1964, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 2, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original action by the State of Indiana on the relation of Joe A. Harris and others, relators, to prohibit respondents, Superior Court of Marion County, Frank A. Symmes, Jr., Judge, from exercising further jurisdiction in a certain action brought to enjoin Alcoholic Beverage Commission.



DISPOSITION: Writ of prohibition and mandate issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, members of the Indiana Alcoholic Beverage Commission (commission), filed a verified petition for a writ of prohibition to respondent Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which had entered a temporary restraining order enjoining the commission from promulgating regulations that authorized certain package liquor store dealers to sell beer.


OVERVIEW: A restaurant owner was a holder of a beer retailer's, wine retailer's and liquor retailer's permit (3-way tavern permittee) to sell alcoholic beverages. He filed his complaint against the state Alcoholic Beverage Commission (commission) seeking both a declaratory judgment and an injunction and restraining order, arguing that the commission should be perpetually enjoined from allowing package liquor store dealers from selling any iced or cooled beer. The trial court assumed jurisdiction and without notice, issued a temporary restraining order against the commission. On the commission's verified petition for a writ of prohibition, the state supreme court concluded that, by reason of the express provisions of Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 12-443, 12-445 (1956 Repl.), the tavern permittee had no property right and thus, no justiciable issue, that would allow him to judicially challenge the proposed action of the commission. Therefore, the superior court had no jurisdiction to review the regulations promulgated by the commission. The court then ordered the trial court to dissolve the restraining order issued by it.


OUTCOME: The court mandated and ordered the trial court to dissolve the restraining order issued by it, holding that the trial court had no jurisdiction to entertain a complaint by a tavern permittee who had no property right under the statute to assert a claim..

Browne v. Blood


No. 30,182


Supreme Court of Indiana


245 Ind. 447; 196 N.E.2d 745; 1964 Ind. LEXIS 225



March 9, 1964, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 1, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Gibson Circuit Court, Ralph A. Seal, Special Judge.

Appellees, Stephen A. Blood and others, filed petition to establish a levee and appellants, Margaret G. Browne and others, sought review of the judgment establishing such levee. Appellants appeal from an adverse decision.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant levee opponents sought review of the decision by the Gibson Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained appellee levee proponents' demurrer to the opponents' complaint for review of a prior decision by the trial court that, pursuant to the Drains and Levees Act, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 27-801 et seq. (1960), determined the benefits of the levee, approved and confirmed assessments for the levee, and declared the proposed levee established.


OVERVIEW: The levee proponents brought an action under the Act to create a levee. The trial court entered a judgment on September 23, 1959 confirming the assessments and declaring the levee established. The levee opponents filed their complaint for review of that judgment on December 22, 1959. The trial court sustained the proponents' demurrer to the claim. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the opponents' complaint was facially deficient because it failed to name two of the original petitioners in support of the levee in its complaint as required by Ind. Stat. Ann. § 2-219. The court also noted that the Act provided for a 30-day period in which an appeal from an order approving and confirming of a levee and assessments for it and, thus, the opponents' action was untimely. Moreover, although the provision in Ind. Stat. Ann. § 27-803 providing no right to appeal a final judgment confirming assessments was unconstitutional, the 30-day time limitation also found in that statute was not unconstitutional because the provisions were severable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment sustaining the demurrer.

No. 30,336


Supreme Court of Indiana


245 Ind. 628; 196 N.E.2d 896; 1964 Ind. LEXIS 246

DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order of the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), which issued a temporary injunction enjoining the city from continuing in eminent domain proceedings against appellees, a landowner and its tenant, and prohibited the city from carrying out its project which involved taking part of the landowner's property by eminent domain.


OVERVIEW: The city commenced eminent domain proceedings against the landowner, condemning a portion of its property for the purpose of widening an intersection. The landowner contested the condemnation and a hearing was held before the Board of Public Works. Ann. § 48-2117 (1963) setting forth the proceedings for a review of the Board's decision were unconstitutional because § 48-2117 precluded the landowner and the tenant from appealing the Board's decision in the supplemental proceeding. Appellees were entitled to appeal the Board's decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting the injunction and ordered the trial court sustain the city's motion to dismiss the temporary injunction, but granted appellees leave to appeal the Board's decision.

Martin v. State


No. 30,180


Supreme Court of Indiana


245 Ind. 224; 194 N.E.2d 721; 1963 Ind. LEXIS 245



December 17, 1963, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 16, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Vigo Circuit Court, Robert Howard Brown, Special Judge.

Appellant, Jack William Martin, was found guilty of assault and battery as a lesser included offense and sentenced accordingly. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Vigo Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of assault and battery as a lesser included offense of assault and battery with intent to gratify his sexual desires, in violation of Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-403 (1956).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of assault and battery with intent to gratify his sexual desires. The charges arose from a single incident involving a female child. On appeal from defendant's conviction, the court rejected defendant's contention that the trial court erred by not sustaining his motion to dismiss on the ground that more than three terms of the trial court had elapsed without trial, in violation of Ind. Stat. Ann. § 9-1403 (1956). The delay was caused by mandamus proceedings instituted by the State after its motion for change of judge was denied. Although the trial judge was named as respondent in the State's petition, defendant's attorneys represented the judge in the proceedings. Therefore, defendant could not deny that the delay was chargeable to him under § 9-1403. The court also rejected defendant's contention that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-403 violated the "plain wording" requirement of Ind. Const. art. 4, § 20. The court reasoned that any alleged error in the charging affidavit was harmless and moot on appeal because defendant was convicted of a lesser included offense that he did not contend was improperly charged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Lower court affirmed the allowance of the bond issuance and appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged a judgment from the Gibson County Circuit Court (Indiana), which ruled in favor of appellee county hospital in an action that challenged the right of appellee county Board of Commissioners to authorize the issuance of certain bonds for financing the hospital.


OVERVIEW: The county Board of Commissioners issued a proper petition requesting the issuance and sale of bonds for the purpose of giving financial aid for the construction, equipment, and improvement of the hospital as a not for profit hospital corporation. OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Board of Zoning Appeals v. Koehler


No. 30,262


Supreme Court of Indiana


244 Ind. 504; 194 N.E.2d 49; 1963 Ind. LEXIS 227



November 22, 1963, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Floyd Circuit Court, Paul J. Tegart, Judge.

Appellee, Mary Koehler, was denied an "Improvement Location Permit" to erect a Shopping Center on her property by the Building Commissioner. Appellant, Board of Zoning Appeals of New Albany, recommended the matter be transferred to the Planning Commission. By writ of certiorari appellee presented the matter to the trial court which rendered judgment in favor of appellee and appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowner applied to the building commissioner for an improvement location permit. After denial, the landowner sought review by respondent board of appeals. The board recommended transfer to the planning and zoning commission. The landowner responded by filing an action in Floyd Circuit Court (Indiana). The trial court found in the landowner's favor. After the trial court denied the board's motion for a new trial, the board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner argued that the denial of an improvement location permit for a shopping center was unconstitutional under the Fifth Amendment and Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution and Ind. Const. art. I, §§ 21, 23. In affirming the trial court's decision to grant the improvement location permit, the court held that the zoning regulations in question did not promote the public health, safety, morals, or welfare within the authorized police power of the state. As such, the court found that the invasion of the landowner's property rights was banned by the Fourteenth Amendment of the U.S. Constitution. The court held that the board attempted to impose an unnecessary restriction on the landowner's lawful occupations under the guise of protecting public interests. The court held that the ordinance in question was unconstitutional as applied to the landowner's property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that granted the landowner an improvement location permit to build a shopping center.

Indiana Toll Road Com. v. Jankovich


No. 30,109


Supreme Court of Indiana


244 Ind. 574; 193 N.E.2d 237; 1963 Ind. LEXIS 233



October 24, 1963, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 17, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Porter Circuit Court, Alban M. Smith, Special Judge.

Appellees, Nick Jankovich and Paul Jankovich, d/b/a Calumet Aviation Company, brought action for damages allegedly sustained from construction of toll road by appellant, Indiana Toll Road Commission, in violation of zoning ordinance regulating height of structures within certain area of airport. From an adverse judgment appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the toll road commission, sought review of a judgment of the Porter Circuit Court (Indiana), which rendered judgment in favor of appellees, lessees of an airport, who brought an action to recover damages for the encroachment of a toll road that was constructed in violation of a zoning ordinance regulating the height of structures within certain areas near the airport.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance at issue provided that structures within six miles of the airport could not be erected to heights that would interfere with the glide angles needed to approach the airport's runways. The lessees of the airport sought damages against the toll road commission because a toll road encroached upon the approach zones to the airport in violation of the ordinance. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment that was entered against the toll road commission because the reasonable and ordinary use of air space above land was a constitutionally protected property right and the ordinance violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 21 and U.S. Const. amend XIV by attempting to authorize an appropriation of the toll road commission's usable air space without the payment of compensation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that was entered in favor of the airport lessees and directed the trial court to sustain the motion for a finding for the toll road commission in an action regarding air space above the commission's property.

State ex rel. McGonigle v. Madison Circuit Court


No. 30,481


Supreme Court of Indiana


244 Ind. 403; 193 N.E.2d 242; 1963 Ind. LEXIS 210



October 21, 1963, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by State of Indiana on relation of Charles E. McGonigle and others, relators, seeking a writ of mandate against respondents, Madison Circuit Court, Carl T. Smith, Judge thereof, and also requesting equitable orders to assure that qualified voters are guaranteed the right to vote in the general city election in Anderson, November 5, 1963. An alternative writ was issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary mandatory injunction issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner voters filed a supplementary petition for a writ of mandate against respondents, numerous election officials, for equitable orders to assure the voters of a newly annexed area that qualified voters were guaranteed the right to vote in an upcoming general city election.


OVERVIEW: The voters filed the petition that sought the circuit court to name a special judge in a certain case. The voters also sought equitable orders against numerous election officials to allow all the qualified voters to vote in the next election. After the filing of the petition, a special judge was named. The voters filed a supplemental petition noting that the special judge only had 10 days to try the case and that, if he failed to do so, they would be prejudiced in the election. The court issued a temporary mandatory injunction, holding that the voters' voting rights could not be denied by any board created by the legislature, or through direct legislative enactment except as the Indiana Constitution expressly provided. There were no provisions within the Indiana Constitution that expressly authorized this limitation upon the right of vote as guaranteed in Ind. Const. art. 2, § 2. If Ind. Stat. Ann. § 29-3503 were construed as purporting to grant the right to vote to persons in territory annexed prior to September 1 and denying the same right to persons living in areas annexed subsequent to September 1, it would be subject to the constitutional prohibition against class legislation.


OUTCOME: The court issued a temporary mandatory injunction.

State ex rel. Blake v. Madison Circuit Court


No. 30,486


Supreme Court of Indiana


244 Ind. 612; 193 N.E.2d 251; 1963 Ind. LEXIS 239



October 21, 1963, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 15, 1964.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original action by the State of Indiana on the relation of relators, Harry P. An alternative writ was issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ of mandate made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator city official sought a writ of mandamus from a judgment entered by respondent Madison Circuit Court (Indiana), which held that Anderson, Ind., Ordinance No. 2345 was void. The court sustained the motion for intervention of State officers and residents of an annexed township area. A temporary alternative writ was issued on the official's petition.


OVERVIEW: The city council passed Ordinance No. 2345, which annexed a township. The residents filed a challenge to the ordinance with a superior court, which was dismissed because the residents' petition lacked the requisite number of signatures. The dismissal was affirmed on appeal. The residents filed an action for declaratory relief with the circuit court and later amended their action with a petition for an injunction that declared Ordinance No. 2345 unconstitutional. The circuit granted the injunction without notice to the city, its council, or the official. The official filed his petition with the court for a writ of mandamus that overturned the circuit court's order. The official asserted that an extreme emergency existed because the order denied 8,000 township residents their right to vote in a general election. The court rejected the residents' assertion that township farmland was improperly annexed for tax purposes. Ordinance No. 2345 was presumed valid. The circuit court's order was void for lack of jurisdiction because the residents had failed to serve the State Attorney General with a copy of the proceedings as required by 1927 Ind. Acts ch. 81, § 11.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the temporary writ issued to the official was made permanent.

 

641 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Welsh v. Sells


No. 30,442


Supreme Court of Indiana


244 Ind. 423; 192 N.E.2d 753; 1963 Ind. LEXIS 212



October 2, 1963, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 23, 1963. Motion for Leave to File Amended Petition for Rehearing Overruled October 30, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Marion Circuit Court, John L. Niblack, Judge.

Dallas Sells and Committee on Political Education, appellees, brought action against James C. Courtney, Revenue Commissioner, Matthew Welsh, Governor and Edwin K. Steers, Attorney General, for a judgment declaring sales and use tax law unconstitutional. Judgment was entered declaring the law to be unconstitutional and an injunction was issued. Appellants, Matthew Welsh, Governor, and James C. Courtney, Revenue Commissioner, appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state officials (the officials) sought review of an order of the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered an order declaring the Gross Income Tax Act of 1933 (the act) unconstitutional. Appellee political activists' (the activists) request for injunctive relief against the operation of the act was also granted.


OVERVIEW: The activists filed a suit seeking a judgment declaring that the act was unconstitutional, and they sought injunctive relief against the officials' operation of the act. The trial court declared the act unconstitutional and granted the activists' request for injunctive relief. On appeal, however, the court reversed the trial court and dissolved the injunction. The court held that the act's title was sufficient to notify those affected by it of its contents and application. The court further held that the exemption of certain classes from the act was not discriminatory and was reasonable. The court also held that the act was susceptible to both an intelligible and reasonable construction, so it was not unconstitutionally vague. Finally, the court held that although the act unconstitutionally delegated certain legislative powers to the department of revenue, those sections were severable from the remaining provisions of the act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed an order of the trial court, which entered an order declaring the act unconstitutional. The activists' request for injunctive relief against the officials' operation of the act was also granted. The court dissolved the injunction.

 

642 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Cassidy v. Indiana State Board of Registration & Examination


No. 30,174


Supreme Court of Indiana


244 Ind. 137; 191 N.E.2d 492; 1963 Ind. LEXIS 171



June 26, 1963, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Lake Circuit Court, Felix A. Kaul, Judge.

License to practice optometry held by appellant, Hugh E. Cassidy, was suspended by appellee, Indiana State Board of Registration and Examination in Optometry, which decision was sustained by Circuit Court. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff optometrist filed a petition for review of a judgment from the Lake Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained the decision of defendant State Board of Registration and Examination in Optometry suspending the optometrist's license to practice optometry for a period of six months. The Board had found that the optometrist guilty of unprofessional conduct pursuant to Ind. Stat. Ann. § 63-1010 (1961) and Ind. Stat. Ann. § 63-1018a.


OVERVIEW: An optometrist resided in Porter County but procured a license to practice in Lake County. He practiced ices in a room having the same outside door entrance, reception room, and receptionist, as an optical company, which carried cut-rate price advertising prohibited by Ind. Stat. Ann. § 63-1018a(e). The Board found the optometrist guilty of unprofessional conduct by knowingly practicing in a county, where he had no license and procuring a license in a county, where he did not reside, by operating a business on the same premises as the optical company, which was not licensed in such county, and by indirectly receiving financial benefits from the company's prohibited advertising. The optometrist sought review of the Board's decision suspending his license. On review, the court held that: (1) Ind. Stat. Ann. § 63-1010 (1961), which restricted an optometrist's practice to a single county, was unconstitutional; and (2) Ind. Stat. Ann. § 63-1018a, which defined "unprofessional conduct" as any other acts that the Board might find unprofessional would be deemed unprofessional conduct, was an abrogation of legislative authority, if relied upon by the board, and unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had sustained the Board's decision to suspending the optometrist's license to practice optometry, with instructions that the trial court restate its finding of facts and conclusions of law and enter judgment in accordance with its opinion.

 

643 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Keener v. Kendallville


No. 30,250


Supreme Court of Indiana


244 Ind. 87; 191 N.E.2d 6; 1963 Ind. LEXIS 163



June 11, 1963, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Stueben Circuit Court, Theodore T. Wood, Judge.

Appellants, Marvin L. Keener, individually and in behalf of taxpayers similarly situated, seek injunctive relief against a proposed off-street parking project of appellee, City of Kendallville. Trial court denied injunction and appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers brought an action for an injunction to enjoin the construction and establishment of an off-street parking program. The Stueben Circuit Court (Indiana) entered a judgment denying the injunction. The taxpayers then filed a motion for a new trial, a number of the specified items being improperly worded. Appellee, a city of the fifth class, moved to dismiss the taxpayers' appeal because no error was properly assigned.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court felt there was a valid basis for sustaining the motion to dismiss, but it determined the case on the merits. The court held that Ind. Const. art. 4, § 21 had no application in the instant case since it applied only to acts which purported to amend other acts, and 1959 Ind. Acts ch. 129, being Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-8482, the statute authorizing the off-street parking project, did not purport to amend any act. There was nothing unconstitutional in the Act of 1959 incorporating by reference 1955 Ind. Acts ch. 190, being Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-8470 et seq. There was no constitutional barrier to the application of the Act of 1959 in the case. Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 48-1247 and 10-3713, prohibiting common councilmen from being interested in contracts with the city, were not applicable under the facts of the case. The action of the city board of public works approving the off-street parking project was not invalid although a remonstrance by 228 persons was filed. The city was not required to have appropriated money for the return of donations made to be used to pay for the project in the event there was not a compliance with the conditions of the donations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

646 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Allen v. Van Buren Township


No. 30,194


Supreme Court of Indiana


243 Ind. 665; 184 N.E.2d 25; 1962 Ind. LEXIS 192



June 26, 1962, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 26, 1963.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Madison Circuit Court, Carl T. Smith, Judge.

Appellant, Wilfred Allen, for himself and on behalf of all others similarly situated, brought action to enjoin appellees, Van Buren Township of Madison County and others, from taking further action regarding issuance of bonds to finance school construction. Injunction denied and appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the Madison Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied an injunction sought by the taxpayer against the townships, a civil township and a school township, to enjoin the townships from taking further action regarding the issuance of bonds to finance school construction and equipment.


OVERVIEW: In seeking the injunction, the taxpayer claimed that the proposed amount of the bonds, together with all other outstanding indebtedness of the townships, would have exceeded the two percent debt limit in both townships in violation of Ind. Const. art. XIII, § 1. The trial court denied the injunction, and the taxpayer appealed, claiming that the trial court's decision was contrary to law. The court held that the two percent debt limitation was to be based upon the assessed value of the property, which was one-third of the true cash value, and thus, the proposed bond issue, when added to the present indebtedness of the townships, would have exceeded two percent of the assessed value of the taxable property in both townships. The court found that under the Indiana Constitution, the value for the purpose of determining the two percent debt limitation was to be the true or actual value of the property as ascertained or determined by the last assessment for state and county taxes. The court concluded that 1961 Ind. Acts 122, § 2 attempted to effect an increase in the bond limitation in contravention of the limit fixed by Ind. Const. art. XIII, § 1 and was, therefore, invalid and void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had denied the injunction sought by the taxpayer against the townships, with instructions to the trial court to issue the injunction as prayed.

State ex rel. Red Cab, Inc. v. Shelby Circuit Court


No. 30,220


Supreme Court of Indiana


243 Ind. 127; 183 N.E.2d 336; 1962 Ind. LEXIS 142



June 21, 1962, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by the State of Indiana on the relation of Red Cab, Inc., relator, for a writ of mandate against the respondents, Shelby Circuit Court, Harold G. Barger, Judge, commanding them to grant a change of venue and for a temporary writ of prohibition directing respondent court to refrain from exercising jurisdiction in certain cause.



DISPOSITION: Writ of mandate and prohibition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator cab company filed for a writ of mandate against respondents, a circuit court and its judge, to command respondents to grant a change of venue and to issue a temporary writ of prohibition directing respondents to refrain from exercising jurisdiction in an underlying action for damages.


OVERVIEW: In the underlying action for damages, brought against the cab company on behalf of a badly injured young girl, the cab company was granted a change of venue. A trial resulted in the jury being unable to agree on a unanimous verdict. The cause was set for retrial in the trial court. The cab company filed another motion for change of venue, alleging that there was widespread publicity concerning the case in the county where trial was to be held. The trial court overruled the motion. The cab company filed a petition for a writ of mandate to compel respondents to grant a change of venue and for a temporary writ of prohibition directing respondents to refrain from exercising further jurisdiction in the underlying cause until further order of the court. The cab company contended that the underlying case was subject to a change of venue by virtue of analogy to the situation where a case was reversed by an appellate tribunal. The court held that the cab company's analogy was inappropriate because no provision was made either by statute or the court's rules for a second change of venue and because no verdict or decision adverse to the cab company had been reached.


OUTCOME: The court denied the cab company's request for a writ of mandate and prohibition.
