State v. Hi-Jinks, Inc.


Nos. 29,898, 29,899, 29,900, 29,901, 29,902, 29,903, 29,904, 29,905, 29,906, 29,907, 29,908, 29,909,29,910


Supreme Court of Indiana


242 Ind. 621; 181 N.E.2d 526; 1962 Ind. LEXIS 233



March 29, 1962, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Allen Circuit Court, Louis H. Dunten, Special Judge.

Allen Circuit Court sustained motion to quash indictment filed against appellees, Hi-Jinks, Inc., et al., for alleged violation of the anti-gambling statute, on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional. Appellant, State of Indiana, appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a judgment from the Allen Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained defendants' motion to quash an indictment filed against it for alleged violation of the Indiana Anti-Gambling Law, Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 10-2329 to 10-2336 (1956), as amended by Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-2330 (1961), on the ground that the law was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The state brought 13 illegal gambling indictments against defendants. The indictments were based on the operation of pinball machines in publicly available places. The operation of the machines was said to involve the chance to win more than just the right to replay. Defendants filed amended motions to quash, which alleged that the Indiana Anti-Gambling Law, Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 10-2329 to 10-2336 (1956), as amended by Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-2330 (1961), was unconstitutional because it deprived them of equal protection under the law because of the distinction in Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-2330 (1961) between public and private venues. The trial court granted the motions. On appeal, the court set the judgment aside and instructed the trial court to overrule the motions. The court noted that it had already held that the challenged anti-gambling law was constitutional in a couple of recent cases. The public versus private classification was a reasonable distinction between a social past time and professional gambling that was inherent in the subject matter of the law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

Jurdzy v. Liptak

Supreme Court of Indiana


243 Ind. 1; 180 N.E.2d 530; 1962 Ind. LEXIS 122

Appellant, Cecelia L. Jurdzy, was awarded $ 12,000 in a default judgment against appellee, John Liptak, which judgment upon motion was set aside and vacated. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Lake Superior Court (Indiana), which upon appellee's motion, vacated and set aside a default judgment that had been entered awarding appellant damages for personal injuries.


OVERVIEW: Appellant obtained a service of summons on the Secretary of State as provided by statute. A default judgment was taken by appellant one day after the summons was returnable. Later in the day, after the default judgment was taken, appellee appeared and was granted two weeks to plead. The following day, appellee moved the trial court to set aside and vacate the default judgment. Several days later, the trial court set the hearing on the motion to vacate. Appellant appeared by counsel and objected to the hearing, but the objection was overruled. After the hearing, the trial court set aside and vacated the default judgment. On appeal, the court found that the default judgment had been vacated and set aside within the term in which it was entered. The record failed to show that appellant was served with any notice of the motion to vacate and set aside the judgment. However, because appellant had appeared and opposed the motion without making any objection to the failure to receive service of the motion, such error was deemed to have been waived. Moreover, the trial court's decision to vacate and set aside the default judgment was not a final, appealable judgment.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal of the trial court's decision to vacate and set aside a default judgment that had awarded personal injury damages to appellant.

652 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Finney v. Johnson


No. 30,162


Supreme Court of Indiana


242 Ind. 465; 179 N.E.2d 718; 1962 Ind. LEXIS 209



January 30, 1962, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room 2, Mercer M. Mance, Judge.

G. Weldon Johnson and Juanita Johnson, appellees, brought this action for a declaratory judgment and for an injunction against enforcement of an act providing that household goods shall be assessed at an amount equal to 5% of the assessed valuation of the improvements on the real estate in which the household goods are kept. Judgment was entered favorable to appellees and this appeal is taken by appellants, David D. Finney, Marion County Assessor and Carl T. Bowen, Washington Township assessor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxing authorities sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which entered judgment for appellee property owners in an action by the owners that sought a declaratory judgment and an injunction against enforcement of the personal property tax assessment law contained in 1961 Ind. Acts 325.


OVERVIEW: The owners sought a declaration that 1961 Ind. Acts 325, which provided that household goods were to be assessed at five percent of the assessed valuation of the improvements on the real estate in which the household goods were kept, was unconstitutional. They also sought to enjoin enforcement of the Act by the taxing authorities. The trial court found that the Act was unconstitutional and enjoined its enforcement. On appeal, the court upheld the judgment. Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1 provided that citizens had a fundamental right to the "just" assessment of their property for tax purposes. While there might be a relationship between the value of real property and the contents of a residence, it was too speculative to be the basis for a "just" valuation. Furthermore, the fact that an aggrieved taxpayer could obtain an on-site valuation of the household goods was not sufficient to make the Act constitutional. The court noted that under-assessed taxpayers were in a more favorable position than other taxpayers and there was no provision to equalize an under-assessment that resulted from the statutory formula.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

653 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. Steers


No. 30,148


Supreme Court of Indiana


242 Ind. 582; 179 N.E.2d 721; 1962 Ind. LEXIS 225



January 30, 1962, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 13, 1962.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 3, Robert G. Robb, Judge.

Appellants, Fred J. Wright and others, brought action for declaratory judgment and asked for injunctive relief against enforcement of Chapter 345, Acts of 1961, which provided for a tax of two (2%) per cent on value of motor vehicles and mobile homes in lieu of ad valorem property tax. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the act, denied appellants relief, and they appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged the order from the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which denied them injunctive relief in their action to prevent appellee public officials from enforcing 1961 Ind. Acts ch. 345 (Act).


OVERVIEW: The Act provided for a tax of two percent on the value of motor vehicles and mobile homes in lieu of an ad valorem property tax. The taxpayers sought to prevent the public officials from enforcing the Act. The trial court ruled that the Act was constitutional. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that the legislation was an ad valorem tax and failed to comply with Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1, which required an equal and uniform rate for all ad valorem property taxes. The Act's fixed tax rate of two percent of the value of the motor vehicle was neither uniform nor equal with the general tax rate established annually on all property. The Act exempted motor vehicles from the general property tax, which ran afoul of art. 10, § 1's provision that prevented any exemptions from ad valorem property tax except property used for municipal, education, literary, scientific, religious or charitable purposes. The Indiana Constitution did not permit an expressed exemption of any property from the general property tax rate other than that specifically named in Ind. Const. art. 10, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied the taxpayers injunctive relief in their action to prevent the public officials from enforcing the Act and directed the trial court to enter judgment for the taxpayers.

Orbison v. Welsh


No. 30,147


Supreme Court of Indiana


242 Ind. 385; 179 N.E.2d 727; 1962 Ind. LEXIS 206

Markleville v. Markle


No. 30,088


Supreme Court of Indiana


242 Ind. 322; 179 N.E.2d 279; 1962 Ind. LEXIS 201



January 4, 1962, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Madison County Superior Court, Henry P. Schrenker, Judge.

Town of Markleville, appellant, brought this suit to condemn real estate and right of way for a sewage treatment plant and sanitary sewer. Appellees, Christina E. Markle and others, filed objections to the proceedings. Judgment was rendered favorable to appellees and appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town sought review of a decision from the Madison County Superior Court (Indiana), which rendered judgment in favor of appellee landowners in an action brought by the town to condemn real estate and right of way for a sewage treatment plant and a sanitary sewer.


OVERVIEW: In 1951 a convention was called to nominate three trustees of the town. The nominees assumed office, although no election was held in November. The nominees and their successors continuously held themselves out as officers of the town although no conventions were held in 1955 or 1959. The town brought suit to condemn real estate and right of way for a sewage treatment plant and a sanitary sewer. The landowners filed objections to the proceedings, stating that the town's trustees were not duly elected. The trial court held in favor of the landowners and overruled the town's motion for a new trial. The town contended that the trial court erred in permitting a collateral attack on the town's condemnation suit. The court held that: (1) the nominees of the 1951 convention held sufficient color of title to the offices they assumed to constitute them de facto officers of the town; (2) where the provisions of Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-118 (1950 Repl.) were complied with when vacancies occurred by resignation, the present officers of the town constituted de facto officers thereof; and (3) where the town officers were de facto officers, the town had authority to maintain the condemnation action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision with directions to sustain the town's motion for a new trial.

 

656 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Little v. Ritchey


No. 29,973


Supreme Court of Indiana


241 Ind. 587; 174 N.E.2d 52; 1961 Ind. LEXIS 168



April 25, 1961, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Vigo County, Lloyd C. Adamson, Special Judge.

Ora Little, appellant, brought an action for possession of real property. Appellees, Earl O. Miller and Irma Miller, were granted permission to intervene and judgment was entered favorable to appellees. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant purchaser sought review of a judgment from the Vigo Superior Court (Indiana), which set aside a conveyance by tax deed in favor of appellee landowners. The landowners were also decreed the owners in fee simple on their cross-complaint after paying a penalty and interest to the purchaser.


OVERVIEW: The county auditor certified the real estate as delinquent for non-payment of taxes. Notice was sent to the landowners, and it was published in a newspaper of general circulation. The purchaser bought the property at a public sale, and he received a deed after the redemption period had expired. Later, the landowners attempted to tender payment to the purchaser. After payment was rejected, the landowners deposited the payment in the clerk's office. On review, the court noted that when a conclusive presumption existed, the legislature could not constitutionally declare a tax deed conclusive evidence of a valid sale. Therefore, the court found that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 64-2203 (1951) could not be applied because it stated that a deed to land was conclusive evidence that the sale met the legal requirements. The court held that the sale had several irregularities. The court reasoned that the property was sold for taxes that were not yet delinquent for a period of 15 months, as required by § 64-2203. In affirmance, the court concluded that the function of determining whether mistake, error, or fraud had produced an instrument that appeared correct on its face, was a judicial act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment.

 

657 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Keene v. Michigan City


No. 30,029


Supreme Court of Indiana


241 Ind. 592; 174 N.E.2d 48; 1961 Ind. LEXIS 169



April 25, 1961, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the La Porte Circuit Court, Felix A. Kaul, Special Judge.

Appellee, The City of Michigan City, by its common council, adopted an ordinance to annex contiguous territory. Appellants, Raymond Keene et al., filed their remonstrance to such ordinance. The trial court sustained a motion to dismiss proceedings and from a judgment dismissing the proceedings appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a judgment from the La Porte Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed their motion to reconsider in favor of appellee Michigan City (Indiana) in a remonstrance action to an annexation ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The City adopted an annexation ordinance. The mayor approved the ordinance and notice was given. The property owners then filed their remonstrance. A special judge was elected, and the City filed a motion to dismiss. The motion to dismiss was sustained, and the property owners' motion to reconsider was dismissed. On review, the court found that there was nothing in the record showing that the circuit court did not determine the sufficiency of the remonstrance. The court stated that, in the absence of such a showing, it was presumed that the circuit court complied with Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-702 (1960). The court held that it was improper for the property owners to serve notice upon the council. The court determined that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 2-804(a) did not state who were the proper officers to receive service in an annexation proceeding. Therefore, the court reasoned that the term "proper officers" meant those officers designated in the general statute providing for the service of process against corporations. The court further held that the circuit court did not lose jurisdiction when it failed to hold a hearing on the remonstrance because the statute was not mandatory.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment with instructions to reassume jurisdiction of the case, and for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

658 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Fruit v. Metropolitan School Dist.


No. 30,005


Supreme Court of Indiana


241 Ind. 621; 172 N.E.2d 864; 1961 Ind. LEXIS 175



March 9, 1961, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Reinstating Opinion of March 9, 1961 Filed May 8, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Randolph Circuit Court, John W. Macy, Judge.

William Fruit and others, appellants, filed action for declaratory judgment asking that the School Reorganization Act be declared invalid. Appellees' demurrer to each of the two paragraphs of complaint was sustained and judgment accordingly. Appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant complainants sought review of an order of the Randolph Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained the demurrer of appellees, a school district and other parties, in the complainants' action challenging the constitutionality of the School Reorganization Act of 1959, 1959 Ind. Acts 261.


OVERVIEW: An election was held pursuant to the Act to determine whether the public schools of a township and a city should be consolidated. A majority of the voters of the township voted against consolidation, and a majority of the voters of the city voted for consolidation. The combined total vote was in favor of consolidation. A corporation assumed charge of a consolidated school district pursuant to the Act. The complainants filed an action against appellees challenging the constitutionality of the Act. The trial court sustained appellees' demurrer. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that the Act was valid whether it was adopted by a de facto or de jure General Assembly because the actions of de facto officers could not be collaterally attacked. The court determined that the General Assembly had broad authority to prescribe the method for the consolidation of schools. The court ruled that the General Assembly had the authority to levy taxes for school purposes or to delegate that authority to the corporation that managed the consolidated school district. Therefore, the court held that the Act was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order sustaining appellees' demurrer in the complainants' action challenging the constitutionality of the Act.

Board of Zoning Appeals v. Schulte


No. 29,919


Supreme Court of Indiana


241 Ind. 339; 172 N.E.2d 39; 1961 Ind. LEXIS 143



February 7, 1961, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, M. Walter Bell, Special Judge.

Appellee, Paul C. Schulte, Archbishop of the Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Indianapolis, petitioned appellant Board of Zoning Appeals of the Town of Meridian Hills for the purpose of building a church-school and related facilities. The petition was denied and the trial court upon administrative appeal reversed the action of the Board. The Board and certain remonstrators appeal.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with instruction to restate findings and modify judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Board of Zoning Appeals of the Town of Meridian Hills (board) and remonstrators, sought review of the adverse ruling of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which reversed the decision of the board that denied the petition of appellee church to build a church, school, and related facilities on land it owned in an area zoned primarily for residential use.


OVERVIEW: The board denied the petition of the church to build a church, school, and related facilities on its land because the project would have had depreciated the value of the residential property bordering it. The trial court found that there was not substantial evidence to support the contention that depreciation in value would have occurred. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court decision that the board erroneously denied the church's petition. The court held that depreciation of adjacent homes was not a constitutionally valid reason for excluding the proposed church and its facilities. The court held that the state and federal constitutions provided for freedom of worship and encouragement of education and board did not have the authority to exclude churches or schools in residence districts. The court noted that it was never intended that zoning laws should be used for the purpose of creating special privileges or private rights in property from creating an exclusive community.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that reversed the denial by the board of the church's petition to build on its property. The court remanded for modification of the judgment to reflect the improper grant by the trial court to the board of a writ of mandate.

 

660 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kuebel


No. 29,920


Supreme Court of Indiana


241 Ind. 268; 172 N.E.2d 45; 1961 Ind. LEXIS 137



January 31, 1961, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From The Marion Criminal Court, Division One. Richard M. Salb, Judge.

Appellant, State of Indiana, prosecutes an appeal from a judgment sustaining a motion to quash an amended affidavit charging appellee, Ray Joseph Kuebel, with the possession and sale of obscene matters in violation of statute.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the decision from the Marion Criminal Court, Division One (Indiana), which granted defendant's motion to quash the amended affidavit charging defendant with a violation of Ind. § 10-2803 (Cum. Supp. 1960) for the possession and sale of obscene matters. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute.


OVERVIEW: The state argued that the statute did not eliminate a scienter requirement and was constitutional. The supreme court affirmed. Based upon legislative intent, the statute was interpreted as a strict liability law since a knowledge requirement was specifically exempted. While strict liability penal statutes were constitutional in certain areas, they were not when questions of freedom of speech and of the press were at issue. Section 10-2803 violated the First Amendment, the Fourteenth Amendment, and Ind. Const. art. I, § 9 under a balancing test between the right of the state to exercise its police powers to prevent the sale of obscenity and free speech and expression. Since the statute imposed strict liability, it acted as a form of self-censorship of written materials. The invalid portion of the statute made the entire statute void.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the criminal court quashing the affidavit was affirmed. The affidavit was based on an unconstitutional obscenity statute.

 

661 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Butler v. Allen Circuit Court


No. 29,967


Supreme Court of Indiana


241 Ind. 627; 170 N.E.2d 663; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 170



December 7, 1960, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted May 9, 1961.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original action by State of Indiana on relation of John Daniel Butler, relator, seeking a writ of mandate to compel Allen Circuit Court, respondent, to furnish relator a transcript and bill of exceptions to enable relator to take an appeal at public expense of a conviction for robbery. An alternative writ was issued.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator brought an original action for a writ of mandate to compel respondent trial court to furnish him with a transcript and bill of exceptions to enable relator to take an appeal at public expense from a conviction for robbery. An alternative writ was issued.


OVERVIEW: Relator was a minor who was charged, tried, and convicted of robbery. The relator's request for a transcript and bill of exceptions at public expense was denied, and he filed a petition for a writ of mandate to compel the trial court to grant his request. The petition was denied. Relator brought an original proceeding in the court for a writ of mandate, and an alternative writ issued. On consideration, the court made its writ permanent. The court noted that Ind. Code Ann. § 4-3511 required that an accused be provided with a transcript at public expense if he lacked the means to pay for it. The court noted that parents were legally obligated to provide necessaries for their children, which included criminal defense expenses. The court ruled that a dependent child whose parents were able to pay for his necessary legal expenses was not considered to be a pauper under § 4-3511. The court also ruled that relator's constitutional right to a trial record for an appeal required more than a cursory inquiry into his ability to pay. Because relator's affidavits were contradicted solely by extraneous information, the court remanded the case to allow further evidence to be taken.


OUTCOME: The court made the alternative writ of mandate permanent. The court set aside the trial court's order denying relator's petition for an order directing the trial court to furnish him with a transcript and bill of exceptions and remanded the cause to the trial court for further evidence, findings, and determination.

 

662 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


McCoy v. State


No. 29,850


Supreme Court of Indiana


241 Ind. 104; 170 N.E.2d 43; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 143



November 15, 1960, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Vigo Circuit Court, Herbert R. Criss, Judge.

Margaret Annabelle McCoy, appellant, was convicted of receiving stolen goods. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Vigo Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted defendant of receiving stolen goods in violation of Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-3017 (1956).


OVERVIEW: After hiding property that was stolen by her son and an accomplice, defendant was convicted of receiving stolen goods. Upon review, the court rejected the contention that the mother-son relationship made defendant immune from prosecution because neither the accessory after the fact statute nor the concealing a felon statute was applicable. The court also held that there was no evidence that the son had coerced the mother. Moreover, notwithstanding that a thief's confessions were inadmissible against one receiving stolen property, the court held that statements made by the son in the presence of defendant, his mother, were admissible. The court also held that when a confession gave information as to where stolen property could be found, the property's discovery was admissible even if the confession was not. Furthermore, the court held that because defendant was not charged as an accessory, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 9-1603, which required the accomplice's consent to testify, was inapplicable. Finally, the court refused to find an unconstitutional search because there was no actual search of defendant's house and because defendant lacked standing to challenge the search of her son's house.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Datisman v. Gary Public Library


No. 29,897


Supreme Court of Indiana


241 Ind. 83; 170 N.E.2d 55; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 140



November 2, 1960, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Lake Circuit Court, Felix A. Kaul, Judge.

Don Datisman, for himself and others similarly situated, appellant, brought this action against appellees, Gary Public Library and members of the board thereof, to enjoin any action to issue and sell bonds for the purpose of providing funds for the construction and equipment of a new library building. Judgment was made favorable to appellees and appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the decision of the Lake Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered judgment for appellees, public library and board members, in the taxpayer's action, for himself and on behalf of all other persons similarly situated, to enjoin appellees from taking any action to issue and sell bonds for the purpose of providing funds to defray the cost of the construction and equipment of a new main library building.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer contended that the Library Law of 1947, Ind. Code §§ 41-901 - 41-921, violated certain provisions of the Indiana Constitution. The taxpayer contended that the creation of separate public corporations for the establishment of libraries was an attempt to evade the constitutional debt limitation in violation of Ind. Const. art. 13, § 1. The court rejected this contention, holding that the creation of library districts in Indiana as public corporations for library purposes, separate and distinct from the civil or municipal corporations, was not prohibited by the Indiana Constitution and was a valid exercise of legislative power. The court rejected the taxpayer's contention that the Library Law of 1947, was invalid for the reasoned that it deprived the people of the library district of their right of local self-government. The taxpayer contended that the Act provided for the appointment instead of the election of members of the Library Board. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that while the legislature has no right or power to appoint municipal officers, it did have to power to enact laws prescribing the manner of selection and the duties of such officers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for appellees in the taxpayer's action to enjoin appellees from issuing and selling bonds to provide funds to defray the cost of the construction of a new library building.

 

664 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Marion County Election Board v. O'Brien


No. 29,962


Supreme Court of Indiana


241 Ind. 36; 169 N.E.2d 287; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 136



September 26, 1960, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Circuit Court, John L. Niblack, Judge.

Appellant, Edwin McClure, upon the death of the incumbent in April, 1959, was appointed by the Governor to the office of the Clerk of the Marion Circuit Court. Jack O'Brien and others, appellees, brought this action under the Uniform Declaratory Judgment Act to determine the right and duties of the Marion County Election Board as they relate to the election of a Clerk of the Marion Circuit Court, at the general election to be held on November 8, 1960. The trial court held that an election for such office should be held at the primary and general election of 1960 and that the person elected shall serve a four-year term beginning January 1, 1961. Appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Governor and others, sought review of an order from the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), which held that an election for such office should have been held at the primary and general election of 1960 and that the person elected should serve a four-year term in an election contest with appellees.


OVERVIEW: Appellants asserted that the question of whether or not a Clerk of the Marion Circuit Court should have been elected at the general election to have been held in November was fully and completely answered by the provisions of Ind. Code § 49-2702. The court could not see where any constitutional rights of appellees would have been violated if a Clerk of the Marion Circuit Court was not elected at the general election. Section 49-2702 did not under the factual situation presented, violate any of the provisions of Ind. Const. art. 1, § 1. The Legislature had complied fully with the mandate of Ind. Const. art. 6, § 9 by prescribing by law for the filling of vacancies in the office of the Clerk of the Circuit Court. For those reasons the provisions of that section were not violated by Ind. Code § 49-2702. The court concluded that § 49-2702 was a valid enactment of the Legislature, that it was now in full force and effect and governed the term for which the Governor was appointed to fill the vacancy that then existed in the office of the Clerk of the Marion Circuit Court, and that no vacancy then existed in such office.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and ordered the clerk to certify its opinion to the trial court.

Evansville-Vanderburgh Levee Authority Dist. v. Kamp


No. 29,912


Supreme Court of Indiana


240 Ind. 659; 168 N.E.2d 208; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 241



July 5, 1960, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Vanderburgh County, Addison M. Beavers, Special Judge.

King Kamp, appellee, brought action in declaratory judgment seeking to establish the unconstitutionality of Chapter 289, Acts of 1959. The trial court granted an injunction against operation of said act for the creation of a levee authority as applicable to City of Evansville and Vanderburgh County, declaring the act invalid and unconstitutional. From such judgment appeal is taken by appellees, Evansville-Vanderburgh Levee Authority District and others, members thereof.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a levee district and others, sought review of a judgment of the Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana), which held that 1959 Ind. Acts 289 was unconstitutional and enjoined the operation of the levee district pursuant to the act in appellee taxpayer's declaratory judgment action challenging the act.


OVERVIEW: 1959 Ind. Acts 289 provided for the creation of a joint city-county levee authority district by counties having a population of not less than 160,000 or more than 180,000 upon adoption of ordinances by the city and county. A city and county created the levee district pursuant to the act. The taxpayer filed a declaratory judgment action against appellants challenging the constitutionality of the act. The trial court held that the act was an unconstitutional special or local law in violation of Ind. Const. art. IV, §§ 22, 23 and enjoined the operation of the levee district. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings. The court held that a law that contained a classification based upon population was not an unconstitutional special or local law so long as there was some relationship between the classification and the objective of the law. The court determined that the method of distributing and levying assessments for local improvements was a matter of legislative discretion. The court ruled that the act did not violate §§ 22, 23 because the classification was not purely arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment holding that the act was unconstitutional and enjoining the operation of the levee district. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

Murley v. State


No. 29,893


Supreme Court of Indiana


240 Ind. 655; 168 N.E.2d 205; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 240



July 1, 1960, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Clark Circuit Court, Owen Voight, Special Judge.

Appellants, Al Murley and Harlow Conklin, were convicted of possessing gambling devices, known as pinball machines, in violation of § 10-2332, Burns' 1956 Replacement. Appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the Clark Circuit Court (Indiana), which overruled their motion in arrest of judgment and convicted them of possessing gambling devices, known as pinball machines, in violation of Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-2332 (1956).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were arraigned and convicted under affidavits alleging that they unlawfully, wrongfully, and knowingly kept and possessed pinball machines in a restaurant for use by the public in violation of the statute prohibiting gambling devices equipped with automatic recording devices providing the right to replay. They argued that their motion in arrest of judgment should have been granted because the original affidavits were insufficient in failing to charge intent, knowledge, and possession. They also alleged that their motion for a new trial was improperly overruled. In affirming the convictions, the court held that any insufficiency in the original affidavits was immaterial where defendants were convicted under affidavits that sufficiently charged intent, possession, and knowledge through the affirmative allegations that they knowingly possessed the machines. Because the motion for a new trial was filed more than 30 days after the verdict was returned, it was untimely and the statutory time limit was not extended by filing a motion in arrest of judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State ex rel. Saylor Development Co. v. Circuit Court of Marion County


No. 29,930


Supreme Court of Indiana


240 Ind. 648; 167 N.E.2d 470; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 237



May 31, 1960, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original action by State of Indiana on relation of Saylor Development Co., Inc. and another, relators, which seeks a writ of prohibition against Circuit Court of Marion County, Niblack, Judge, respondents. A temporary writ was issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ dissolved and permanent writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator development company brought an original action seeking a writ of prohibition against respondents, a trial court and a judge, to prevent the trial court from assuming jurisdiction over an injunction action challenging an amended zoning ordinance. A temporary writ issued.


OVERVIEW: The development company owned land zoned for agricultural use. In order to erect a shopping center on the land, the company obtained an amendment of the metropolitan master plan zoning ordinance from the plan commission. Nevertheless, the court held that judicial review was available because every litigant was entitled to an appeal. The court ruled that such an appeal could be pursued by an action in equity. The court also ruled that the trial court was a court of general jurisdiction, which had jurisdiction to issue injunctive relief under Ind. Code Ann. § 3-2101 (1946).

Peachey v. Boswell


No. 29,840


Supreme Court of Indiana


240 Ind. 604; 167 N.E.2d 48; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 233; 89 A.L.R.2d 801



May 5, 1960, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 23, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Boone Circuit Court, John L. Niblack, Special Judge.

Appellants, James H. Peachey and John D. Ward, d/b/a Ward-Peachey Vending Machine Co., sought to enjoin appellees, Charles Boswell, Mayor of City of Indianapolis et al., from interfering with appellants' business of maintaining and operating in Marion County, mechanically operated free replay pinball machines which record the right of replay. Judgment was entered adverse to appellants and they appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment from the Boone Circuit Court (Indiana), which dissolved an injunction against appellees, a sheriff, a mayor, and a prosecutor, and upheld the constitutionality of 1955 Ind. Acts 265 (amend. 1957), which outlawed, as gambling devices, pinball machines that awarded anything other than an immediate and unrecorded right of replay.


OVERVIEW: Appellants challenged the constitutionality of the Act, which outlawed, as gambling devices, pinball machines that awarded anything other than an immediate and unrecorded right of replay. Following an unfavorable judgment, appellants sought review. Upon review, the court held that the Act was a lawful exercise of the police power because gambling prevention was related to the public morals, safety, and welfare. The court also held that the phrase "in any place accessible to the public" did not create an unconstitutional classification because there was a reason for the classification and because the Act treated all publicly maintained machines alike. In so holding, the court noted that in order to profit from the machines, the machines had to be maintained in a public place. Moreover, in rejecting the contention that that the Act only applied to the "professional gambler," the court held that the Act applied to persons whose conduct brought them within the Act, regardless of whether they were, or were not, professional gamblers. Finally, the court held that the Act's prohibitions did not amount to a deprivation of property without due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

669 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Bailey v. Evansville-Vanderburgh Airport Authority Dist.


No. 29,883


Supreme Court of Indiana


240 Ind. 401; 166 N.E.2d 520; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 202



April 21, 1960, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Vanderburgh Probate Court, French Clements, Judge.

Robert A. Bailey, appellant, brought this suit as a taxpayer to enjoin the appellees, Evansville-Vanderburgh Airport Authority District et al., from proceeding further and pursuant to § 14-1201 et seq., Burns' 1950 Replacement, an act authorizing the creation of airport authority district. A trial was had before the court without a jury and judgment was rendered for the appellees and the appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the decision of the Vanderburgh Probate Court (Indiana), which denied the taxpayer's motion for a new trial and entered judgment in favor of appellees, Evansville-Vanderburgh Airport Authority District (airport authority) in the taxpayer's action to enjoin the airport authority from acting under its authority granted by Ind. Stat. Ann. § 14-1201 et seq. (Act).


OVERVIEW: The Act authorized the creation of airport authority districts and fixed the powers and duties of the airport authority. The taxpayer challenged whether the passage of the Act violated the Indiana state constitution. The court found that the act did not violate Ind. Const. art. 11, § 13 since it provided for the creation of a municipal corporation. The court found that the Indiana Legislature could create municipal corporation. Despite the taxpayer's contention that due to the population limitation in the Act, the Act was a local and special law, the court found that the Act should not be regarded as a local or special act simply because at the time of its enactment it may have only applied to one city. The court found that the act was not unconstitutional for failure to comply with Ind. Const. art. 4, § 19, in that two matters contained in the Act were not covered by the title. The court affirmed the trial court's decision and found that the title satisfied the requirements of the Indiana Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and found the Act constitutional.

Aurora v. Bryant


No. 29,780


Supreme Court of Indiana


240 Ind. 492; 165 N.E.2d 141; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 212



March 9, 1960, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 28, 1960.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Dearborn Circuit Court, John W. Goddard, Special Judge.

Julia S. Bryant and others, appellees, remonstrated against a city ordinance adopted by the City of Aurora annexing certain territory to the city. From a judgment adverse to appellant, City of Aurora, it now appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the judgment of the Dearborn Circuit Court (Indiana) finding that annexation of territory was not in the interest of the city pursuant to Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-702 after appellee property owners filed written remonstrances in their action challenging the annexation.


OVERVIEW: The city's common council adopted an ordinance annexing certain territory. The property owners, whose land was located within the territory, filed written remonstrances in the trial court. After hearing evidence, the trial court found that annexing the territory to the city was not in the city's interest and would cause manifest injury to the property owners. The trial court concluded that the territory described in the ordinance should not be annexed to the city. The city appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court had the authority under § 48-702 to determine whether the annexation of the territory was in the city's interest or would work manifest injury to the property owners. The found that § 48-702 did not attempt to vest legislative power in the courts, but simply authorized the trial court to determine and adjudge whether or not certain statutory requirements necessary to sustain the legislative action of the city's common council in annexing the territory were met after the property owners filed remonstrances. The court also concluded that the only purpose of the annexation was to secure additional tax revenue for the city.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding that annexation of the territory was not in the city's interest.

State ex rel. Rans v. Fulton Circuit Court


No. 29,868


Supreme Court of Indiana


240 Ind. 288; 164 N.E.2d 111; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 186



February 4, 1960, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by State of Indiana on relation of Delbert R. Rans, Jr., relator, for writ of mandate and prohibition asking that respondent, Special Judge Roy E. Sheneman, be mandated to expunge the record made in a certain cause in respondent Fulton Circuit Court overruling relator's motion to withdraw the submission of said cause from respondent judge and to further expunge all subsequent rulings by respondent judge, to prohibit any further proceeding by said judge and that a new judge be appointed to assume jurisdiction in said cause. Temporary writ was issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ dissolved and permanent writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator sought a writ of mandate and prohibition asking that respondent judge of the Fulton Circuit Court (Indiana) be mandated to expunge the record made in a certain cause overruling relator's motion to withdraw the submission of said case from the judge and to further expunge all subsequent rulings by the judge, to prohibit any further proceedings by the judge, and that a new judge be appointed.


OVERVIEW: Relator brought suit against a railroad company for damages and the jury returned a verdict in relator's favor. The railroad filed a motion for a new trial. Ninety four days after the filing of the new trial motion, relator filed a motion to withdraw the submission from the judge for the reason that under Ind. Sup. Ct. R. 1-13 the judge should not have held the same under advisement for longer than 90 days. The judge overruled relator's motion to withdraw the submission and set the motion for a new trial. That ruling by the circuit court was deemed to have been an appealable final judgment. However, relator did not come into the court with his original action until more than a month after the appealable judgment was rendered. The court held that a writ of mandate and prohibition was never intended to be a substitute for the remedy of appeal. The circuit court determined the matters before it and the court could have reviewed them fully on appeal, but could not review them in a mandate and prohibition proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved the temporary writ and denied the permanent writ.

 

672 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Mann v. Terre Haute


No. 29,864


Supreme Court of Indiana


240 Ind. 245; 163 N.E.2d 577; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 179



January 12, 1960, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Vigo Circuit Court, Thomas M. Patrick, Special Judge.

This is an action brought by appellant to enjoin the issuance of revenue bonds by the City of Terre Haute, appellee, for the purpose of building a sewage treatment and disposal plant. The appellant, Hansford C. Mann, appeals from an adverse decision below.

Transferred from Appellate Court pursuant to § 4-217, Burns' 1946 Replacement.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order of the Vigo Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered a judgment for appellee city in an action to enjoin the city from issuing revenue bonds for the construction of a sewage treatment and disposal plant.


OVERVIEW: The Stream Pollution Control Board of the State of Indiana issued an order pursuant to Ind. Stat. Ann. § 68-517 et seq. (1951), finding that a river was polluted by sewage and directing the city to cease and desist the pollution. The city proposed the issuance of revenue bonds to finance the construction of a sewage treatment and disposal plant. The taxpayer filed an action to enjoin the city from issuing the revenue bonds. The trial court entered a judgment for the city. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the revenue bonds did not constitute a direct obligation of the city, so constitutional or statutory debt limitations were not applicable. The court determined that the Act did not grant the taxpayer a right to appeal the city's actions, but the trial court considered his contentions that the Act was unconstitutional and that the city's actions were arbitrary and unreasonable. The court ruled that the taxpayer failed to allege that the evidence did not support the trial court's judgment. The court held that the trial court properly refused to order a continuance and that there was no evidence of misconduct of the part of a special judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the city in the taxpayer's action to enjoin the issuance of the revenue bonds.

 

673 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


No. 29,783


Supreme Court of Indiana


240 Ind. 230; 163 N.E.2d 605; 1960 Ind. LEXIS 177



January 11, 1960, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Gibson Circuit Court, A. Dale Eby, Judge.

The appellants, Leonard Jones et al., were compelled by mandatory injunction to cooperate and assist agents of the Indiana Livestock Sanitary Board, appellee, in inspecting and testing appellants' cattle in compliance with the laws and regulations of the brucellosis program and they appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant cattle owners appealed an order from the Gibson Circuit Court (Indiana), which issued a mandatory injunction compelling the cattle owners to cooperate and assist agents of plaintiff Indiana Livestock Sanitary Board in inspecting and testing cattle in compliance with the laws and regulations of the brucellosis program.


OVERVIEW: The State of Indiana on the relation of the Indiana Livestock Sanitary Board brought seven separate actions under Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 16-120 et seq. (1957 Supp.) to compel certain cattle owners to cooperate and assist agents of the board in inspecting and testing their cattle, in compliance with the laws and regulations of the brucellosis program. The trial court granted the mandatory injunction requested. In a consolidated appeal, the court upheld the constitutionality of the brucellosis statute that was enacted by the State under its police power. However, in reviewing the record, the court noted that there was no record or minutes of the board of county commissioners in which they authorized the contract with the board to carry out the eradication program in the county as the statute required. Because there was no record of any action by the board of county commissioners upon which the statute authorized the Indiana Livestock Sanitary Board to act in the county, the court reversed, concluding that the trial court was without sufficient facts to issue the mandatory injunction empowering the state board to carry out its program in opposition to the cattle owners' objections.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment issuing a mandatory injunction requiring compliance with the state's brucellosis eradication program, with directions that the trial court enter judgment for each of the cattle owners.

 

674 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Ice v. State


No. 29,774


Supreme Court of Indiana


240 Ind. 82; 161 N.E.2d 171; 1959 Ind. LEXIS 253



November 2, 1959, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Gibson Circuit Court, A. Dale Eby, Judge.

This action was brought by the appellee, State of Indiana on relation of Indiana State Board of Dental Examiners, for an injunction to restrain appellant, Robert B. Ice, from engaging in the practice of dentistry. The injunction was issued and appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dental technician sought review of a decision by the Gibson Circuit Court (Indiana), which issued an injunction to restrain the dental technician from engaging in the practice of dentistry. The action was brought by appellee State on behalf of the Indiana State Board of Dental Examiners.


OVERVIEW: Indiana law, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 63-522 (1951), defined the practice of dentistry and limited such practice to licensed dentists. The dental technician, who during his military service fitted and manufactured dentures, claimed that the law was unconstitutional. The State filed an action against the dental technician to prohibit him practicing dentistry. The trial court issued an injunction against the dental technician and he sought review. The court affirmed. The court held that dentistry was a profession directly related to the public health and that the exercise of the State's police power for the control of its practice was a matter that rested with the legislature. As such, the court said, the State's regulation of the profession could not have been annulled by a court unless it contravened a provision of the Constitution. The court responded to the dental technician's argument that the licensing statute violated the privileges and immunities clauses of both the state and federal constitutions by pointing out that the dental technician did not have a vested right to practice dentistry. The practice of dentistry, the court said, was a personal privilege, not a matter of right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that imposed an injunction against the dental technician's practice of dentistry.

Gurecki v. State


No. 0-570


Supreme Court of Indiana


240 Ind. 177; 161 N.E.2d 610; 1959 Ind. LEXIS 266



October 22, 1959, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 8, 1959.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petitioner, Stanley Gurecki, has filed a petition in forma pauperis for a delayed appeal.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a pro se petition in forma pauperis for a delayed appeal from the judgment of a trial court (Indiana). The trial court's judgment convicted him of assault and battery with intent to commit a felony and of being an habitual criminal, but only sentenced him to life imprisonment as an habitual criminal, under the Indiana Habitual Criminal Act, Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 9-2207, 9-2208 (1956) (Act).


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of assault and battery with intent to commit a felony and of being an habitual criminal. The trial court failed to sentence him to a term of imprisonment agreeable to the applicable statute on assault and battery with intent to commit a felony before it sentenced him to life imprisonment as an habitual criminal, under the Act. The inmate filed an unsuccessful petition for a writ of habeas corpus. He then filed a pro se petition in forma pauperis for a delayed appeal. Upon consideration, the court denied the petition. The court held that his failure to move for modification of the trial court's judgment to conform with the Act constituted a waiver of his right to appeal from the trial judge's error when imposing his sentence. Further, the court rejected the inmate's argument that the Act was unconstitutional. The court noted that the Act's constitutionality had been repeatedly upheld. The court found that the inmate's petition wholly failed to allege or aver any grounds or merit for an appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied the inmate's petition for a delayed appeal.

Knutson v. State


No. 29,647


Supreme Court of Indiana


239 Ind. 656; 160 N.E.2d 200; 1959 Ind. LEXIS 211



July 17, 1959 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reported at: 239 Ind. 656 at 666.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of April 7, 1959, Reported at: 239 Ind. 656.



DISPOSITION: ON PETITION FOR REHEARING. Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants petitioned for rehearing of the court's opinion that declared a municipality's subdivision control ordinance unconstitutional. Appellants argued that the court failed to decide on of the issues presented.


OVERVIEW: Prior to the decision in which the court declared a municipality's subdivision control ordinance unconstitutional, the municipality enacted a second subdivision control ordinance. Appellants petitioned for rehearing and argued that since the second ordinance was in effect at the time of the trial and judgment, the plan commission rather than the town board had exclusive authority to approve the plat in question, and the order of mandamus against the town board was contrary to law. The court denied the petition and held that the second ordinance was substantive in its effect and not retroactive. The court held that the adoption of the second ordinance after appellees' right of action had accrued and been asserted by a demand for approval and the filing of an action did not nullify appellees' right to the remedy they sought.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellants' petition for rehearing.

State ex rel. McClure v. Marion Superior Court


No. 29,787


Supreme Court of Indiana


239 Ind. 472; 158 N.E.2d 264; 1959 Ind. LEXIS 187



May 1, 1959, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 3, 1959.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original action by State of Indiana on relation of Edwin McClure, Clerk of the Marion Circuit Court, relator, which seeks a writ of prohibition and mandate against Marion Superior Court, Room No. 1, Walter M. Bell, Jr., Judge, respondent. A temporary writ was issued.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ made absolute and permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator clerk of the Marion Circuit Court sought a writ of prohibition and mandate against respondent judge of the Marion Superior Court. A temporary writ was issued.


OVERVIEW: After a clerk of the Marion Circuit Court died, the Governor designed relator as an appointee to fill the vacancy and issued his commission. Relator took an oath of office and submitted his bond to the Board of County Commissioners of Marion County for approval. Two members of the Commission refused the bond, contending that they had the power to make the appointment rather than the Governor. Thereafter, the Marion Circuit Court entered an order mandating the Commissioners to accept the bond and approve relator. The two commissioners filed an action in quo warranto in the Marion Superior Court and respondent issued an order restraining relator from entering the office of clerk. The court held that a first court to assume jurisdiction had jurisdiction as against another court of equal and coordinate power. The court also concluded that the Governor had the authority to fill a vacancy in the office of clerk of the circuit court, under Ind. Code Ann. § 49-404 (1951). The clerk of a circuit court was a circuit officer, not a county clerk. The Commissioners only had authority to fill vacancies in "county or township offices," pursuant to the Ind. Const. art. VI, § 9.


OUTCOME: The court made the alternative writ absolute and permanent.

 

678 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Alldredge v. State


No. 29,634


Supreme Court of Indiana


239 Ind. 256; 156 N.E.2d 888; 1959 Ind. LEXIS 157



March 13, 1959, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Vanderburgh Circuit Court, R. Owen Williams, Special Judge.

Malcolm W. Alldredge, appellant, was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. He appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. Defendant claimed that he was deprived of his right under Ind. Const. art. I, § 13 to be tried before a judge without a jury and that evidence he had refused to take a drunkometer test was wrongly admitted at trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor. The court affirmed his conviction. Defendant asserted that he was wrongfully deprived of his right to be tried before a judge without a jury. Under Ind. Const. art. I, § 13, defendants were entitled to a jury trial. There was no correlative right to a bench trial. Under 1905 Ind. Acts ch. 169, § 258, p. 584, Ind. Code § 9-1803 (1956) the right to a jury trial could only be waived by the consent of both parties. Defendant also objected to the admission of evidence suggesting he failed to take a drunkometer test. Usually, evidence suggesting an accused freely and voluntarily consented to a drunkenness test was admissible. Conversely, the results of compulsory blood tests were not usually admissible evidence. Evidence suggesting an accused failed to take a test was admissible because it involved no compulsion. The constitutional safeguard against self incrimination enacted by Ind. Const. art. I, § 14 was inapplicable to this dispute because no testimonial compulsion was involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

679 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Gradison v. Ohio Oil Co.


Nos. 29,583, 29,618


Supreme Court of Indiana


239 Ind. 218; 156 N.E.2d 80; 1959 Ind. LEXIS 152; 10 Oil & Gas Rep. 490



February 16, 1959, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room 4, Walter Pritchard, Judge in case No. 29,583; Paul J. DeVault, Special Judge in case No. 29,618.

Appellee, Ohio Oil Company, brought these actions against appellants, Jules T. Gradison, Rita Gradison, Mechel Dotlich, and others, to condemn an easement across real estate owned by appellants. From a judgment for appellee, appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two eminent domain cases consolidated for hearing, appellant landowners challenged an order of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) granting an easement across their property to appellee common carrier for the right of way for an oil pipeline. They argued that neither the condemnation statute nor the Indiana General Corporation Act allowed the common carrier, which was a foreign business, to condemn Indiana real estate for the pipeline.


OVERVIEW: The common carrier operated under the jurisdiction of the Interstate Commerce Commission. The right of a foreign corporation to exercise the power of eminent domain could only exist by an affirmative grant of statutory power. The Eminent Domain Act of the State of Indiana, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 3-1713 (1946) provided that an Indiana corporation could exercise eminent domain to carry out certain public purposes. The General Corporation Act of 1929, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 25-302 (1948), had an equalizing clause that placed foreign corporations on the same basis as Indiana corporations. A foreign corporation authorized to do business in Indiana could exercise the power of eminent domain when domestic corporations were given the privilege. The business must exercise the power of eminent domain for a public use or utility without discrimination. Other Indiana common carriers were authorized to exercise the power of eminent domain. It was immaterial that the carrier leased portions of their electrical output to other public utilities. Likewise, the common carrier from outside Indiana was authorized to exercise the power of eminent domain. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Book v. Board of Flood Control Comm'rs


No. 29,717


Supreme Court of Indiana


239 Ind. 160; 156 N.E.2d 87; 1959 Ind. LEXIS 151



February 3, 1959, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Superior Court, Room 3, Norman E. Brennan, Judge.

William H. Book, appellant, brought this action for injunction against the Board of Flood Control Commissioners of the City of Indianapolis and others, appellees, to enjoin the appellees from undertaking certain flood control project under the provisions of the Flood Control Act of 1937, as amended. Judgment was rendered in favor of appellees and appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the Marion County Superior Court (Indiana), which denied him injunctive relief in his action against appellee board to enjoin the board from undertaking flood control project under the provisions of the Flood Control Act of 1937. The taxpayer claimed that the statute violated the Indiana Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought an action against the board to enjoin it from the conduct of flood control projects under the provisions of the Flood Control Act of 1937, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-4727 et seq. (1950), on grounds that the statute was unconstitutional. The trial court denied relief and the taxpayer sought review. The court held that: (1) the statute did not violate Ind. Const. art. XIII, § 1, by exceeding the municipal debt limit, because special improvement districts and debts in connection therewith were not indebtedness of the municipality; (2) the statute did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 23, by the unequal grant of privileges because the legislature could levy a tax upon all or a part of the property in the district by a uniform rule according to its value and determine what property was benefitted; (3) the statute did not violate Ind. Const. art. IV, § 19, by embracing subjects that were not in the title of the Act, because the improvement of bridges and roads was limited to the purpose of flood control; and (4) the statute did not violate Ind. Const. art. XI, § 12, because it did not give the board the power to give property to a private individual.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied injunctive relief to the taxpayer in his action against the board to enjoin flood control projects.

McCoy v. Evansville


No. 29,705


Supreme Court of Indiana


239 Ind. 98; 154 N.E.2d 804; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 166

Basil McCoy, and others, seek to enjoin appellees, The City of Evansville acting by and on behalf of the City of Evansville Redevelopment Commission and others, from proceeding under Acts 1953, ch. 176, as amended, to condemn appellants' property. DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, property owners, sought review of the decision of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained the demurrer filed by appellee city, in an action brought by the property owners challenging the city's condemnation of their property.


OVERVIEW: A redevelopment commission of the city sought to condemn the property owners' land under Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 48-8541 et seq. The city also sought to issue bonds to provide funds for the operation of the redevelopment commission. The property consisted of two residences and a commercial building used as a restaurant. DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which found defendant guilty of felonious possession of narcotic drugs and sentenced him to a term of imprisonment of not less than one or more than ten years.


OVERVIEW: Police officers arrested defendant after observing him gambling and upon searching defendant discovered a tube containing 14 capsules that were found to contain heroin. Finally, the court ruled that defendant was not entitled to inspect the record of the evidence taken before the grand jury or to a copy of his own evidence before the grand jury. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the term of imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for felonious possession of narcotic drugs and the term of imprisonment of not less than one or more than ten years.

685 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


O'Donnell v. Krneta


No. 29,673


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 582; 154 N.E.2d 45; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 267



November 19, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Pulaski Circuit Court, Robert E. Thompson, Judge.

Appellees, Peter Krneta and Sophie Krneta, bring this action to quiet title and to set aside a tax deed under which appellant, Geraldine Anselm O'Donnell, claims title to certain real estate as a successor in interest of the original purchaser at tax sale. From an adverse judgment appellant takes this appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant alleged landowner challenged an order of the Pulaski Circuit Court (Indiana) granting judgment to appellee alleged landowners in their action to quiet title in a certain piece of property and to set aside a tax deed. Appellant claimed title to the property as a successor in interest of the original tax sale purchaser. She argued that the action was barred by a one-year limitations period under Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 64-2203a and 64-2212.


OVERVIEW: Appellees contended that the general 15-year statute of limitations, under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 2-603, applied. The court disagreed and reversed. The 1941 amendment encompassed in Ind. Stat. Ann. § 64-2212 revised the earlier act. This sale and deed were executed under the 1941 act and the one-year statute of limitations applied. The one-year statute was not unconstitutional. Ind. Const. art. 4, § 21 required that the wording of an amended section be set out in full. It did not restrict direct or implied amendments or repeals when the extra section was set out in full text. The purpose was to prevent surprise or fraud by a title that did not apprise the public of the subject-matter of the proposed law. Although Ind. Stat. Ann. 64-2212 did not designate in its body any specific section that it amended and sections in the amendment did not cover the same subject matter as the original act, the subject matter of the period of limitations did fall within the purview of the act to be amended and was a valid amendment. An amendatory act could repeal or modify another statute by implication to the extent that it was repugnant to the limited area it covered.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment with directions to grant a new trial.

 

686 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Ben Davis Conservancy Dist.


No. 29,624


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 502; 153 N.E.2d 125; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 259



October 2, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Circuit Court, John L. Niblack, Judge.

Ulice Martin, appellant, brought this action to determine the constitutionality of the Conservancy Act of Indiana, Acts 1957, ch. 308, p. 851, being §§ 27-1501 to 27-1599, Burns' 1957 Cum. Supp. Judgment was rendered favorable to appellee, The Ben Davis Conservancy District, and appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment of the Marion County Circuit Court (Indiana) in favor of appellee conservancy district, rejecting the taxpayer's constitutional challenge to the Conservancy Act of Indiana (the Act), 1957 Ind. Acts, ch. 308.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a state law later declared unconstitutional, the circuit court entered judgment establishing the district, which was created to control pollution and had authority to levy tax assessment for improvements to real estate within the district. When the circuit court entered judgment, no objection was made concerning the constitutionality of the law. The legislature subsequently passed the Act, which contained a curative provision that validated districts established under the prior law. After the circuit court reiterated its establishment of the district, the taxpayer brought an action alleging that the Act was unconstitutional. The circuit court granted judgment against the taxpayer. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that (1) the unconstitutionality of the prior law did not have retroactive effect because the initial circuit court judgment, entered without objection, was the law of the case and because the Act's curative provision was effective, (2) the Act was not in any respect unconstitutionally defective, but was properly enacted under the legislature's authority to create taxing districts for the purpose of funding local public improvements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the conservancy district, which rejected the taxpayer's constitutional challenge to the Conservancy Act of Indiana.
