State v. Young


No. 29,507


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 452; 151 N.E.2d 697; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 252



July 2, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court No. 3 of Allen County, Floyd S. Hartzler, Judge.

Appellants, State of Indiana, State Highway Department of Indiana, Neil Godwin, James R. Hardendorf, and C.J. LaTourette, appeal from a permanent injunction restraining them from the commission of threatened trespasses or assertion of title or claim of title to certain real estate owned by appellees R.M. Young and B.D. Hayes, a partnership d/b/a Fort Wayne Oil Co.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed as to State of Indiana and affirmed in all other respects.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the state of Indiana, the State Highway Department of Indiana, and three individuals, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court No. 3 of Allen County (Indiana), which granted a permanent injunction restraining them from the commission of threatened trespasses or assertion of title or claim of title to appellee owners' real estate.


OVERVIEW: The owners purchased the real estate without any notice that the former owners had executed a grant to the state, which was never recorded, for a right-of-way for highway purposes. The owners sought an injunction to prevent the state or the highway department from trespassing on the real estate or asserting title or claim of title. The trial court ruled in favor of the owners. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that: (1) Ind. Stat. Ann. § 36-2940 (1949 Repl.), which required the recording of rights-of-way and easements in the county recorder's office, was constitutional; (2) § 36-2940 was intended to protect purchasers against prior and secret unrecorded grants to the state, and it was liberally construed; (3) the owners were bona fide purchasers of value without notice, either actual or constructive; and (4) the employees of the state were threatening continuing and repeated trespasses on the land in controversy, which the owners were entitled to prevent by injunction. However, the court also held that no statute authorized a judgment against the state, and for this reason, the court reversed the judgment as to the state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment as to the state but affirmed the trial court's judgment in all other respects.

 

688 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Plymouth v. Stream Pollution Control Board


No. 29,494


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 439; 151 N.E.2d 626; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 249



June 30, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Elkhart Circuit Court, Aldo A. Simpson, Judge.

Appellant, The City of Plymouth, Indiana, brought action for judicial review of an order of the Stream Pollution Control Board, appellee, requiring appellant to cease and desist from causing pollution of Yellow River and requiring appellant to construct certain facilities. The lower court affirmed the order, appellant's motion for new trial was stricken out and appellant takes this appeal.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a judgment of the Elkhart Circuit Court (Indiana), which affirmed an order of appellee, the Stream Pollution Control Board of the State of Indiana, and struck the city's motion for a new trial. The Board ordered the city to cease and desist from polluting a river and required the city to build certain facilities. The Board filed a motion to dismiss the city's appeal.


OVERVIEW: The Board ordered the city to construct facilities to treat sanitary and domestic sewage including the city's industrial wastes. The Board argued that the city failed to timely file its notice of appeal under the Administrative Adjudication and Court Review Act of 1947 (Administrative Act), Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 63-3001 to 63-3030 (1951). The city argued that its appeal was field within 15 days of the trial court's order striking its motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court found that the city's judicial review was governed by the Administrative Act. The Stream Pollution Control Board Act of 1943 (Stream Act), Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 68-517 to 68-534 (1951) did not provide for judicial review of the Board's orders, which was repugnant to the Administrative Act. Section 28 of the Administrative Act, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 63-3028 removed the application of the Stream Act to cases of repugnancy between the two acts. There was no basis for the city's motion for a new trial under the Administrative Act, and the motion was correctly stricken out. Because the city improperly filed a motion for a new trial, its notice of appeal was not timely filed within 15 days of the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the city's appeal.

 

689 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


General Tel. Co. v. Public Service Com.


No. 29,547


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 646; 150 N.E.2d 891; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 271



June 12, 1958, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 24, 1958.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Owen Circuit Court, Robert B. Stewart, Special Judge.

Appellant, General Telephone Company of Indiana, brought this action to review an order of appellee, Public Service Commission, granting a certificate of territorial authority to appellee, Clay County Rural Telephone Co-operative. The order was sustained by the trial court and appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant telephone company sought review of a judgment of the Owen Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained the order of appellee Public Service Commission of Indiana that granted a certificate of territorial authority to appellee competitor telephone company.


OVERVIEW: The telephone company insisted the action brought by another company to review the order of the Commission declaring the area "open territory" suspended the right of the Commission to grant a certificate of territorial authority to the competitor. The court disagreed. The court found nothing in Ind. Stat. Ann. § 54-601(b) (1951) that prohibited the Commission from granting a certificate. In addition, the court found that when the telephone company sought to obtain a certificate of territorial authority under § 54-601(b), it estopped itself from thereafter claiming in the same proceeding that the section was unconstitutional. As the telephone company asserted the findings of the Commission were insufficient to sustain the order. Where the telephone company offered uncontroverted and unimpeached testimony, the Commission was not at liberty to disregard such evidence and make no special findings upon it. The findings were too general to permit an appellate court as a court of review to intelligently judge whether the action was based upon substantial evidence. The findings were so defective that the order based thereon was void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

690 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Scott v. Scott


No. 29,512


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 474; 150 N.E.2d 740; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 256



June 4, 1958, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 24, 1958.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Grant Circuit Court, Robert T. Caine, Judge.

Appellee, Gertrude E. Scott, as administratrix of the Estate of Glenn A. Scott, deceased, filed petition to determine heirship as between a second childless wife of decedent and appellant, G. Alfred Scott, natural son of decedent by a former marriage who had been adopted by his paternal grandparents during his minority. Judgment in lower court that decedent's widow, Gertrude E. Scott, appellee, was sole and only heir of decedent. Appellant appeals.

Transferred from Appellate Court pursuant to Sec. 4-214, Burns' 1946 Replacement.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, decedent's natural son who had been adopted by his paternal grandparents, sought review of a judgment from the Grant Circuit Court (Indiana), which held that appellee, the decedent's widow, was the sole and only heir of the decedent.


OVERVIEW: The decedent's natural son was adopted by his paternal grandparents when he was two years old. The decedent later remarried, and the trial court determined that the decedent's widow was his sole and only heir. On appeal, the court affirmed. Section 208 of the Probate Code of 1953, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 6-208 (1953), was applicable because the rights of the son and widow were determined by the statutes of descent in force at the time of the decedent's death. Under this section, the son was precluded from inheriting from his natural father in accordance with the principles of intestate succession because he had been adopted. The son did not acquire an "accrued right" at birth in his natural father's estate within the meaning of Ind. Stat. Ann. § 6-102. Section 6-208 did not violate Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. The legislature had not discriminated between adopted minors whose parents died before the effective date of the Probate Code of 1953 and adopted minors whose natural parents died thereafter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that had held that the decedent's widow was the sole and only heir of the decedent.

Tinder v. Clarke Auto Co.


No. 29,611


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 302; 149 N.E.2d 808; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 234; 34 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P71,498



April 30, 1958, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 3, 1958.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room 1, John M. Ryan, Judge.

Appellee, Clarke Auto Co., Inc. brought this action in behalf of itself and all other automobile dealers similarly situated, to enjoin appellants from enforcing § 10-4305, Burns' 1957 Supp., which prohibited automobile dealers from buying or selling automobiles at retail on Sunday. An injunction was granted and appellants, John Tinder, Prosecuting Attorney, and others, take this appeal.



DISPOSITION: Injunction ordered vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state prosecuting attorney challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which granted plaintiff automobile dealer an injunction that enjoined the State of Indiana from enforcing Ind. Code § 4305 (1957 Supp.), a statute which prohibited automobile dealers from buying or selling automobiles at retail on Sunday.


OVERVIEW: The automobile dealer, on behalf of himself and all other automobile dealers similarly situated, sought to enjoin the enforcement of Ind. Code § 10-4305 (1957 Supp.). That statute subjected automobile dealers that engaged in the business of buying, selling, and/or exchanging motor vehicles at retail on Sunday to fines and/or imprisonment greater than those imposed upon dealers and other businesses that were made unlawful by the general Sunday closing law, Ind. Code § 10-4301 (1956 Repl.). The trial court granted the injunction on the ground that the classification of the act, which imposed a greater penalty on the class, was "wholly arbitrary and unreasonable," and therefore in violation of Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23, and Ind. Const. art. 4, §§ 22, 23. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the state had the authority under its police power to provide a day for man's recurring need for rest and relaxation. Because there were characteristics in the several businesses that distinguished them from the retail sales of automobiles, the automobile car dealer did not overcome the presumption in favor of the statute's constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the temporary injunction issued by the trial court that enjoined the state from enforcing a statute that prohibited car dealers from buying or selling automobiles at retail on Sunday.

Book v. State Office Bldg. Com.


No. 29,608


SUPREME COURT OF INDIANA


238 Ind. 120; 149 N.E.2d 273; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 213



April 2, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Superior Court, Room No. 4, Walter Pritchard, Judge.

Appellant, William H. Book, brought a taxpayers' suit to enjoin the appellees, Harold W. Handley and others as members of the State Office Building Commission from proceeding further in the construction of a state office building. Appellees' demurrer was sustained and upon appellants' failure to plead further judgment was entered for the appellees. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which sustained appellees', State Office Building Commission and members, demurrer and entered judgment in favor of the appellees in an action initiated by the taxpayer to enjoin the appellees from proceeding in the construction of a state office building, pursuant to the State Office Building Commission Act, Ind. Code §§ 60-2101 to 60-2134 (1953).


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer initiated an action against the appellees to enjoin them from proceeding in the construction of a state office building, pursuant to the State Office Building Commission Act (Act), Ind. Code §§ 60-2101 to 60-2134 (1953). The trial court sustained appellees' demurrer and entered judgment in their favor, and the taxpayer sought review. The court held that the appellees were not a corporation within the meaning of Ind. Const. art. 11, § 13. The court held that the bonds acquired by the appellees were not an obligation of the state despite the fact that once such bonds were paid the building would have become a part of the state building system. The court held that the appellees, as a municipal corporation, were permitted to contract for necessary services over a period of years and agree to pay for such services in periodic installments. The court held that the Act was not in violation of Ind. Const. art. 10, § 5. The court held that Ind. Code § 60-2102, which allowed legislative members to serve on the Act's commission, was in violation of Ind. Const. art. 3, § 1. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part a judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part a judgment of the trial court, which sustained the appellees' demurrer and entered judgment in an action initiated by the taxpayer to enjoin the appellees from proceeding in the construction of a state office building, pursuant to State Office Building Commission Act. The court held that bonds acquired by the appellees were not the state's obligation, although the building would be state property.

Sun Oil Co. v. Gross Income Tax Div.


No. 29,449


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 111; 149 N.E.2d 115; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 212; 58-1 U.S. Tax Cas. (CCH) P15,145



April 1, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 4, Walter Pritchard, Judge.

Appellant, Sun Oil Company, brought this action to recover gross income taxes on Indiana sales of gasoline and oil which had been paid under protest. From a decision favorable to appellee, Gross Income Tax Division of the State of Indiana, appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana) in favor of appellee, Gross Income Tax Division of the State of Indiana (division), in the taxpayer's action to recover gross income taxes on Indiana sales of gasoline and oil that the taxpayer paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was an out-of-state corporation qualified to do business in Indiana. The taxpayer engaged in producing, refining, transporting, and selling gasoline, lubricating oils, and petroleum products. The taxpayer paid federal excise taxes on gasoline and lubricating oils. Most of the taxpayer's sales were made wholesale to service or filling stations. Its invoices to its customers included the amount of federal excise tax in the sales price. The division collected gross income taxes from the taxpayers, asserting that the amounts of federal excise taxes charged and received were gross receipts to the taxpayer. The taxpayer filed an action against the division to recover the gross income taxes paid. The trial court found in favor of the division. The taxpayer appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the assessment of gross income taxes was proper. The court reasoned that although the amount of federal excise tax was added as a separate charge on the invoices, no excise tax was imposed or paid by the taxpayer's customers. By adding the federal excise taxes as a separate charge, the taxpayer in effect raised the cost of the gasoline to its customers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the division in the taxpayer's action to recover gross income taxes paid on sales of gasoline and oil.

State v. Buxton


No. 29,534


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 93; 148 N.E.2d 547; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 209



March 20, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Scott Circuit Court, S. Morris Wilson, Special Judge.

Appellee, Loran O. Buxton, was acquitted on a charge of arson and the appellant, State of Indiana, appeals on a reserved question of law.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment by the Scott Circuit Court (Indiana), which acquitted defendant on a charge of arson. The State appealed on a reserved question of law only, claiming that under the Fire Marshal's Act, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 20-808 (1950 Repl.), no search warrant was necessary, and therefore the trial court erred in sustaining the objection of defendant to the admission of certain evidence.


OVERVIEW: A restaurant building, owned by defendant, caught fire causing the interior to be badly burned. Upon investigation, a state trooper photographer was sent to the scene. While the photographer was taking a picture of a hole in the utility room where the fire originated, he discovered a hot plate at the bottom. Further examination revealed a cord for the hot plate, a pile of torn newspapers, and a sack soaked in fuel oil. The materials were seized as evidence. Upon the strength of the evidence, defendant was arrested and placed on trial for arson. The general question was whether the evidence so obtained was taken unlawfully in violation of defendant's constitutional rights under Ind. Const. art. 1, § 11. The court held that under the Fire Marshal law the fire marshal and his deputies and agents had to obtain a search warrant prior to searching a person's dwelling, effects, or possessions for the purpose of obtaining evidence to be used in criminal prosecution and that basic constitutional requirement could be and was by implication incorporated as a necessary part of the responsibility and activity authorized by the law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bruce v. State


No. 29,602


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 79; 148 N.E.2d 553; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 207



March 19, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Vanderburgh Circuit Court, Ollie C. Reeves, Judge.

William J. Bruce, appellant, was convicted of a misdemeanor in the City Court of Evansville. On appeal to the Vanderburgh Circuit Court, the State's motion to dismiss the appeal was sustained and appellant's petition for a belated appeal from the city court conviction was overruled. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained the State's motion to dismiss defendant's appeal from a misdemeanor conviction in city court and overruled defendant's petition for a belated appeal from the city court conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to 180 days on a penal farm with a fine, and within 15 days, the transcript from city court and all connected papers were filed in circuit court. The State moved to dismiss the appeal on the ground that it was not initiated within 10 days after the city court's judgment, and defendant filed a verified petition for a belated appeal. The circuit court overruled the petition and dismissed defendant's appeal. On appeal, the court held that defendant filed his transcript and papers within the 15 days allowed for taking an appeal to the circuit court without bond and that Ind. Code Ann. § 9-721 (1956) allowed such an appeal when a defendant remained in jail instead of furnishing a recognizance. The court found full compliance with the statutory requirements in such cases, as § 9-721 required only the filing of the necessary papers within 15 days, and found no oral or written demand requirements. It held that such proceedings were intended to be as simple as possible.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case with directions to the trial court to overrule the motion to dismiss the appeal from the city court.

Homecroft v. Macbeth


No. 29,504


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 57; 148 N.E.2d 563; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 205



March 17, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 5, George A. Henry, Special Judge.

Lorne C. Macbeth, appellee, was denied a variance to erect a filling station by the Board of Zoning Appeals of the Town of Homecroft, Marion County. The trial court, on review, reversed the decision of the Board of Zoning Appeals. Appellants, the Town of Homecroft, said Board of Zoning Appeals and others, take this appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Board of Zoning Appeals of the Town of Homecroft, Town of Homecroft, and residents, appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), reversing a decision of the board which denied appellee owner's petition for a variance to erect a filling station on land owned by him in the town, and ordering the board to issue a building permit to the owner.


OVERVIEW: When the town was incorporated, it was zoned entirely as a dwelling house district. Prior thereto, the owner operated a grocery store on her land, which was located near a busy intersection and highway. The store's business declined and the owner tried to sell the land. For almost a year, nobody was interested in the land as either a store or a residence. The owner received an offer to buy the land for the construction of a cottage type filling station. At a hearing before the board, the residents opposed the owner's request for a variance because, they argued, a filling station would have depreciated the value of their land. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly reversed the board's decision to deny the owner's request for a variance. The court determined that the zoning ordinance restricting the owner's land to residential purposes was unreasonable because it precluded the owner's use of the property for any purpose for which it was adapted. The court ruled that the evidence sufficiently showed that, given the heavy traffic in the area, it was unreasonable to restrict the owner's land to a residential use in an effort to provide a dignified village frontage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the owner.

Payne v. Buchanan


No. 29,563


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 231; 148 N.E.2d 537; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 226



March 17, 1958, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 14, 1958.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Vanderburgh Circuit Court, Ollie C. Reeves, Judge.

Action by appellants, members and officers of Unity Lodge Numbered 2040, International Association of Machinists, AFL-CIO, and Vanderburgh County Farm Bureau, Inc., against the Public Service Commission of Indiana, to vacate and set aside an order granting a rate increase to Southern Indiana Gas & Electric Company, appellee. This appeal is taken from a judgment dismissing the action for lack of jurisdiction.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, lodge, associations, and corporation, sought review of the decision of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed for lack of jurisdiction their action against appellee Public Service Commission of Indiana to vacate and set aside an order granting a rate increase to a gas and electric company.


OVERVIEW: The commission granted a gas and electric company a rate increase and appellants challenged the rate increase. The lower court dismissed appellants' action for lack of jurisdiction and the court reversed. The court found that there was no clear conflict between the general 1929 Act and the 1933 Act, which was specific to rate increases, and that therefore the 1933 Act did not repeal the earlier act and appellants' action was timely filed under the provisions of the 1929 Act. The court concluded that although appellants' complaint was not as specific as it could have been, the allegations were sufficient to clearly imply that the gas and electric company operated in the forum county; therefore there was no jurisdictional bar. The court determined that appellants were entitled to their day in court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's dismissal of appellants' action to vacate a rate order and held that there were not any jurisdictional bars to the commencement of the action.

Johnson v. Burke


No. 29,483


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 1; 148 N.E.2d 413; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 201



March 10, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Vanderburgh County, James M. Buthod, Special Judge.

Edmond Johnson, appellant, filed petition for writ of habeas corpus which was denied. He appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant arrestee sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Vanderburgh County (Indiana), which denied his petition for writ of habeas corpus in an extradition proceeding. The arrestee alleged that the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act, 1935 Ind. Acts ch. 49, §§ 1-30 (Repl. 1956) were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The State of Arizona, the demanding state, wanted to extradite the arrestee for failure to pay support. The arrestee attempted to show by his testimony that, inter alia, he was not in the State of Arizona on the date of the offense, but the lower court sustained the objection to the introduction of such evidence. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the arrestee's petition for habeas corpus. The court found, inter alia, that (1) in a habeas corpus proceeding to test the validity of an arrest and detention made by virtue of a governor's extradition warrant, the arrestee could not offer evidence to prove that he was not in the demanding state at the time of the alleged offense; (2) the construction of the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act, which limited introduction of the evidence to the question of arrestee's identity, did not violate the U.S. Const. art. 4, § 2, cl. 2; the 14th Amendment; or Ind. Const. art. 1, §§ 1, 12, 27; and (3) a state could by appropriate legislation enlarge the scope of extradition beyond that provided for under federal law, such that the extradition proceedings, authorized under state law but which did not offend federal law, were lawful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the arrestee's petition for habeas corpus in the extradition proceedings where the arrestee challenged the constitutionality of the Uniform Criminal Extradition Act.

 

700 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Matthews v. State


No. 29,574


Supreme Court of Indiana


237 Ind. 677; 148 N.E.2d 334; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 194



March 6, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Vanderburgh Circuit Court, W. C. Welborn, Special Judge.

Appellant, Jasper Leroy Matthews, was found guilty of assault and battery with intent to commit murder and carrying a pistol without a license. He appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions in the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of assault and battery with intent to commit murder and of carrying a pistol without a license therefor in violation of Ind. Acts of 1935, ch. 63, as codified later in the Uniform Firearms Act, Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 10-4736, 10-4747 (1956).


OVERVIEW: The convictions arose from an assault in which defendant aimed at one man, but shot another. First, the court disposed of defendant's claims that his assault count varied from the proof and that he had been misled in his defense, finding that they lacked merit. Next, the court addressed defendant's constitutional challenges to the Uniform Firearms Act and held that they, too, lacked merit. Thus, the court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court reasoned that the act fixed the general standard of fitness, character, and reputation necessary to qualify for a firearms license and provided for review by a circuit court. The court found no unlawful delegation of legislative power in the act and held that it did not violate the Due Process Clause or Ind. Const. art. 4, § 1. Lastly, the court rejected defendant's claim that the act violated Ind. Const. art. 1. §, which granted the right to bear arms. The legislature had the power, in the interest of public safety and welfare, to provide reasonable regulations for the use of firearms such as pistols, which could be readily concealed. The act did not unduly restrict the right of the people to bear arms.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for assault and battery with intent to commit murder and for carrying a pistol without a license in violation of the Uniform Firearms Act.

State ex rel. County Welfare Board v. Starke Circuit Court


Nos. 29,617, 29,621


Supreme Court of Indiana


238 Ind. 35; 147 N.E.2d 585; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 203



February 4, 1958, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 13, 1958.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original action by the State of Indiana on relation of the Starke County Welfare Board and its members seeking a writ of mandate and prohibition against the Starke Circuit Court and Jack Murray, the judge thereof. A temporary writ of prohibition and an alternative writ of mandate were issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ of prohibition made permanent and alternative writ of mandate made absolute.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, a county welfare board and its members, sought a writ of mandate and prohibition against respondents, a trial court and a trial court judge, to prohibit the trial court from enforcing an order for the board to make all of its records available for inspection and to compel the trial court to return all the records that had previously been impounded by the sheriff pursuant to the trial court's order.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had ordered the sheriff to impound records of the board and had subsequently ordered the board to produce certain records for the trial court's inspection. The trial court overruled the board's motion to set aside the court's orders. The board filed an action, seeking a writ of mandate and prohibition against the trial court. The court granted a permanent writ of prohibition, concluding that the trial court lacked the jurisdiction and the authority to enter the orders. The power granted to trial courts under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 52-1118 (1951), as part of the Indiana Public Welfare Act, did not include the right to order, sua sponte, county welfare boards to deliver their records to the courts or to impound them for the purpose of determining if there had been any misconduct, incapacity, or neglect by the members of the board, nor was such power incidental or necessary to the determination of that issue. The trial court's attempt to conduct an administrative review violated the separation of powers doctrine under Ind. Const. art. 3, § 1. The trial court was not, either directly or indirectly, authorized to seize the records under 1953 Ind. Acts ch. 115.


OUTCOME: The court made its temporary writ of prohibition permanent and made the alternative writ of mandate absolute, enjoining the trial court from obtaining the board's records.

New York C. R. Co. v. Public Service Com.


No. 29,493


Supreme Court of Indiana


237 Ind. 544; 147 N.E.2d 547; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 185



January 27, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Hendricks Circuit Court, George W. Hadley, Judge.

The New York Central Railroad Company, appellant, brought an action to set aside and vacate an order of the Public Service Commission, appellee, requiring installation of a flagman or flasher lights at a railroad crossing in the town of Brownsburg. From an adverse judgment, appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad challenged a decision of the Hendricks Circuit Court (Indiana), which, in the railroad's action to set aside and vacate an order of appellee Public Service Commission of Indiana, found in favor of the commission.


OVERVIEW: The railroad brought an action to vacate and set aside an order requiring it to provide a flagman (or, at the railroad's election, flasher lights) at a railroad crossing in the town of Brownsburg, Indiana. The trial court found in favor of the commission and denied relief to the railroad. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that: (1) it was unable to agree with the railroad's contention that, under Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 48-301 (Repl. 1950), 55-2016 (Repl. 1951), a town board had exclusive jurisdiction over the matter of requiring watchmen or signal devices at crossings within the town; (2) the "extra-hazardous" statute, Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 55-2012, 55-2013 (Repl. 1950), made no particular reference to obstructed crossings, nor did it apply to any crossings unless state highways were involved; (3) neither the town board of Brownsburg nor the public service commission was a court, and concepts of concurrent jurisdiction did not apply to the duplicity or overlapping of such agencies or departments of the government; and (4) the obstructive view statute did not violate Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23 or Ind. Const. art. 3, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the commission.

 

703 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


In re Petition of Justice of Peace Asso., Inc.


No. 29,596


Supreme Court of Indiana


237 Ind. 436; 147 N.E.2d 16; 1958 Ind. LEXIS 177



January 10, 1958, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding wherein the Justice of the Peace Association of Indiana, Inc., filed a petition requesting authority to prepare examination questions for Justice of the Peace for the approval of the Supreme Court and that its officers be authorized to conduct an examination after approval of the court is granted.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Justice of the Peace Association of Indiana, filed a petition asking that the court authorize it to prepare examination questions for the approval of the court, and that its officers be authorized to conduct an examination at a time and place to be determined after approval of the court was granted pursuant to the latter part of § 7 of Ch. 322 of the 1957 Ind. Acts 322, § 7, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 5-132 (1946).


OVERVIEW: The General Assembly by enacting 1957 Ind. Acts 322, § 7 provided additional qualifications for eligibility of a justice of the peace. The Association filed a petition, seeking to proceed under the statute. The court noted the rule that where the Constitution prescribed qualifications for constitutional officers, the General Assembly could not prescribe additional qualifications. Construing the statutes and the Constitutional provisions relating to justices of the peace, the court determined that it was beyond the constitutional power of the General Assembly to provide qualifications for the office of justices of the peace in addition to those which were prescribed by the Constitution of Indiana. Accordingly, the court concluded that part of 1957 Ind. Acts 322, § 7, which purported to provide additional qualifications for eligibility for justices of the peace, was unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition.

 

704 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 29,467


Supreme Court of Indiana


237 Ind. 532; 146 N.E.2d 86; 1957 Ind. LEXIS 298



November 25, 1957, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 23, 1958.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Vigo Circuit Court, Herbert R. Criss, Judge.

Forrest Eugene Smith, appellant, takes this appeal from a denial of his motion for writ of error coram nobis.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the denial of his "motion to vacate void judgment" by the Vigo Circuit Court (Indiana), the judgment being his prior conviction for vehicle taking and being an habitual criminal. Defendant had previously, and unsuccessfully, sought direct appeal of his conviction.


OVERVIEW: At trial, defendant was charged with and convicted of vehicle taking and being a habitual criminal pursuant to the Habitual Criminal Act, Ind. Code Ann. §§ 9-2207 and 9-2208 (1952). In an earlier proceeding, the court affirmed the conviction. Then defendant filed a "motion to vacate void judgment." The trial court overruled the motion. The court affirmed the trial court's order. The court first held that defendant's motion was properly treated as a petition for writ of error coram nobis because there was no procedure in the court for vacating a judgment at the end of the court's term. As a coram nobis petition, defendant failed to show why the alleged constitutional infirmities he alleged in this action were not alleged at trial or on direct appeal. Because he failed to make such a showing, he was not entitled to relief. But the court went on to note that the provision of the Habitual Criminal Act requiring being charged with the third felony and with being a habitual criminal, then requiring conviction of both, was constitutional. The Act did not impose life imprisonment for an additional crime, but for the status of being a habitual criminal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's "motion to vacate void conviction."

Department of Financial Institutions v. Universal C.I.T. Credit Corp.


No. 29,505


Supreme Court of Indiana


237 Ind. 404; 146 N.E.2d 93; 1957 Ind. LEXIS 292



November 22, 1957, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 7, 1958.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Marion Circuit Court, Lloyd D. Claycombe, Judge.

The Department of Financial Institutions, appellant, issued a cease and desist order against Universal C.I.T. Credit Corporation, appellee, and the Circuit Court upon the application of appellee set aside and vacated such order. The Department and other appellants take this appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), in which the court vacated the cease and desist order that appellant had issued against appellee, based on appellee's business practices involving automobile installment contracts.


OVERVIEW: Appellant issued a cease and desist order against appellee, which prohibited appellee from paying more than 10 percent of the gross finance charge on automobile installment contracts when it purchased or proposed to purchase cars from automobile dealers within the State of Indiana. The order was entered after a hearing on a complaint filed by appellee and other parties holding licenses to purchase retail installment contracts for the sale of automobiles. The court vacated the order. On appeal, the court held that appellee had not acted with any malice when it attempted to obtain a larger amount of business for itself. The court determined the record disclosed that appellee had not obtained a monopoly or entered into any agreement that would create a monopoly. Instead, there was a free play of competition in the State, and only a small part of the business went to appellee. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed the lower court's decision, which vacated the cease and desist order appellant issued against appellee, because it held there was no proof that appellee had obtained a monopoly or entered into any agreement that would create a monopoly.

 

706 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


National City Bank v. Bledsoe


No. 29,568


Supreme Court of Indiana


237 Ind. 130; 144 N.E.2d 710; 1957 Ind. LEXIS 256



September 12, 1957, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Vanderburgh Probate Court, French Clements, Judge.

National City Bank of Evansville, Indiana, personal representative of the estate of Thelma Able Bledsoe, and others, appellants, brought proceedings in the Vanderburgh Probate Court to sell real estate to pay debts and Millard Fisher, personal representative of the estate of Bynus Bledsoe, and others, appellees, were made defendants in such proceedings. Appellee-personal representative filed demurrer which was sustained and upon appellants' failure to plead over, judgment was rendered for appellees. Appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, personal representative of wife's estate and others, sought review of an order from the Vanderburgh Probate Court (Indiana), which rendered a judgment for appellees, personal representative of husband's estate and others, on appellees' demurrer to appellants' complaint alleging that the husband murdered the wife, both of whom held title to certain real estate as tenants by the entirety.


OVERVIEW: The husband and the wife held title to the real estate as tenants by the entirety. Appellants brought the proceedings in the trial court against appellees to sell the real estate to pay debts. In their complaint, appellants alleged that the husband murdered the wife. Appellees' demurred to appellants' complaint for insufficient facts. Appellees' demurrer was sustained by the trial court. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment, concluding that the husband or his estate should not in equity have been permitted to take and keep the entire interest in fee in the property, which he had thus acquired by his wrongful act. The court further concluded that the husband, who was the murderer, became a constructive trustee for the estate of the wife, who was the victim, in one-half of the property. Because appellants' complaint stated a good cause of action for equitable relief as against appellees' demurrer for insufficient facts, the court concluded that the trial court erred in sustaining appellees' demurrer to appellants' complaint.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which was rendered for appellees on their demurrer to appellants' complaint alleging that the husband murdered the wife.

708 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Bissell Carpet Sweeper Co. v. Shane Co.


No. 29,327


Supreme Court of Indiana


237 Ind. 188; 143 N.E.2d 415; 1957 Ind. LEXIS 260



May 22, 1957, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 17, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Superior Court of Marion County, Hezzie B. Pike, Judge.

Bissell Carpet Sweeper Company, appellant, brought this action against Shane Company, Inc., appellee, under the Fair Trade Act, charging that appellee sold its goods at less than fair trade prices. Appellee's demurrer was sustained and upon failure to plead over judgment accordingly. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of order of the Marion County Superior Court (Indiana) sustaining appellee's demurrer in action brought under the Indiana Fair Trade Act, 1937 Ind. Acts ch. 17, §§ 66-301 to 66-309, charging appellee sold appellant's goods at less than fair trade prices.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered into contracts with retailers that established minimum resale prices of its goods. Appellee was not a party to a resale price contract, and resold the goods at less than contractually established minimum prices. Appellant subsequently notified appellee of the contracts and sued after appellee refused to comply with the minimum prices. The court held the Indiana Fair Trade Act (FTA), 1937 Ind. Acts ch. 17, §§ 66-301 to 66-309, allowed parties to contract for vertical price fixing from the original seller to the ultimate retailer. The Indiana General Assembly had authority to except fair trade price fixing by contract from the antitrust acts. The FTA was not an attempt to allow price fixing by private persons. Thus, appellant could not by contract with certain retailers make a price binding upon everyone retailing its goods. The contractual minimum prices were only binding on parties that contractually agreed to them.


OUTCOME: Order sustaining appellee's demurrer affirmed because appellee was not party to vertical price fixing contract and was not bound by minimum prices established in appellant's contracts with other retailers.

 

709 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Steers v. Holovachka


No. 29,464


Supreme Court of Indiana


236 Ind. 565; 142 N.E.2d 593; 1957 Ind. LEXIS 208



May 7, 1957, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Criminal Court of Lake County, William J. Murray, Judge.

The State of Indiana by the Attorney General, appellant, filed a verified application for the appointment of a special prosecutor to replace the regular prosecutor, Metro M. Holovachka, appellee. The court sustained appellee's motion to dismiss and appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Indiana appealed a judgment from the Criminal Court of Lake County (Indiana), which dismissed its verified application for the appointment of a special prosecutor to replace appellee, the regular prosecutor.


OVERVIEW: After an investigation, the State filed a report that contained evidence that a public officer might have committed certain criminal offenses with regard to certain public works and contracts during the time that he had been a city controller and chair of the municipal Board of Public Works. Both Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-3713 (1956) and Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-1247 (1950) prohibited a public officer from becoming financially interested in public contracts executed under his authority. Because the public officer was the current county prosecuting attorney, the state attorney general requested that he disqualify himself. He refused and the attorney general then filed a verified application for appointment of a special prosecutor. The trial court dismissed the application. On appeal, the court reviewed the statutes alleged to have been violated and determined that the sewer construction contracts involved were "public contracts" entered into by public authorities in the exercise of a governmental power. The court then reversed, concluding that the trial court should have ordered the prosecutor disqualified and appointed a disinterested person in his place.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the State's verified petition to appoint a special prosecutor and remanded with instructions for the trial court to order the prosecuting attorney disqualified from the proceedings and to appoint a disinterested person in his place.

Tinder v. Music Operating, Inc.


No. 29,476


Supreme Court of Indiana


237 Ind. 33; 142 N.E.2d 610; 1957 Ind. LEXIS 247



May 2, 1957, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 27, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room 1, Earl C. Townsend, Jr., Special Judge.

John Tinder and other public officials, appellants, were enjoined from interfering with the installation or operation by Music Operating, Inc., appellee, of its pinball machines in the City of Indianapolis.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed in part, reversed in part and ordered amended in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public officials sought review of a order of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which permanently enjoined them from interfering with the installation or operation by appellee corporation of its pinball machines. The public officials contended that the pinball machines were excluded under the Hasbrook Law, Ind. Code §§ 10-2329-2336 (1956 Repl.).


OVERVIEW: The public officials contended that the corporation was prohibited from installing and operating pinball machines under the Hasbrook Law, Ind. Code §§ 10-2329-2336 (1956 Repl.). The trial court entered a permanent injunction against the public officials enjoining them from interfering with the corporation's business regarding the machines. The public officials sought review. Pursuant to Ind. Const. art. 15, § 8, no lottery was authorized. The court determined, however, that if any substantial degree of skill or judgment was involved, it was not a lottery. The court held that the pinball machines were not lotteries within the meaning of the provision. The court held that the trial court had jurisdiction to issue restraining orders where property rights were invaded by the acts of the public officials. The court determined that the operation of the machines was legal under the new statute. However, the court found that any machines, which provided a right or replay were illegal under the statute. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part an order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part an order of the trial court, which entered a permanent injunction against the public officials enjoining them from interfering with the corporation's installation or operation of its pinball machines, and held that such machines were not prohibited under the Hasbrook Law.

Caesar v. De Vault


No. 29,410


Supreme Court of Indiana


236 Ind. 487; 141 N.E.2d 338; 1957 Ind. LEXIS 199



April 3, 1957, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Porter Circuit Court, G. L. Burns, Judge.

Appellees, Harold DeVault, township trustee of Calumet Township, Metro Holovachka, individually and as Prosecuting Attorney of Lake County, brought this action for declaratory judgment against Victoria Caesar, appellant, asking that appellant's appointment as Justice of the Peace be declared null and void and the trial court so found. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nominee sought review of a judgment from a trial court in Porter County (Indiana) in an action for declaratory judgment brought by appellees, a township trustee and a county prosecuting attorney, successfully asking that the nominee's appointment as Justice of the Peace be declared void.


OVERVIEW: The question presented was whether the township was entitled to more than one justice of the peace. The trial court found that at the time of her appointment there was a duly elected, qualified, and acting justice of the peace in the township, and that her appointment as a second justice of the peace was unlawful. The court held that the Indiana Acts of 1943, 1945, and 1949 were unconstitutional as violating equal protection, and that the number of justices of the peace permitted in the township was determined by the 1927 Ind. Acts ch. 155, § 1, which was obviously generally applicable throughout the state and prescribed the limit of such number to be two. As there was no question but that the nominee was otherwise qualified by her selection by the board of county commissioners, and her appointment and receipt of a commission from the governor, the decision of the trial court was contrary to law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, rendering judgment for the nominee.

 

712 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pearson Constr. Co.


No. 29,394


Supreme Court of Indiana


236 Ind. 602; 141 N.E.2d 448; 1957 Ind. LEXIS 211



March 26, 1957, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 14, 1957.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Marion Superior Court, Room No. 5, Paul B. Clark, Judge.

Pearson Construction Company, a Michigan Corporation, appellee, brought this action for the refund of gross income and bonus taxes levied on income derived from contracts to erect buildings for the U.S. Government on lands ceded to or purchased by the federal government. The trial court sustained the tax as to the part of income derived from contracts on land purchased by the U.S. Government but held the tax not applicable to contracts performed upon lands ceded to the federal government. The appellants, State of Indiana, Gross Income Tax Division and others, appealed, and the only issue raised on appeal regards the judgment as to the ceded property.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State of Indiana and others, appealed a judgment from a trial court (Indiana) in favor of plaintiff foreign construction corporation. The corporation had brought an action for the refund of gross income and bonus taxes levied on income derived from contracts to erect buildings for the United States Government on lands ceded to or purchased by the federal government under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 64-2614 (1951).


OVERVIEW: The trial court sustained the assessment of the tax on that part of the income derived from contracts on land that was purchased by the United States Government as distinguished from contracts performed upon lands, which were ceded, but held that by reason of the Cession Act of 1883, as amended by Acts 1901, Ind. Stat. Ann. St., §§ 62-1001, 62-1002, income derived from contracts performed upon lands ceded to the federal government by the State was not subject to the tax. The court held that the trial court erred in finding that such part the corporation's gross receipts in question and derived from construction work performed upon land ceded to the Federal Government were exempt from the provisions of the Indiana Gross Income Tax Act, as amended. The State acquired the right to tax private interests within the location by permission of Congress under the Buck Act, 4 U.S.C.S. §§ 104-110, which permitted state sales, use, and income taxes. The court also held that the State could tax when the United States divested itself of proprietary interest over the area on which the tax was sought. The Buck Act revoked any State tax immunity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

No. 29,414


Supreme Court of Indiana


236 Ind. 298; 140 N.E.2d 220; 1957 Ind. LEXIS 177



February 6, 1957, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room 2, Hezzie B. Pike, Judge.

Arthur John Mogilner, appellant, brings this action against the Metropolitan Plan Commission of Marion County, the Metropolitan Planning Department of Marion County and others, appellees, in which he seeks an injunction and declaratory judgment that chapter 283 of the Acts of 1955, Sections 53-901 to 53-990, Burns' 1951 Replacement, is unconstitutional. The trial court denied permanent injunction but found unconstitutional the last paragraph of Section 36 (Sec. 53-936), paragraph 5 of Section 38 (Sec. 53-938), last paragraph of Section 56 (Sec. 53-956), the middle paragraph of Section 69 (Sec. 53-969) on page 803 beginning with the word "neither" and ending with the word "director", the clause in Section 72 (Section 53-972) granting the Board of Zoning Appeals the right to issue a restraining order, the first paragraph of Section 81 (Sec. 53-981) and that Sections 83 and 84 (Sec. 53-983, Sec. 53-984) are each unconstitutional. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed as to that part of decree finding particulars of the Act unconstitutional. Affirmed as to that part of decree denying permanent injunction [***2] .


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Marion County Superior Court (Indiana) which held that certain sections of 1955 Ind. Acts ch. 283, §§ 53-901 to 53-990 (Act) were unconstitutional and denying appellant an injunction against appellee boards and officials.


OVERVIEW: The Act established a metropolitan plan commission and vested in the commission the power to establish a master plan and zoning authority for all areas within the county. Paragraph 5 of § 38 of the Act was not unconstitutional because appellant failed to show that the classification of cities and different treatment for those classifications was unjust or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed insofar as it found that certain sections of the Act were unconstitutional. The judgment was affirmed insofar as it denied appellant a permanent injunction.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) convicted defendant of burglary with intent to commit a felony, rape. Defendant appealed the trial court's determination that he was not a criminally sexually psychopathic person.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with burglary, with the intent to commit a felony rape, and with rape. The trial court found that defendant was not a criminally sexual psychopathic person. The trial court did not abuse its discretion.

716 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Cemetery Co. v. Warren School Township


No. 29,397


Supreme Court of Indiana


236 Ind. 171; 139 N.E.2d 538; 1957 Ind. LEXIS 162



January 7, 1957, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Circuit Court, Lloyd D. Claycombe, Judge.

Warren School Township of Marion County, appellee, filed a suit to take by eminent domain for school purposes the property already dedicated to a public use owned by the Cemetery Company, appellant. Appellant filed objections to which the appellee addressed a motion to dismiss which was sustained and the court appointed appraisers. Appellant now takes this interlocutory appeal in which Memorial Park Cemetery Association is also named as appellee.



DISPOSITION: Remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged a decision of the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), which dismissed the landowner's objections to appellee school corporation's action that sought to take by eminent domain for school purposes property that was dedicated to another public use.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the landowner's objections to the school corporation's eminent domain action were improperly dismissed. The court held that courts could not inquire into the administrative determination of the propriety, reasonableness, or necessity for the taking of property by eminent domain by a proper authority, except for fraud, or where the proceeding is a subterfuge for taking property for private use. On the other hand, the court held that courts had the duty to determine the legal authority and the limits thereof of those persons or bodies attempting to exercise the power of eminent domain. However, the appellate court held that the trial court, under guise of interpreting the law, improperly granted a priority to one public use over another conflicting public use. According to the court, the legislature had not seen fit to expressly grant such superior or overriding power of eminent domain.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which dismissed the landowner's objections to the school corporation's eminent domain action. The court remanded for further proceedings.

 

717 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Gross Income Tax Div. v. Chi. Dist. Elec. Generating Corp.


No. 29,227


Supreme Court of Indiana


236 Ind. 117; 139 N.E.2d 161; 1956 Ind. LEXIS 245



December 20, 1956, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Lake Circuit Court, Felix A. Kaul, Judge.

The Chicago District Electric Generating Corporation brought action to recover taxes paid under protest for years 1947 through 1952 together with interest. From a judgment in favor of plaintiff, the Gross Income Tax Division appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Gross Income Tax Division (division) sought review of a judgment from the Lake Circuit Court (Indiana), which held a tax on appellee utility's gross income from electricity transmissions was a tax on interstate commerce in violation of the Gross Income Tax Act (Act) and U.S. Const. art. 1, § 8. The division claimed the utility's transmission of electricity across state lines was wholly within the state and a purely local activity.


OVERVIEW: The utility, which was located in Indiana but which abutted the boundary line with Illinois, transmitted electricity to a power plant in Indiana and to a power plant in Illinois. When the division taxed the utility's gross income from its transmissions of electricity, the utility challenged the tax, claiming it was a tax on interstate commerce in violation of the Act and U.S. Const. art. 1, § 8. Following a judgment for the utility, the division sought review, and the court affirmed. Noting the generation and transmission of electrical energy was a continuous and simultaneous operation, the court held that where transmissions of electrical energy were made to points within a state different from the state in which it was generated and produced, such transactions were in interstate commerce. Therefore, the court held the utility's transmissions of electricity across Indiana's state line and into Illinois had constituted transactions in interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that held a tax on the utility's gross income from electricity transmissions was an illegal and unconstitutional tax on interstate commerce.

 

718 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Fox v. La Porte Circuit Court


No. 29,396


Supreme Court of Indiana


236 Ind. 69; 138 N.E.2d 875; 1956 Ind. LEXIS 243



December 17, 1956, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by the State of Indiana on relation of Raymond M. Fox, Jr., Prosecuting Attorney, relator, which seeks a writ of mandate asking that respondents, LaPorte Circuit Court, Jacob A. Fleishbein, Special Judge, etc., be mandated to expunge the records of said court of the entry granting a change of venue from LaPorte County. An alternative writ was issued.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ heretofore issued made parmanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought a writ of mandate asking that respondents court and judge be required to expunge the records of the court of an entry granting a change of venue in a murder trial.


OVERVIEW: Following a defendant's indictment for murder, a motion for a change of venue was filed and granted, and venue was changed. A verdict of guilty was returned, but a motion for a new trial was granted. In the second trial, the defendant sought a change of venue and was denied. Defendant then sought change of venue from the judge, and respondent judge was selected and qualified. Defendant again sought a change in venue. The judge granted the change of venue. The state sought a writ of mandate asking that the court and judge be mandated to expunge the records of the court of the entry granting the change of venue. The court granted the writ of mandate, holding that because the defendant had received the only change of venue permitted by statute, the lower court had no jurisdiction to entertain or grant the subsequent change of venue.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ of mandate to expunge the record.

 

719 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Griffin Tel. Corp.V Public Service Com.


No. 29,310


Supreme Court of Indiana


236 Ind. 29; 138 N.E.2d 150; 1956 Ind. LEXIS 237



November 16, 1956, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Superior Court (General Term), Walter Pritchard, Presiding Judge.

Appellant Utility, Griffin Telephone Corporation, brought action to vacate, set aside and enjoin adverse decision of Public Service Commission in rate increase petition. Upon the motion to dismiss, filed by the Commission, the court dismissed the action.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to vacate and enjoin the decision of appellee Public Service Commission of Indiana in a rate increase petition, appellant utility challenged a judgment from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana) dismissing the action for lack of jurisdiction of the subject matter. The utility asserted that the trial court had jurisdiction to review a rate order under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 54-203 (1951).


OVERVIEW: When the Commission denied the utility's petition for a rate increase, the utility brought an action to review the order. The trial court dismissed the case for lack of jurisdiction and the utility appealed, urging that the trial court had jurisdiction under § 54-203. The Commission insisted that the complaint was defective in not alleging that the subject matter of the procedure had been in the trial court's county. The court disagreed, explaining that § 54-203 provided for de novo review in the circuit court of the county where a utility was located or in the superior court of Marion County (Indiana). The Commission contended that § 54-203 was unconstitutional to the extent that it attempted to amend a prior statute because it omitted certain sections from its title. However, this claim failed because the omitted sections had already been superceded and an act which attempted to amend a non-existent law or section was itself void. The court held that § 54-203 was constitutional and was the proper procedure for obtaining a review of rulings of the Commission in rate cases. Thus, the utility's complaint seeking review had been sufficient as against the motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court with directions to overrule the Commission's motion to dismiss the utility's complaint.

 

720 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Kees v. Smith


No. 29,431


Supreme Court of Indiana


235 Ind. 687; 137 N.E.2d 541; 1956 Ind. LEXIS 208



October 18, 1956, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Wells Circuit Court, Homer J. Byrd, Judge.

Appellants, Charles Kees and others, as taxpayers, brought action to enjoin appellees, Lester E. Smith, as Trustee of Springfield School Township, and Springfield Township School Building Corporation, from carrying out provisions of lease and having lease declared void.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers filed an action against appellees, the trustees of a township school and a township school building corporation, seeking to enjoin appellees from carrying out the provisions of a school building lease. The taxpayers appealed after the Wells Circuit Court (Indiana) upheld the validity of the lease and entered a judgment that the taxpayers should take nothing under their complaint.


OVERVIEW: The trustees sold property to the corporation with the understanding that the corporation would build a school building and then lease it back to the school over 30 years; the school would acquire title to the building at the end of the lease's term. On appeal, the taxpayers contended that the arrangement violated the equal protection provision found in Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23 because it granted a special privilege to the corporation that others did not enjoy. They also asserted that, when the lease payments were considered together, the lease violated the debt limitation imposed by Ind. Const. art. 13, § 1. The court rejected the taxpayers' arguments. Ind. Stat. Ann. § 28-3227 (Cum. Supp. 1955), which allowed the trustees to sell the property to the corporation, did not extend a special privilege in violation of Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23; the statute merely insured that the property would continued to be used for its intended public purpose. The lease did not give rise to an to an indebtedness for the aggregate of all the rentals for the entire term because it was truly a lease and not an installment purchase contract; no violation of Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23 was shown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

721 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Pennsylvania R. Co. v. Iroquois Conservancy Dist. Court


No. 29,299


Supreme Court of Indiana


235 Ind. 353; 133 N.E.2d 848; 1956 Ind. LEXIS 161



April 20, 1956, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by the State of Indiana on relation of the Pennsylvania Railroad Company, Chicago, Indianapolis and Louisville Railway Company, and The New York Central Railroad Company, relators, seeking a writ of prohibition to prohibit further proceedings for the establishment of a Conservancy District by respondents, Iroquois Conservancy District Court of Indiana, Jasper Circuit Court, Moses Leopold, as Judge of Jasper Circuit Court, 30th Judicial Circuit: Moses Leopold as Judge of Iroquois Conservancy District Court of Indiana: Newton Circuit Court, Newell A. Lamb, as Judge of Newton Circuit Court, 79th Judicial Circuit: Newell A. Lamb as Judge of Iroquois Conservancy District Court of Indiana. A temporary writ of prohibition was issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ of prohibition heretofore issued made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator railroads filed an action seeking a writ of prohibition to prohibit respondent judges from establishing respondent conservancy district as provided in the Conservancy Act (act), 1947 Ind. Acts ch. 239. The railroads contended that the judges were without jurisdiction because the act was unconstitutional as violating Ind. Const. art. 4, § 19, which provided that an act shall embrace one subject. The court issued a temporary writ.


OVERVIEW: The railroads contended that the act violated Ind. Const. art. 4, § 19 which provided that every act shall embrace but one subject and matters properly connected therewith which subject shall be expressed in the title. Section 6 of the act created a special court made up of judges of each circuit court where a proposed conservancy district was located to establish districts upon appropriate petition. The purpose of that act as set forth in its title was to prevent floods, to protect cities, towns, farms and highways from inundation, to conserve water for beneficial uses, and to authorize the organization of drainage and conservancy districts, and declaring an emergency. The court held that the title to the act was not sufficiently broad to include the establishment of a new court because the title to the act was narrow in scope, limited to issues relating to flooding and conservation of water, and one reading the act would be surprised to find that an entirely new and novel court was created to administer the act. The court concluded that, pursuant to art. 4, § 19, the act could not be construed to extend its operations beyond the conservation purpose expressed in the title.


OUTCOME: The court made the temporary writ previously issued permanent.

 

722 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Wright-Bachman, Inc. v. Hodnett


No. 29,277


Supreme Court of Indiana


235 Ind. 307; 133 N.E.2d 713; 1956 Ind. LEXIS 157



April 12, 1956, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion County Superior Court No. 3, Norman E. Brennan, Judge.

Nolan Jack Hodnett, appellee, brought this action against Wright-Bachman, Inc., appellant, and Goshen Churn & Ladder, Inc., appellee, to recover damages for injuries sustained in falling from a scaffold. A verdict was returned against appellant and judgment accordingly and appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant seller, a ladder manufacturer, challenged the decision of the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which overruled the seller's motion for a new trial in appellee buyer's products liability action.


OVERVIEW: The action was brought by the buyer, a construction worker, against the seller to recover damages for personal injuries the buyer sustained when he fell from a scaffold, which allegedly collapsed because of a defective ladder. The first paragraph of the amended complaint alleged a breach of warranty concerning the ladder, and the second paragraph was grounded on negligence in the ladder's construction. The trial court, after a jury trial, entered a verdict in favor of the buyer. The trial court overruled the seller's motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court. The court found that under § 13 of the Workmen's Compensation Act (Act), Ind. Code § 40-1213, the buyer had six months from the date his injuries accrued in which to have brought his action. The buyer failed to do so. The court held that under the Act the buyer was allowed to bring a products liability action in either tort or contract. The Act was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which overruled the seller's motion for a new trial in the buyer's products liability action.

 

723 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Bartley v. Marion Circuit Court


No. 29,333


Supreme Court of Indiana


235 Ind. 226; 132 N.E.2d 703; 1956 Ind. LEXIS 147



March 13, 1956, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by State of Indiana on relation of Robert Bartley, relator, for a writ of prohibition against the Judge of the Marion Circuit Court from assuming jurisdiction of certain criminal charges against relator.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ of prohibition, as amended, is made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner instituted an action for a writ of prohibition against respondent, a circuit court judge, to bar the judge from assuming jurisdiction of certain criminal charges against petitioner. The court granted petitioner's application for a temporary writ of prohibition.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with criminal offenses in a magistrates court, pleaded not guilty and demanded a jury trial, and was bound over to the circuit court for trial. Petitioner challenged the transfer, claiming that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 4-3806(c) (1946), which created the magistrates court, was unconstitutional in that it deprived persons charged with a crime of a jury trial in such court. The court determined that the right to a jury trial was subject to reasonable regulations and conditions made by the legislature and that defendant's constitutional privilege to a jury trial was not infringed upon. The court also ruled that the circuit court's blanket order for bonds applying to transfers from the magistrates court was authorized by Ind. Stat. Ann. § 4-3805 (1946) and that petitioner could not object to the amount of the bond since he did not exhaust his remedy by applying to the circuit court for special or discriminatory treatment. The court further ruled that the county criminal court, not the circuit court, had exclusive jurisdiction to try cases transferred from the magistrates court.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that its previously issued temporary writ of prohibition be amended to prohibit the circuit court from entertaining jurisdiction of the criminal charges against petitioner and, as amended, made the writ permanent.

 

724 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Becker v. Albion-Jefferson School Corp.


No. 29,291


Supreme Court of Indiana


235 Ind. 204; 132 N.E.2d 269; 1956 Ind. LEXIS 143



February 21, 1956, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Steuben Circuit Court, Harris W. Hubbard, Judge.

Rolla Becker and others, appellants, sought a permanent injunction to prevent appellees, Albion-Jefferson School Corporation and Albion-Jefferson School Building Corporation, from carrying out the terms of a certain lease and to have said lease declared void. From a judgment favorable to appellees, appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to invalidate a lease of school property, appellants challenged a judgment from the Steuben Circuit Court (Indiana) in favor of appellees, Albion-Jefferson (Indiana) School Corporation and Albion-Jefferson (Indiana) School Building Corporation. Appellants urged that the lease under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 28-3227 (Supp. 1955) (Act) violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sought to permanently enjoin appellees from carrying out a certain lease and to have the lease declared void. From a judgment for appellees, appellants sought review, insisting that the Act was unconstitutional because it granted a special privilege to the building corporation organized under the Act which was not available to any other person or corporation. The court disagreed, explaining that the Act permitted school corporations owning land to sell it to a private corporation, which would then provide a needed building and lease it to the school corporation. The provision that property owned by a school corporation could not be sold or leased to any person or corporation other than one formed solely for the purpose of erecting a school building and leasing it to the school corporation was meant to assure the public use of the property as originally intended at the time of its purchase by the school corporation. The Act conferred no privilege upon any person or group in a holding corporation and it did not limit the number of corporations which could be organized and could negotiate to provide school facilities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
