Public Service Com. v. Indianapolis


No. 29,266


Supreme Court of Indiana


235 Ind. 70; 131 N.E.2d 308; 1956 Ind. LEXIS 132



January 11, 1956, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, in banc.

The City of Indianapolis, appellee, brought action to set aside and enjoin enforcement of an order of appellants, Public Service Commission, Warren Buchanan, M. Eliot Belshaw and Wendell Tennis, as members of the Commission, which order approved a new rate schedule for appellant, Indianapolis Water Company. Pursuant to the trial court's instructions, appellee perfected a statutory appeal from the Commission's order and the same was consolidated with the injunction action. Judgment was entered vacating the Commission's order and granting permanent injunction. Appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Public Service Commission of Indiana (Commission) and a water company, sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which denied their motion for a new trial in an action filed by plaintiff city to set aside a new rate schedule.


OVERVIEW: The city filed an action to set aside and enjoin enforcement of an order from the Commission, which approved a new rate schedule for the water company. The trial court awarded judgment to the city. The trial court denied the motion for a new trial filed by the Commission and the water company. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, determining that the findings of the trial court were contrary to law and not supported by the evidence. The court further found that the trial court's determination that the fair valuation of the used and useful property of the water company as fixed by the Commission was unreasonable and excessive was not supported by the evidence. Accordingly, the court held that the Commission performed its legislative function within its proper sphere. It did not step outside the statutory or constitutional limitations placed upon it.


OUTCOME: The order denying the motion for a new trial filed by the Commission and the water company and the order setting aside the rate schedule were reversed and remanded.

 

726 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Foltz v. Indianapolis


No. 29,293


Supreme Court of Indiana


234 Ind. 656; 130 N.E.2d 650; 1955 Ind. LEXIS 187



December 16, 1955, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Hancock Circuit Court, Samuel J. Offutt, Judge.

Appellants, Gerald L. Foltz, Van Camp Hardware & Iron Co., John S. Elmore, William F. Krieg, Burford Danner and Helen D. Garrigues, sought a declaratory judgment and injunction challenging the constitutionality of the Off-Street Parking Act. Appellees are City of Indianapolis, Indianapolis Off-Street Parking Commission, Indianapolis Department of Off-Street Parking and Edwin K. Steers, Attorney General of State of Indiana. From a judgment in favor of appellees, appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, individuals and a store, filed an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against appellee municipality and state attorney general. The individuals and the store challenged a judgment of the Hancock Circuit Court (Indiana), which determined that the First-Class Cities Off-Street Parking Act ("Act"), Acts 1949, ch. 241, §§ 48-8421 to 48-8443, as amended (§§ 48-8430 1950 Replacement (1955 Supp.)), was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The individuals and store contended that if off-street parking facilities were a public necessity justifying the condemnation of land for public use, the legislature lacked constitutional authority to divest the state of its constitutional right to exercise its police power over the two sites involved. The court rejected that contention, holding that the state could delegate a portion of its police power to a subordinate municipality, commission or board created by the state under a long-term lease arrangement, and that the Act was constitutional. However, the court, based on the meaning of the words used in the Act, held that the municipality failed to follow the provisions outlined in the Act with respect to asking for bids for leasing the two sites. Thus, the acceptance of the bids were rendered invalid. The court ruled that terms and provisions which would assure that the off-street parking facilities would not be diverted under some private contract to the exclusion of the public generally were required, and determined that the bidding and the proposed leases were defective in failing to provide such safeguards. The judgment was thus reversed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment in favor of the municipality was reversed and the trial court was directed to restate its conclusions of law and grant the individuals' and store's prayer for a permanent injunction to the extent indicated with regard to the bidding and leasing procedure.

State ex rel. Savery v. Criminal Court of Marion County


No. 29,329


Supreme Court of Indiana


234 Ind. 632; 130 N.E.2d 128; 1955 Ind. LEXIS 183



November 18, 1955, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 14, 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original action by relator, Paul Walcott Savery, alias Robert L. Dennison, alias Roger Donovan, for writ of mandate and prohibition against the Criminal Court of Marion County, Division One, Scott A. McDonald, Judge, to compel court to proceed on an application of relator under Sexual Psychopathic Act.



DISPOSITION: Temporary Writ dissolved and permanent writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case came before the court on an original action for writ of mandate and prohibition against respondent Criminal Court of Marion County, Division One (Indiana) brought by relator accused to compel respondent to proceed on an application of the accused under the Sexual Psychopathic Act, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 9-3401 (Cum. Supp. 1953). A temporary writ issued.


OVERVIEW: The accused was charged with robbery and physical injury while in the commission of robbery. The accused pled not guilty and also filed a plea of insanity. After a statutory examination, the accused filed a verified application with statements of his physicians and requested the court to hold a hearing for the purpose of declaring the accused a criminal sexual psychopathic person. The trial court contended that under the Act, although the proceedings were mandatory when requested by the prosecuting attorney, they were discretionary with the court when requested on behalf of the accused in a criminal case. The court held that the Act did not apply because the accused was not charged with a sexual offense. Also, since the Act placed no restriction on the trial court's denial of a request on behalf of the accused for a hearing, the accused could not force the trial court to grant a hearing. The trial court could take into consideration the accused's plea of insanity, which the Act excluded, in exercising its discretion.


OUTCOME: The temporary writ was dissolved and the permanent writ denied.

 

728 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Madison v. State


No. 29,188


Supreme Court of Indiana


234 Ind. 517; 130 N.E.2d 35; 1955 Ind. LEXIS 169



November 4, 1955, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Vanderburgh Circuit Court, Ollie C. Reeves, Judge.

James B. Madison, appellant, was found guilty of murder in the second degree. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) which, following a jury trial, convicted defendant of murder in the second degree under an indictment charging murder in the first degree. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in overruling his motion to quash the indictment and in overruling his motion for a new trial, which alleged that the verdict was not sustained by the evidence and was contrary to law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a paratrooper just returned from overseas duty. He went to a dance hall and was attacked during a brawl. Defendant pulled the safety pin out of a grenade to keep the crowd back. He either dropped or threw the grenade. The grenade exploded and killed the victim. Defendant was charged with murder with a deadly weapon called a hand grenade loaded with nitroglycerin. The court found that one of the jury instructions given was fatally defective in that it left the impression that defendant might be convicted of a lesser included offense without proof beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also determined that the erroneous instruction was not cured by other instructions giving the correct principles involved. In addition, the court held that, pursuant to Ind. Const. art. I, § 13, defendant had a constitutional right to be prosecuted on a specific charge intended to give warning of the evidence that might be introduced against him so that he might defend against it. The court concluded that, where the prosecution falsely represented that nitroglycerin was the explosive in the grenade in order to inflame the jury, there was a variance between the proof and the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and granted a new trial.

Goldstine v. State


No. 29,185


Supreme Court of Indiana


234 Ind. 388; 126 N.E.2d 581; 1955 Ind. LEXIS 154



May 23, 1955, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 14, 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Noble Circuit Court, Walter Brubaker, Special Judge.

Appellant, Sam Goldstine (also Goldstein) was convicted of second degree burglary and possession of burglar tools by one previously convicted of a felony, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Noble Circuit Court (Indiana) for second degree burglary, in violation of Ind. Code Ann. § 10-701 (1942), and possession of burglar tools by one previously convicted of a felony, in violation of Ind. Code Ann. § 10-703 (1942). Defendant assigned as error the trial court's overruling of his motion to quash, motion in arrest of judgment and his motion for new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the second degree burglary count was insufficient because it failed to allege that the grocery store where the crime was committed was a place other than a dwelling house or place of human habitation. He also challenged the constitutionality of § 10-703. The State sought dismissal of the appeal because defendant's assignment of errors was filed under the name of "Sam Goldstine" while the judgment of conviction in the trial court was against "Sam Goldstein." Affirming, the court held that the State should not have been allowed to take advantage of technical errors and that the name in the assignment of errors and the name in the judgment of conviction were phonetically identical even though the spelling was slightly different. The court noted that in a prior appeal it had held that the second degree burglary count adequately charged the crime of second degree burglary. Moreover, § 10-703 was constitutional and did not unreasonably classify ex-convicts in violation of the Fourteenth Amendment or Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23 and art. 4, § 20. The court found ample evidence of probative force to support the decision of the trial judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

DISPOSITION: ON PETITION FOR REHEARING. Petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen sought review of an order in favor of defendant, state and its officials, by an Indiana trial court, which found that 1945 Ind. Acts. § 11-1424 (Cum. Supp. 1953), which exempted former members of the armed services of the United States from paying any consideration for hunting and fishing licenses, was constitutional. After the court reversed the trial court, the state and its officials filed a petition for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: The Indiana General Assembly passed § 11-1424, which exempted former members of the armed services of the United States from paying any consideration for hunting and fishing licenses. The citizen filed suit and maintained that the legislation violated both Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23, and the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. The trial court held in favor of the state and its officials and the court reversed on appeal. The state and its officials filed a petition for rehearing. The court denied the petition for rehearing and held that: (1) the purpose of 1937 Ind. Acts ch. 21 (Act) was the protection of the state's wildlife; (2) the exemption provided to those who served in the military was artificial, unreasonable, and in direct conflict with the purpose of the Act; and (3) 1945 Ind. Acts. § 11-1424 (Cum. Supp. 1953) was unconstitutional under the state and federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for rehearing.

Book v. Indianapolis-Marion Bldg. Authority


No. 29,228


Supreme Court of Indiana


234 Ind. 250; 126 N.E.2d 5; 1955 Ind. LEXIS 142



April 20, 1955, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Circuit Court, Lloyd D. Claycombe, Judge.

William H. Book, appellant, brought this action to enjoin Indianapolis-Marion Building Authority, its directors and trustees, from expending any funds appropriated to it by the Marion County Council and from taking any action under Ch. 54, Acts of 1953. Appellees filed their demurrer which was sustained and appellant refused to plead over and judgment was entered accordingly.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a county taxpayer and citizen, brought an action in the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana) to enjoin appellees, a city building authority, its directors, and trustees, from expending any funds appropriated to it by the county council for the payment of rents for office space. The trial court sustained appellees' demurrer and the taxpayer refused to plead over. A judgment was then entered for appellees. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to an act passed by the General Assembly, the county was given the authority to lease property for county employees. Pursuant to the act, the county council could have committed to pay rental on a building for a period of 40 years. The aggregate amount of the rental over the entire period of the lease constituted an indebtedness that was in excess of the indebtedness permitted under Ind. Const. art. XIII, § 1. The taxpayer filed his action asserting that the lease was void because it violated § 1 and its limitation on indebtedness. Appellees' demurrer asserted that the complaint did not state facts sufficient to show that the rentals reserved under the leases constituted indebtedness in excess of the indebtedness permitted under § 1 in that the annual indebtedness did not exceed the constitutional limitations. On appeal, the court held that the demurrer was properly sustained. The entire aggregate rental over the 40-year term of the lease was not the basis for determining the amount of debt assumed by the county. The constitutional debt limitation applied to the annual rent because the future annual rent did not become debts until earned.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order sustaining appellees' demurrer.

 

732 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Johnson v. Reeves


No. 29,252


Supreme Court of Indiana


234 Ind. 225; 125 N.E.2d 794; 1955 Ind. LEXIS 138



April 14, 1955, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by Edmond Johnson, on relation of the State of Indiana, seeking a writ of prohibition to prevent the Vanderburgh Circuit Court and Ollie C. Reeves, as Judge thereof, from enforcing an order and judgment entered under the Reciprocal Enforcement of Duties of Support Act.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ dissolved and permanent writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator father sought a writ of prohibition to prevent respondents, trial court and judge, from enforcing an order and judgment entered under the Reciprocal Enforcement of Duties of Support Act, Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 3-3103 to 3-3120 (Burns' 1946 Repl.) (1953 Cum. Supp.).


OVERVIEW: A complaint was filed in the trial court in order to enforce a judgment of support obtained in another state and the father entered a special appearance to file a plea in abatement. However, the father filed a motion to dismiss on non-jurisdictional grounds, which was denied, and thereafter filed an answer and appeared at trial. Judgment was entered against the father and he filed a petition for a writ of prohibition to prevent the trial court and judge from enforcing the judgment. The court issued an alternative writ and thereafter dissolved the writ and denied a permanent writ of prohibition. Because the trial court had all the essential elements of jurisdiction the court was without power to grant the writ. It was not disputed that the trial court had jurisdiction over the subject matter and jurisdiction over the father. The trial court had jurisdiction over the case because the father failed to timely challenged the trial court's jurisdiction and, therefore, waived the issue. While he filed a special appearance he failed to challenge the jurisdiction of the trial court and subsequently made a general appearance and participated in the trial.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of prohibition sought by the father against the judge and trial court.

Appellee, William Leon Fifer, on relation of the State of Indiana, brought this action to obtain judgment for his salary as a probation officer and to mandate appropriation for the amount due. Trial resulted in judgment for $ 5,600.00 against appellant Board of Commissioners of Noble County and the decree further ordered the appellant, John Singleton, Jr., Auditor of Noble County, to prepare an ordinance of appropriation of this sum. The decree further ordered appellant Noble County Council, to meet and adopt said ordinance of appropriation. The Board of Commissioners and Auditor were then ordered to pay over to appellee the sum of $ 5,600.00. The appellants, Noble County Council, its members, the Board of County Commissioners of the County of Noble and its members and John Singleton, Jr., Auditor of Noble County, prosecute this appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed, except the trial court is ordered to vacate its decree of mandate directed to certain appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Board of Commissioners and the county council, sought review of the judgment of the Noble Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered a judgment in favor of appellee probation officer in the officer's action to obtain judgment for his salary and to mandate appropriation for the amount due.


OVERVIEW: The probation officer was appointed by the county court to his position, and his salary was fixed at $ 2,500 per annum. The court found that the county court had the inherent, constitutional and statutory authority to appoint the officer and to fix his salary. Thereafter, it became the mandatory duty of the county council to appropriate funds for that expense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which entered a judgment in favor of the probation officer in the officer's action to obtain judgment for his salary and to mandate appropriation for the amount due.

Bally v. Guilford Township School Corp.


No. 29,223


Supreme Court of Indiana


234 Ind. 273; 126 N.E.2d 13; 1954 Ind. LEXIS 285



December 22, 1954, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] (Recalled) Rehearing Granted April 19, 1955. Judgment Affirmed April 21, 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Hendricks Circuit Court, Walter O. Lewis, Judge.

Appellants, William G. Bally and Margaret Bally, husband and wife, and Alan Johnston and Mary Catherine Johnston, husband and wife, brought this action against Guilford Township School Corporation and the Board Members thereof. The constitutionality of Chapter 88, Acts of 1953, was at issue and the trial court adjudged the statute valid and constitutional. Appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens sought review of a judgment of the Hendricks Circuit Court (Indiana), which held that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 28-2455 et seq. (Supp. 1953), was constitutional. After the court issued its original opinion, appellees, the Guilford Township School Corporation (Indiana) and its Board Members, filed a petition for rehearing. The court granted rehearing and recalled its original opinion.


OVERVIEW: Section 28-2455 et seq. provided that the voters of a township could elect to transfer control of the township schools from the township trustee, in whom such control had traditionally resided in Indiana, to a school corporation, under a five-member board of school trustees. In accordance with § 28-2455 et seq., the Corporation was established and the Board Members were appointed. The citizens claimed that the statute was a local and special law in contravention of Ind. Const. art. 4, § 22(10), (13), § 23. Specifically, the citizens contended that the statute was invalid on the ground that it was too limited in application because it applied only to townships with an incorporated town of at least 2,000 persons. On rehearing, the court held that the statute was not unconstitutional. The court reasoned that the legislature was entitled to create a classification based on population and that the classification was constitutional because it was not arbitrary, capricious, unreasonable, irrational, or artificial. The citizens failed to show that the statute constituted unreasonable discrimination against any other school corporation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

735 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Hanley v. State


No. 29,170


Supreme Court of Indiana


234 Ind. 326; 123 N.E.2d 452; 1954 Ind. LEXIS 288



December 21, 1954, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 20, 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Hancock Circuit Court, Samuel J. Offutt, Judge.

Harry G. Hanley, appellant, filed his complaint asking for a declaratory judgment that Section 11-1424, Burns' 1942 Replacement (1953 Supplement), providing for free hunting and fishing licenses to veterans, be declared unconstitutional. Appellees, State of Indiana, Indiana Department of Conservation, Doxie M. Moore, director thereof, and others, received a favorable judgment. Appellant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment entered in the Hanley Circuit Court (Indiana) in favor of appellees, State of Indiana, Indiana Department of Conservation, and state officials, in appellant's declaratory judgment action which requested a determination that a statute providing for free hunting and fishing licenses to veterans was unconstitutional. Appellant also sought review of the denial of his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a complaint contending that § 11-1424 Burns' 1942 Repl. Cum. Supp., providing for free hunting and fishing licenses to veterans, was in conflict with Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1. The trial court ruled that the statute was constitutional. On appeal, the court reversed and ruled that the legislation was not a valid exercise of the legislature's police power. The court took judicial notice of the fact that a high percentage of persons of hunting age were ex-members of the armed forces and concluded that to exempt them from paying the fee for hunting and fishing licenses would have tended to deplete the funds available for protection and propagation of wildlife and thereby retarded and delayed conservation objectives. The court found that the legislative act which produced this result could not have had even a tendency to protect public health, morals, order, safety, or welfare and that the statute was in contravention of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment entered in favor of appellees in appellant's declaratory judgment action which requested a determination that a statute providing for free hunting and fishing licenses to veterans was unconstitutional. The court instructed the lower court to sustain appellant's motion for a new trial.

 

736 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Archer v. Indianapolis


No. 29,197


Supreme Court of Indiana


233 Ind. 640; 122 N.E.2d 607; 1954 Ind. LEXIS 255



November 17, 1954, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Circuit Court, Lloyd D. Claycombe, Judge.

Appellant, Ralph Archer, Jr., on behalf of himself and others similarly situated, brought an action to enjoin the Indianapolis Sanitary District from issuing and selling bonds and to enjoin tax levy by said district for payment thereof and from adverse decision, he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision by the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered judgment for appellees, the City of Indianapolis, the Indianapolis Sanitary District, and certain city officials, in the taxpayer's action to enjoin the District from issuing and selling bonds and to enjoin a tax levy by the District for the payment of the bonds.


OVERVIEW: The District sought to issue and sell certain tax bonds to provide for additions, extensions, and improvements to the City's existing sanitation facilities. The bonds the District proposed to issued, together with bonds previously issued and outstanding, totaled an amount in excess of two percent of the net assessed valuation of taxable property within the district. The taxpayer claimed that the issuance of the bonds was in conflict with Ind. Const. art. XIII, § 3, which prevented a municipal corporation from becoming indebted in an aggregate exceeding two percent of the value of taxable property within that corporation. The trial court entered judgment for appellees and overruled the taxpayer's motion for a new trial. On appeal, the court held that The District did not constitute a political or municipal corporation. The court noted that the District acted in the name of the City and that it could sue or be sued in the name of the City. The court concluded, therefore, that the legislature, when it created the District, did not create a separate entity or distinct municipality, but a special taxing district that was not subject to the restriction of Ind. Const. art. XIII, § 3.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

737 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Phillips v. Officials of Valparaiso


No. 29,153


Supreme Court of Indiana


233 Ind. 414; 120 N.E.2d 398; 1954 Ind. LEXIS 208



June 16, 1954, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the LaPorte Circuit Court, John J. Davie, Judge.

Robert Phillips and others on behalf of other freehold taxpayers instituted an action for injunction against city officials of Valparaiso seeking to prevent issuance of certain obligation bonds of city for acquisition of land for off-street parking facilities. From a denial of the injunction, appellants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged a decision of the LaPorte Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted judgment to appellee city in the taxpayers' action to enjoin the city from issuing city obligation bonds for the acquisition of land for off-street parking facilities.


OVERVIEW: The state provided cities with authority to acquire property for off-street parking and to use city obligation bonds to finance the purchases. When the city began efforts to make the acquisitions, the taxpayers initiated an action to enjoin the city from issuing city obligation bonds. The trial court granted judgment to the city because it determined that the city's actions were valid exercises of the powers granted in the enabling legislation. The taxpayers asserted that: (a) the trial court erred when it refused to permit evidence that the city abused its discretion in enacting the ordinances; (b) 1947 Ind. Acts. ch. 288, which enabled the city action, violated Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23; and (c) the bond ordinance was unreasonable and void. The court affirmed the decision that denied the taxpayers' request to enjoin the city because: (1) the off-street parking was a legislative function, and the courts could not examine the legislative process; (2) the provision of off-street parking did not discriminate against taxpayers who did not own cars; and (3) the taxpayers made no showing that the off-street parking ordinances were unreasonable and void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

738 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State


No. 29,102


Supreme Court of Indiana


233 Ind. 398; 120 N.E.2d 165; 1954 Ind. LEXIS 207



June 15, 1954, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Criminal Court Division No. 1, Harry O. Chamberlin, Judge.

Joe Robert Taylor was charged by indictment returned June 12, 1950, with crime of first degree burglary. After being held by warden in Hospital for Insane Criminals, he was sent back for trial upon regaining sanity, and after trial was ordered committed to Epileptic Village and as long as he remained case was taken under advisement. In 1953, after escape and apprehension, he was taken before court for sentencing and was sentenced. He appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Marion Criminal Court (Indiana) sentencing him on a first-degree burglary guilty plea following his escape from an epileptic center.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by indictment with the crime of first degree burglary. After being held in a hospital for insane criminals, he was sent back for trial upon regaining sanity. He pleaded guilty to the charges against him and after trial was ordered committed to an epileptic center. Subsequently, defendant escaped from the epileptic center and was apprehended. He was then taken before the trial court for sentencing and was sentenced. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in overruling his motion for a new trial, in withholding ruling on his motion to be discharged, proceeding with the case while such motion was pending, and never ruling on that motion, in denying him due process of law, and in proceeding without jurisdiction of the subject-matter involved or the jurisdiction of the person of defendant.The court noted that a defendant was entitled to have sentence pronounced with reasonable promptness. Unusual delay must be for some recognized legal purpose, and, even then, termination of the delay must be fixed. Accordingly, the court reversed the trial court judgment with instructions to enter judgment for defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment sentencing defendant after his escape from an epileptic center.

 

739 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Crawford v. Calumet Paving Co.


No. 29,053


Supreme Court of Indiana


233 Ind. 127; 117 N.E.2d 368; 1954 Ind. LEXIS 159



February 15, 1954, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Johnson Circuit Court, Oral S. Barnett, Judge.

Action by Robert Crawford to recover for injuries sustained as a result of an automobile accident occurring on State Highway No. 31 at a place where such highway was under construction by appellee. From the sustaining of a demurrer to his complaint, he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist sought review of a decision of the Johnson Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained the demurrer of appellee paving company to the motorist's complaint when the motorist brought an action for injuries that he suffered as a result of a car accident at a place where a highway was under construction by the paving company.


OVERVIEW: The motorist brought an action against the paving company for injuries that he suffered as a result of a car accident at a place where a highway was under construction by the paving company. The trial court sustained the paving company's demurrer to the complaint. On appeal, the motorist contended that the trial court erred in sustaining the demurrer. The court held that: (1) a state statute under which the paving company escaped liability was unconstitutional because it violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23, which provided that privileges and immunities were not to be granted to any citizen or class that did not, upon the same terms, apply to all; and (2) the facts stated in the motorist's complaint were such that reasonable men might draw different conclusions therefrom; hence, the question of the proximate cause of the alleged injury to the motorist was one that was to be submitted to a jury and was not a question of law to be decided on demurrer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and instructed the trial court to overrule the paving company's demurrer.

Shutt v. State


No. 29,086


Supreme Court of Indiana


233 Ind. 120; 117 N.E.2d 268; 1954 Ind. LEXIS 158



February 11, 1954, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Vanderburgh Circuit Court, Ollie C. Reeves, Judge.

Melvin Shutt was charged by affidavit with crime of robbery and also under habitual criminal statute. Appellant filed motion to quash affidavit under habitual criminal law which motion was overruled. Appellant filed other motions and objections which were also overruled and from a judgment on verdict of guilty, he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Vanderburgh County (Indiana), which convicted him of robbery and determined that he was a habitual criminal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with robbery and included in the charging affidavit was a further charge that he was a habitual criminal. The affidavit listed two prior felonies in another state and one prior felony in the forum state. Defendant requested that references to his status as a habitual criminal be removed from the affidavit. The trial court denied all requests to delete the information and convicted defendant. Defendant asserted that the affidavit was defective in that it failed to disclose the court and county of the asserted felonies in the other state. The court reversed the conviction and remanded the case with instructions that the trial court sustain the motion to quash that part of the affidavit that attempted to charge defendant with the status of a habitual criminal because the affidavit portion improperly omitted location information necessary for defendant to have proper notice of the claims made against him.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case with instructions to sustain the motion to quash that part of the affidavit that attempted to charge defendant with the status of a habitual criminal and other required proceedings.

Board of Zoning Appeals v. Decatur Co. of Jehovah's Witnesses


No. 29,119


Supreme Court of Indiana


233 Ind. 83; 117 N.E.2d 115; 1954 Ind. LEXIS 154



February 1, 1954, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Adams Circuit Court, Myles F. Parrish, Judge.

Action by Jehovah's Witnesses to secure permission to build a new church in the city of Decatur. The board of zoning appeals denied their request for a variance and they filed a petition for writ of certiorari in the Adams Circuit Court. The Circuit Court reversed the zoning board and this appeal is prosecuted.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. With instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Zoning Appeals (Board) challenged a finding of the Adams Circuit Court (Indiana), that reversed the Board's denial of appellee church's request for a zoning adjustment.


OVERVIEW: A church sought to build a new building in a city. The Board of Zoning Appeals (Board) denied the church's request for a variance, but the trial court reversed that decision. The Board appealed. Specifically, the Board contended that the church's plans did not comply with both the setback and parking requirements. The court found that the setback requirement was a reasonable exercise of the city's police power. However, the church could easily comply with that provision. On the other hand, the fact that there existed five other churches in the area without adequate off street parking such that they used the adjacent street parking, was evidence that the parking regulation was being applied unconstitutionally to the church, as a hindrance to freedom of worship. Thus, the trial court's judgment was reversed only insomuch as it was to restate its findings as a judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court, but demanded that it restate its findings as a judgment.

 

742 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Dowd v. Basham


No. 29,029


Supreme Court of Indiana


233 Ind. 207; 116 N.E.2d 632; 1954 Ind. LEXIS 173



January 18, 1954, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 1, 1954.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the LaPorte Circuit Court, Alban M. Smith, Judge.

Charles S. Basham was convicted on two charges and sentenced to Indiana Reformatory. He was paroled and while on parole, commited another crime and was sentenced. Upon commitment, Board of Trustees held hearing and found appellee to be parole violator, requiring him to serve five years of original sentences and then after this period discharged him on original sentences and gave him a new number and then required him to start serving sentence imposed while he was on parole. He filed petition for writ of habeas corpus which was granted and state appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State sought review of a judgment by LaPorte Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted appellee prisoner's petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted on two charges and sentenced to the Indiana Reformatory. He was later paroled. While on parole, the prisoner committed second degree burglary and was convicted and sentenced to a jail term. Upon commitment, the Board of Trustees of the Indiana State Prison held a hearing and found the prisoner to be parole violator, requiring him to serve five years of his original sentences. After the five-year period, the Board discharged the prisoner and required him to start serving the sentence imposed while he was on parole. The prisoner filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus, contending that he had completed serving his full maximum sentence for second degree burglary and that he was therefore entitled to discharge. The trial court granted the writ. On the State's appeal, the court held that the trial court erred in ordering the prisoner's release on writ of habeas corpus because the sentence imposed for burglary began to run on the date of the prisoner's discharge from the previous sentences. Ind. Stat. Ann. § 9-2250 (1953) operated to postpone the execution of the sentence for second degree burglary until the other sentences had been served or annulled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had granted the prisoner's petition for writ of habeas corpus, and remanded the cause to the trial court with instructions to deny the writ.

Dowd v. Grazer


No. 29,030


Supreme Court of Indiana


233 Ind. 68; 116 N.E.2d 108; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 287



December 15, 1953, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 29, 1954.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the LaPorte Circuit Court, Alban M. Smith, Judge.

Action by Leo E. Grazer upon an application for a writ of habeas corpus, challenging his conviction under habitual criminal statute. From an order discharging him from prison the state appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment from the LaPorte Circuit Court (Indiana) that granted defendant's application for a writ of habeas corpus, which challenged his conviction under the Indiana Habitual Criminal Statute and ordered that defendant be discharged from prison.


OVERVIEW: The State contended that the constitutionality of a statute may not be tested in a habeas corpus proceeding. The court held that the trial court that convicted and sentenced defendant had the jurisdiction to determine the constitutionality of the Indiana Habitual Criminal Statute, Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 9-2207 and 9-2207 (1942), which defendant failed to raise in the proceedings. The court also held that the proper remedy was for defendant to have appealed his conviction and sentence, which he did not do, but that defendant was not entitled to raise the constitutionality of the statute, when prior to his conviction, the statute had not been held unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded to the trial court for a new trial.

 

744 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. State


No. 28,986


Supreme Court of Indiana


233 Ind. 16; 115 N.E.2d 595; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 283



November 19, 1953, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 6, 1954. Certiorari Den. U.S. Sup. Ct. May 24, 1954.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Criminal Court of Marion County, Division 2, Thomas M. Scanlon, Special Judge.

Isaac Mitchell was charged by eight separate indictments with various violations of the gaming laws. From an adverse judgment he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision from the Marion Criminal Court, Division 2 (Indiana), which convicted defendant for violating the gaming laws. The criminal court denied motions to suppress, to change venue, and to quash the indictments. Defendant also filed a plea in abatement to each of eight indictments.


OVERVIEW: The police made a search under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-6111 (1950), which allowed for searches on the basis of citizen complaints. On appeal, the court found no reversible errors. The statute violated the Fourth Amendment because probable cause was a judicial determination. However, defendant waived the issue by denying ownership or interest in the property seized or the premises. The grand jury could have inquired into the offenses out of order. Legal conclusions that the State improperly influenced the grand jury could not be considered in pleas of abatement. There was no abuse in discretion in failing to change venue from the county. The motions to quash on the basis of incomplete indictments were correctly denied. Stating the exact amount of money involved or the description or method of the game was not required. The parties could have stipulated to consolidating the indictments. When that was done, defendant could not later complain that they should have been separated. Defendant was not entitled to three peremptory challenges for each indictment. Finally, there were no errors in the jury instructions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

745 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Green v. State


No. 29,020


Supreme Court of Indiana


232 Ind. 596; 115 N.E.2d 211; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 250



November 10, 1953, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Criminal Court, Division 2, Saul I. Rabb, Judge.

Affidavit against William C. Green for bigamy. Defendant filed a motion in arrest of judgment which was overruled and was found guilty. He appealed from a judgment on the verdict sentencing him to six months on the state farm and a fine of $ 1,000.00.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Marion County Criminal Court, Division 2 (Indiana), which convicted and sentenced defendant for the offense of bigamy. The trial court also denied defendant's motion in arrest of judgment.


OVERVIEW: After an Attorney General filed a brief with the court in which he confessed that the judgment should have been reversed, the court nonetheless addressed defendant's argument that the crime charged by affidavit was committed in Alabama and Florida and that under the Indiana Constitution, as well as the proper construction of Indiana statutes, no crime had been charged that was committed in Indiana. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had convicted and sentenced defendant for bigamy. Specifically, the court held that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-4204 (Repl. 1942) had to have been construed as limited to the act of contracting a bigamous marriage within the State of Indiana and that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-4205 (Repl. 1942), purporting to deal with the venue of the offense and the trial, was not intended to attempt to give courts of Indiana jurisdiction over a bigamous marriage consummated in another state. Thus, the court concluded that defendant's guilty verdict had been contrary to law and that defendant's motion in arrest of judgment should have been sustained. Accordingly, the court reversed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had convicted defendant of bigamy. As a result, the court instructed the trial court to sustain the motion in arrest of judgment.

 

746 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Harris v. Mutschler


No. 28,993


Supreme Court of Indiana


232 Ind. 580; 115 N.E.2d 206; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 248



November 5, 1953, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marshall Circuit Court, Henry S. Bailey, Special Judge.

The appellant, Philip J. Harris, as Prosecuting Attorney of the 54th Judicial Circuit, and others brought an information in the nature of quo warranto charging in substance that school city of Nappanee and Scott School Township failed to effect a de jure consolidation of schools under Ch. 123 of the 1947 Acts. (Section 28-5901 et seq., Burns' 1948 Replacement) or Ch. 268 of 1949 Acts (Section 28-5901 -- 28-5911, Burns' 1948 Replacement, Supp.) and sought to enjoin members of school board of consolidated school from acting as such and for declaratory judgment declaring no consolidation had been effected, and to declare all acts of officers of consolidated school corporation null and void.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a prosecuting attorney and associated parties, sought a review of a judgment from the Marshall Circuit Court, 54th Judicial Circuit, (Indiana) that sustained the demurrers of appellees, a township board, a mayor, and city council members, to appellants' quo warranto information to prevent appellees from consolidating two school districts and declare their actions in the process to consolidate null and void.


OVERVIEW: In their petition, appellants claimed that appellees had violated Ind. Stat. Ann. § 28-5901 et seq. (1948) and Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 28-5901 through 28-5911 (Supp. 1948)) in that appellees had failed to effect a de jure consolidation of the schools. The court determined that the statutes were neither unconstitutional nor void for uncertainty. The court held that the legislature, by virtue of Ind. Const. art. VIII, § 1, had the power to consolidate the school systems without notice to the voters and without any referendum by an election. The court also held that any defects in the process used by appellees to consolidate the schools were cured by the provisions of 1949 Ind. Acts. ch. 268, § 12, because after the effective date of 1949 Ind. Acts. ch. 204, the school system was a de jure municipal school corporation, which allowed it to be consolidated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Fairchild v. Schanke


No. 29,050


Supreme Court of Indiana


232 Ind. 480; 113 N.E.2d 159; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 225



June 29, 1953, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 4, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Superior Court of Marion County, No. 4, Walter Pritchard, Judge.

Leo Schanke, doing business as Novel Printing Company and others brought an injunction action against Frank H. Fairchild, Prosecuting Attorney, and other law enforcement officers from enforcing any of provisions of Acts of 1953, Ch. 147 on grounds of unconstitutionality. From a decree granting an interlocutory judgment, the appellants appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a prosecutor and other law enforcement officers, sought review of a decree of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which granted an interlocutory judgment to appellees in their action to enjoin the enforcement of 1953 Ind. Acts 147 as unconstitutional and void.


OVERVIEW: 1953 Ind. Acts 147 created gambling crimes and established penalties therefor. Section 2(8) of the Act excluded bona fide religious, patriotic, charitable, and fraternal clubs from the provisions of the Act. Appellees asserted that the exclusion was an arbitrary and invalid classification and that, therefore, the entire Act was invalid. On appeal, the court held that § 2(8) of the Act violated Ind. Const. art. 1, § 23 because the classification was neither reasonable nor based upon a substantial distinction with regard to the subject matter of the Act. The court further held that the entire Act was invalid and void because removal of § 2(8) of the Act broadened the scope of the Act, which was contrary to legislative intent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's interlocutory order granting a temporary injunction to appellees.

 

748 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


McClanahan v. State


No. 28,935


Supreme Court of Indiana


232 Ind. 567; 112 N.E.2d 575; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 245



June 2, 1953, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 3, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Huntington Circuit Court, Burr Glenn, Judge.

James R. McClanahan was found guilty of second offense of driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor and he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the Huntington Circuit Court (Indiana) of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicating liquor (DUI). The trial court overruled his motion for a new trial. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: After his arrest at about 12:30 a.m., defendant was taken to police headquarters. He argued that the trial court erred in admitting testimony as to his statements and condition at police headquarters because police had failed to comply with Ind. Stat. Ann. § 47-2307(4) (1952), requiring arrestees to be immediately taken before a magistrate in DUI cases. The court stated that it did not believe that the legislature intended to require an accused who was drunk or intoxicated to be brought before a magistrate. More important, the court stated, for § 47-2307 to be construed to be constitutional, it had to be limited to bringing an accused before a magistrate during his usual hours for conducting court. To hold otherwise would violate Ind. Const. art. III, § 1, which divided the powers of the Indiana government into three separate departments, in that the legislature would be attempting to hamper judicial functions or interfering with the discharge of judicial duties. The legislature could not require that magistrates conduct court 24 hours a day.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

749 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Nelson v. Haley


No. 28,984


Supreme Court of Indiana


232 Ind. 314; 111 N.E.2d 812; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 202; 32 L.R.R.M. 2152; 23 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P67,559



April 28, 1953, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 28, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Montgomery Circuit Court, Howard A. Sommer, Judge.

Action by John Haley to recover damages for injuries sustained arising out of assault and battery allegedly committed on plaintiff by Alphonso Nelson, against Nelson and others as representative of labor union, its members, agents and employees. From a judgment for plaintiff, defendants appealed. (Transferred from the Appellate Court under § 4-209, Burns' 1946 Replacement.)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to part. Set aside as to part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a union representative and the members, agents, and employees of the union, challenged a decision of the Montgomery Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted judgment in favor of plaintiff in his action to recover damages for injuries arising out of assault and battery committed on him by the union representative.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought suit for personal injuries that he received in an assault and battery committed on him by the union representative while serving as an agent and organizer for the union. The union was an unincorporated voluntary association of individuals. Judgment was rendered in plaintiff's favor. The court reversed the judgment as to the agents and employees of the union. It found that the naming of the union meant its members and, by naming the individuals as a representative of the union and not as a representative of the members, agents, and employees of the union, the agents and employees were never properly made parties to the suit. The court affirmed the judgment in all other respects, as there was ample evidence to sustain the finding that the union representative did commit the assault and batter. Further, the complaint clearly charged the union representative as an individual with the assault and battery and sought also to recover from the members of the union on the theory that he was acting on their behalf when the assault and battery was committed.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the judgment for plaintiff in his personal injury case as to the agents and employees of the union and affirmed the judgment in all other respects.

 

750 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Bryarly v. State


No. 28,970


Supreme Court of Indiana


232 Ind. 47; 111 N.E.2d 277; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 173



March 31, 1953, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Noble Circuit Court; Kenneth A. King, Judge.

Appellants brought a declaratory judgment action to have Section 10-703 Burns' 1942 Replacement, declared unconstitutional and void. A demurrer to the complaint was sustained and appellants refused to plead further and judgment was rendered accordingly from which judgment appellants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment from the Noble Circuit Court (Indiana), which found for appellee State in an action under the Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act, Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 3-1101 to 3-1116 (1946), that was brought to determine the constitutionality of the criminal statute upon which appellants' prosecution was based. Appellants filed the action after their motions to quash the charging affidavit were overruled.


OVERVIEW: Appellants moved to quash a charging affidavit, challenging the constitutionality of the statute upon which their prosecution for burglary was based. After the motions were overruled, appellants filed a declaratory judgment action, seeking to have the trial court pass upon the statute's constitutionality. Following an unfavorable judgment, appellants sought review. Upon review, the court held that persons having a property interest that might be affected by a mala prohibita criminal statute could have their status, rights, and other legal relations with reference to such statute determined by declaratory judgment. However, the court held that there was no authority for seeking a declaratory judgment to determine the rights, status, and other legal relations of a party with respect to a mala in se criminal statute. The court also held that appellants' question had been determined and that a declaratory judgment action could not substitute for an appeal. Finally, the court held that the statute did not limit appellants' legal rights; thus, the Act was inapplicable because the Act only gave courts the power to declare legal rights, legal statuses, and other legal relations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

751 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


East Chicago v. Sinclair Refining Co.


No. 28,794


Supreme Court of Indiana


232 Ind. 295; 111 N.E.2d 459; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 201



March 27, 1953, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Lake Superior Court, No. 4, Homer E. Sackett, Judge.

Sinclair Refining Company sought to determine the force and effect of a zoning ordinance as it related to its right in and to the use of land under the Declaratory Judgments Act. Court held ordinance unconstitutional insofar as it related to the company's land. The City of East Chicago appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a judgment from the Lake Superior Court (Indiana) entered in favor of appellee company, concluding that the challenged zoning ordinance of the city, insofar as it restricted the use of two parcels of the company's land, violated Ind. Const. art. 1, § 21, and the Fourteenth Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The company brought this action for declaratory judgment to determine the force and effect, if any, of the challenged amendatory zoning ordinance of the city as it related to the company's rights to the use of two of its parcels of land. The city contended that the trial court erred in overruling its motion for a new trial. The supreme court reversed the trial court's judgment with instructions to sustain the city's motion for a finding in its favor at the close of the company's evidence, and for further proceedings. Both 1947 Ind. Acts § 53-778 and City of East Chicago, Ind., Ordinance 2449 provided an administrative remedy for persons whose property was unreasonably restricted by the terms of a zoning ordinance or where, owing to special conditions, a literal enforcement of the ordinance would have resulted in unnecessary hardship. Where such an administrative remedy was provided, it must have been exhausted before judicial review was requested.


OUTCOME: Regarding the trial court's conclusion that the challenged ordinance of the city was unconstitutional as applied to the company, the supreme court reversed the trial court's judgment with instructions to sustain the city's motion for a finding in its favor at the close of the company's evidence, and for further proceedings.

 

752 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Gross Income Tax Div. v. Surface Combustion Corp.


Nos. 28,834, 28,835 consolidated


Supreme Court of Indiana


232 Ind. 100; 111 N.E.2d 50; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 181



March 19, 1953, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 21, 1953. Certiorari Denied U. S. Supreme Court October 12, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Marion Superior Court No. 3; William R. Higgins, Judge.

Appellee's predecessors in interest brought one of the consolidated causes of action to recover tax payments and interest allegedly improperly collected. Appellee brought the other action in its own name to recover payments made, together with interest. From a judgment for appellees, the state department appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee corporation filed a complaint to recover tax payments and interest allegedly improperly collected by appellant tax agency. The trial court granted judgment in favor of the corporation, from which the tax agency appealed.


OVERVIEW: The tax agency contended that the tax payments were lawful and should not be refunded. The corporation alleged that the tax collected was a tax on interstate commerce in violation of the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. 1, § 8(3). The corporation had manufactured large furnaces and sold them to a customer in the neighboring state where the tax was collected. The only work performed in the state was the putting together of the parts of the furnaces, and the installation and adjustment thereof. There was no evidence that the furnaces were built or fabricated in the state. The court held that the transactions involved were clearly sales of personal chattels in interstate commerce and that the installation and reassembling were inherently a part of the sale. The tax burdened and interfered with the free flow of interstate commerce and was invalid.


OUTCOME: Judgment to recover tax payments and interest in favor of the corporation was affirmed.

Department of State Revenue v. Estate of Callaway


No. 28,862


Supreme Court of Indiana


232 Ind. 1; 110 N.E.2d 903; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 167



March 16, 1953, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Benton Circuit Court, W. Douglas Elwood, Judge.

The Inheritance Tax Division filed an amended petition for reappraisement and redetermination of inheritance and transfer taxes pursuant to Section 6-2412 Burns' 1933. A demurrer to the petition was sustained and this appeal followed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of State Revenue, Inheritance Tax Division (department) sought review of the decision of the Benton Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained a demurrer to the department's amended petition for reappraisement and redetermination of inheritance and transfer taxes due by appellee estate. The petition was filed pursuant to Ind. Stat. Ann. § 6-2412 (1933).


OVERVIEW: The department argued on appeal that the trial court had erred in sustaining the estate's demurrer to its petition because the petition did state grounds for reappraisement and redetermination of inheritance and transfer taxes within the meaning of the Indiana Inheritance Tax Law. The court, finding no reversible error, affirmed the judgment. The court held that § 6-2412 was unconstitutional. The legislature, in attempting to permit the mandatory setting aside of the judgment of a probate court, violated the Indiana Constitution by infringing upon the judicial department of government. Section 6-2412 provided no discretion with a probate court, but, by the filing of a petition by the department, the original determination was set aside. The court decided that Ind. Const. art. III, § 1, which provided for three separate governmental departments, was violated by the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that sustained the estate's demurrer to the department's petition for reappraisement and redetermination of inheritance and transfer taxes.

 

754 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Evansville & O. v. R. Co. v. Southern Ind. Rural Electric Corp.


No. 28,916


Supreme Court of Indiana


231 Ind. 648; 109 N.E.2d 901; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 156



January 16, 1953, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 5, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Dubois Circuit Court, Eldo W. Wood, Judge.

The Southern Indiana Rural Electric Corporation brought an action against appellant utility company to collect penalty, attorney fees and costs provided by subsection (d), Section 55-4418, Burns' 1951 Replacement, and a demurrer to each paragraph of the third amended complaint was overruled and appellant then filed affirmative paragraphs of answer setting up unconstitutionality of Act. The alleged error assigned by appellant is the overruling of the demurrer.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility company challenged a judgment from the Dubois Circuit Court (Indiana), which overruled the utility company's demurrer in appellee rural electric corporation's action to collect a penalty, attorney fees, and costs for an alleged violation of a statute regarding electric distribution lines.


OVERVIEW: The rural electric corporation instituted an action against the utility company to collect a penalty, attorney fees, and costs pursuant to Ind. Stat. Ann. § 55-4418(d) (1951) for the allegedly illegal construction and operation of electric distribution lines. The trial court overruled the utility company's general demurrer to each paragraph of the third amended complaint in the case and entered a judgment in favor of the rural electric corporation. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court concluded that the utility company's demurrer to the rural electric corporation's third amended complaint should have been sustained. The court determined that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 55-4418(d) (1951) violated Ind. Const. art. I, § 23 because it was clearly class legislation. Section 55-4418(d) attempted to give rural electric corporations a right to collect penalties and excluded other utilities that were engaged in the same line of public utility service in the same territory from the benefit of the penalties. The court found that § 55-4418(d) did not apply upon the same terms to all in the same situation and that there was no apparent natural reason for any distinction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the rural electric corporation with instruction to sustain the utility company's demurrer.

 

755 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Protsman v. Jefferson-Craig Consol. School Corp.


No. 28,933


Supreme Court of Indiana


231 Ind. 527; 109 N.E.2d 889; 1953 Ind. LEXIS 148



January 9, 1953, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Switzerland Circuit Court, Harry E. Nichols, Judge.

Action by taxpayers (appellants) to set aside lease entered into by school corporation with school building corporation concerning a new school building. From a judgment for the defendants, the plaintiffs appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of the decision of the Switzerland Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered a judgment for appellees, lessee and lessor, in an action to set aside a lease for a new school building.


OVERVIEW: The lessee, the school corporation, and the lessor, the building corporation, entered into a lease under which the lessor would finance the acquisition of certain land and the erection of a school building thereon. In addition to rent payments, the lessee was required to provide for repairs, insurance, and taxes. The lease also contained a purchase option. The taxpayers filed an action to set aside the lease, claiming that the lease violated Ind. Cont. art. 13, § 1. The trial court entered a judgment for the lessee and lessor. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the fact that the lessee could, by paying a reasonable rental over a period of years, become the owner of the building, did not change the lease-contract into a contract to purchase the building, nor did it create a present indebtedness where none actually existed. Further, limitation of the activities in which the lessee and lessor might be required to engage in during the lease were impotent to effect such a change. Finally, because the evidence showed the necessity for the execution of the lease and that the rental was reasonable, no part of the rental payments could be purchase price payments in disguise.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision entering a judgment for the lessee and the lessor in the action to set aside the lease for the new school building.

 

756 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Indianapolis v. Brennan


No. 28,962


Supreme Court of Indiana


231 Ind. 492; 109 N.E.2d 409; 1952 Ind. LEXIS 172



December 18, 1952, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by Vinard S. Buckner, as a taxpayer, on behalf of himself and others similarly situated, filed his amended complaint against appellants under Declaratory Judgments Act for a declaration of rights, status, or other legal relations between the parties, and that Chapter 287, Acts of 1951 be declared unconstitutional. The court made special findings of fact and conclusions of law in favor of plaintiff, and this action is brought for a writ of prohibition against the court below.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ dissolved and permanent writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, city and associated individuals, sought a writ of prohibition against respondent judges regarding an order entering a judgment for the taxpayer in an action brought under the Declaratory Judgments Act for a declaration of rights, status, or other legal relations between the parties.


OVERVIEW: Relators alleged that the judges were without jurisdiction of the subject-matter of the action because certain additional parties named in the petition were not made parties defendant in the action. The court held that it was clear under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 3-1101 (1946) and Ind. Stat. Ann. § 3-1102 (1946), that the court and its judge had full and complete jurisdiction of the subject-matter of the action unless there was such a defect of parties defendant as to deprive them of jurisdiction thereof. Since it was undoubtedly the very purpose of the Declaratory Judgments Statute to give to "any person" whose rights, status or other legal relations were affected by a statute, the right to have any question of construction or validity arising under it determined and to have a declaration of rights, status or other legal relations thereunder, the court did not think that the jurisdiction of the trial court of the subject-matter of the action could possibly have depended upon whether everyone who might have had or claimed to have had an interest that would have been affected by the declaration were made parties to the action.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved the temporary writ of prohibition and denied writ permanently prayed for.

 

757 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Ennis v. State Highway Com.


No. 28,914


Supreme Court of Indiana


231 Ind. 311; 108 N.E.2d 687; 1952 Ind. LEXIS 153



November 17, 1952, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Superior Court, Room 2; Hezzie B. Pike, Judge.

Action by Samuel Ennis against the State Highway Commission of Indiana to obtain a declaratory judgment with respect to the Constitutionality of Chapter 281 of the Acts of 1951, more commonly known as the Toll Road Act.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of a judgment from the Marion Superior Court (Indiana), which found that the Toll Road Act (Act), 1951 Ind. Acts 281, was valid and not in violation of the United States Constitution or the Indiana Constitution after the individual filed a suit against appellees, State Highway Commission (commission) and officials, for an injunction to prevent enforcement of the Act.


OVERVIEW: The individual filed a suit against the commission and the officials, seeking a declaratory judgment that the act was unconstitutional and an injunction to prevent enforcement of the Act. After the superior court found that the Act was valid and not in violation of the Constitution of the United States or the Constitution of Indiana, the individual appealed. The court affirmed. The Act did not violate the Indiana Constitution. State real estate was not subject to payment of toll road revenue bonds. The Act did not create a state debt. Nor could state tax monies be used to pay the Act's revenue bonds. The Act did not create a private corporation. The Act's purposes were public in character. It did not provide for the disposition of the net income from any toll road project. It provided for the paying of all expenses and costs of the project, including the bonds. Under the Act, there could have been no net income involved. Commission funds could have been expended out of any funds available for the purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that found that the Act was valid and not in violation of the United States Constitution or the Indiana Constitution, in the individual's action against appellees for an injunction to prevent its enforcement.

Finkenbiner v. Dowd


No. 28,809


Supreme Court of Indiana


231 Ind. 416; 108 N.E.2d 261; 1952 Ind. LEXIS 164



October 23, 1952, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 5, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: From LaPorte Circuit Court, Lee L. Osborn, Judge.

Robert Finkenbiner having been committed to the Indiana State Hospital for the Criminal Insane by the Wabash Circuit Court, filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus in the LaPorte Circuit Court. A motion to quash the petition was filed by the state, and sustained. Appellant filed this appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a writ of habeas corpus in the LaPorte Circuit Court (Indiana) from his commitment to the hospital for the criminally insane by the Wabash Circuit Court (Indiana). The trial court granted the State's petition to quash the habeas corpus petition. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was found incompetent to stand trial for an assault on a police officer and was committed to the hospital for the criminally insane by the Wabash court. The warden subsequently notified the Wabash court that petitioner was restored to sanity, but the Wabash court held that petitioner was still incompetent to stand trial and returned petitioner to the mental hospital. Petitioner alleged that he was entitled to be released once the warden determined that he was returned to his sanity. The court held that the LaPorte court lacked jurisdiction to vacate a commitment made by the Wabash court. Once the Wabash court obtained jurisdiction over petitioner, the Wabash court retained jurisdiction. Only the Wabash court or the court, on appeal from a decision of the Wabash court, could order petitioner's release from the hospital for the criminally insane. The court held that Ind. Code Ann. § 22-1223 (1950) applied only to civil commitments and did not apply to criminal commitments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State ex rel. Gramelspacher v. Martin Circuit Court


No. 28,934


Supreme Court of Indiana


231 Ind. 114; 107 N.E.2d 666; 1952 Ind. LEXIS 133



September 10, 1952, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by the State of Indiana, on the relation of Robert E. Gramelspacher, against the Martin Circuit Court, and Eldo W. Wood, as Judge thereof, for a writ of prohibition to restrain further proceedings for a recount of votes cast at a primary election for office of representative to the General Assembly. A temporary writ of prohibition was issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ of prohibition dissolved and a permanent writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original action, petitioner, the State of Indiana, by relator, winner of a primary election, sought a writ of prohibition against respondents, the Martin Circuit Court, Indiana, and its presiding judge, to restrain further proceedings for a recount of votes cast at a primary election for state representative brought by the elected official's adversary. The court issued a temporary writ of prohibition. The trial court filed a response.


OVERVIEW: The winner of the primary election sought to stop his adversary from conducting a recount in the trial court. In considering a permanent writ of prohibition, the court found that the primary election did not comport with the requirements set forth in Ind. Const. art. IV, § 10. The court found that the constitutional provision only applied to general elections that resulted in a winner taking actual office. In denying the writ, the court found that the primary election only resulted in the winner taking a spot on the ballot in the general election. The court held that the trial court had jurisdiction under Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 29-5401 to 29-5417 (1949) to conduct a recount proceeding at the opposing candidate's request.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved the temporary writ of prohibition. The court denied a permanent writ of prohibition.

Property Owners, Inc. v. Anderson


No. 28,767


Supreme Court of Indiana


231 Ind. 78; 107 N.E.2d 3; 1952 Ind. LEXIS 129



July 23, 1952, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Madison Circuit Court, Cleon Wade Mount, Special Judge.

Action by Property Owners, Inc., and another against the City of Anderson and others to enjoin the defendants from issuing and selling Electric Revenue Bonds authorized by ordinance. From a judgment for defendants, plaintiffs appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant concerned citizens challenged the decision of the Madison Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied the citizens' request for a permanent injunction that would have prohibited appellee city from issuing and selling electric revenue bonds authorized by ordinance. The citizens had filed an action against the Indiana Public Service Commission to prevent the approval of the bond issuance, but a decision was entered against them.


OVERVIEW: The city wanted to update its obsolete electric power plant and passed an ordinance that authorized the issuance of revenue bonds for such purpose. The Indiana Public Service Commission approved a rate and increase and the amount of the bond issue. The ordinance was read in full at a public meeting and the adoption of the ordinance complied with the laws of Indiana. It was not necessary to issue a declaratory resolution to the vote of the people of the city.

State ex rel. Ayer v. Ewing


No. 28,878


Supreme Court of Indiana


231 Ind. 1; 106 N.E.2d 441; 1952 Ind. LEXIS 123



June 20, 1952, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by the State of Indiana on the relation of Frank Ayer against Urdix B. Ewing, Judge of the Spencer Circuit Court, and the Spencer Circuit Court for a writ of prohibition to prohibit the respondents from exercising further jurisdiction in a cause pending in respondent court. A temporary writ of prohibition issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ of prohibition made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator trustee brought an original action against respondents, circuit court and its judge, seeking a writ of prohibition to prevent respondents from exercising further jurisdiction in a pending cause instituted by a verified accusation for the removal of the trustee under § 35 of the Impeachment Act of 1897, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 49-836, based on the trustee's alleged refusal and neglect to perform his official duties.


OVERVIEW: The trustee contended the verified accusation did not state facts essential to give respondents jurisdiction under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 49-836. The court agreed and issued the permanent writ of prohibition, holding that: (1) the only averment in the verified accusation was that the trustee neglected and refused to consider the applications of two individuals for employment as school teachers; (2) a condition precedent to the employment of any teacher was that the applicant was a licensed teacher or that the superintendent had made a required report concerning him, which had not been averred; (3) it was not unusual for a township trustee to have more teacher applicants than he had positions to fill; (4) no law required the trustee to give a good reason why he employed some and did not employ others; (5) because the trustee employed qualified teachers for the schools in his township, he properly performed his duties; (6) failure to perform just one duty required by law was not sufficient for impeachment; (7) there was not a general failure to perform official duties alleged; therefore, (8) the pleading was insufficient to confer jurisdiction to hear the impeachment charges brought.


OUTCOME: The court made the temporary writ of prohibition permanent to prevent respondents from exercising further jurisdiction in the pending cause for removal of the trustee for his alleged refusal and neglect to perform official duties.
