PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion of October 1, 1951, Reported at 230 Ind. 277.

 

763 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Ballman v. Duffecy


No. 28,799


Supreme Court of Indiana


230 Ind. 220; 102 N.E.2d 646; 1952 Ind. LEXIS 185



January 7, 1952, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 1, John L. Niblack, Judge.

Proceeding on a petition by Charles W. Ballman and others for a writ of certiorari to review a decision of the Board of Zoning Appeals of the City of Indianapolis against Michael J. Duffecy and others. From a judgment dismissing the petition, petitioners appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana). The trial court dismissed appellants' petition for a writ of certiorari to review a decision from the Board of Zoning Appeals of the City of Indianapolis (board).


OVERVIEW: After the board granted a variance, appellants filed a petition for a writ of certiorari to review the decision pursuant to Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 53-783, 53-784, and 53-785 (1951). The trial court dismissed the petition, agreeing with appellees that its statutory jurisdiction to hear the controversy had not been timely invoked. The court affirmed. Pursuant to § 53-783, a party aggrieved by any decision of the board had to present a petition to the trial court within 30 days of the decision. The statutory time limit was necessary so the trial court could enter an order that set the date to show cause why a writ should not issue and the time for the return of the writ. This procedure was jurisdictional and mandatory. Where a statute provided the remedy of judicial review and specified the procedure to be followed, an aggrieved party had to comply with the procedure. The statute was not unconstitutional because the procedure for review did not prohibit the remedy of judicial review. Because appellants had failed to present their petition to the court within the prescribed time, the trial court had not acquired jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed a petition for certiorari to review a decision of the board, which had granted a variance.

Witte v. Dowd


No. 28,718


Supreme Court of Indiana


230 Ind. 485; 102 N.E.2d 630; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 237



December 20, 1951, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 10, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the LaPorte Superior Court, Robert S. Baker, Judge.

Petition by John Witte against Alfred F. Dowd, as Warden of the Indiana State Prison, for a writ of habeas corpus. From a judgment quashing the writ, petitioner appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought review of a judgment of the LaPorte Superior Court (Indiana), which sustained a motion to quash a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had entered a plea of guilty to a charge of forgery and to being an habitual criminal. The inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, contending that the trial court had failed to pronounce a sentence of imprisonment against him for a specific term on the forgery charge as required by Ind. Stat. Ann. § 9-2208 (1942). The trial court had simply imposed a life term due to his status as an habitual criminal, and the State was unsuccessful in its effort to correct the judgment nunc pro tunc. The trial court quashed the writ. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that although the failure to impose a specific sentence for the forgery count was an irregularity, the judgment was not void, and the inmate was in no way harmed because the life sentence was proper under the Habitual Criminal Act. The irregularity did not deprive the trial court of jurisdiction to impose the life sentence, and the judgment was not subject to collateral attack by habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

765 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Sutton v. State


No. 28,758


Supreme Court of Indiana


230 Ind. 62; 101 N.E.2d 636; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 218



November 14, 1951, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Grant Circuit Court, Oliver D. Clawson, Judge.

Ernest L. Sutton was convicted in the City Court of Marion of the offense of unlawfully peeping into an occupied residence and he appealed to the Grant Circuit Court. From an order sustaining the state's motion to dismiss the appeal and remand the cause to the city court for the execution of the judgment of that court, he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the Grant Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained the State's motion to dismiss defendant's appeal from a city court conviction on the offense of unlawfully peeping into an occupied residence, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-4910-12. The circuit court accepted the State's contention that more than 90 days had passed since the city court judgment and remanded the case to city court for execution of its judgment.


OVERVIEW: After conviction, defendant appealed to the circuit court, and the transcript of the city court proceedings was duly filed in the circuit court. About 93 days after the city court judgment, the State filed its written motion to dismiss. Defendant insisted that the statute authorizing dismissal if the appeal was not decided within 90 days, 1935 Ind. Acts ch. 169 (1935 Act), was expressly repealed by 1939 Ind. Acts ch. 112 (1939 Act). The 1935 Act was amended in the interim by 1937 Ind. Acts ch. 152, § 1 (1937 Act), which allowed the parties to seek an extension of the 90-day period. Though the 1939 Act expressly repealed the 1935 Act, the 1937 Act was never repealed. The court held that, although only the 1935 Act was expressly repealed by the 1939 Act, the 1937 Act fell within the repeal, as the 1937 Act was not complete within itself or understandable and enforceable without reference to the 1935 Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's decision to dismiss the appeal and remand the case to city court with instructions to overrule the State's motion to dismiss and to reinstate the appealed case on the circuit court's docket.

State ex rel. Standard Oil Co. v. Review Board of Indiana Employment Sec. Div.


No. 28,751


Supreme Court of Indiana


230 Ind. 1; 101 N.E.2d 60; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 205



October 11, 1951, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 3, William Higgins, Judge.

Action by the State of Indiana on the relation of the Standard Oil Company (Indiana) against the Review Board of the Indiana Employment Security Division and others for a writ of prohibition to prevent respondents from hearing and determining sixteen claims for unemployment compensation benefits. A temporary writ was issued. From a judgment dissolving that writ and denying a permanent writ, the relator appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which dissolved a temporary writ of prohibition and denied a permanent writ of prohibition to prevent appellee administrative board from hearing and determining 16 claims for unemployment compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: The employer obtained a temporary and alternative writ of prohibition to stop the administrative board from hearing and determining 16 claims for unemployment compensation benefits. The lower court dissolved the temporary writ and denied a permanent and absolute writ of prohibition but the court reversed. The court found that the lower court had jurisdiction to issue the writ but that the employer had no other remedy available at law. The court found that review in the appellate court would not be adequate because the employer would have to deal with all 16 cases separately, which would be costly and time consuming. The writ was timely sought and the employer did not waive its right to seek the writ because the right to challenge the jurisdiction of a court over the subject matter could never be lost or waived. The court instructed the lower court that it should grant the permanent and absolute writ of prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court and ordered that the permanent and absolute writ of prohibition be granted.

Todd v. State


No. 28,697


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 664; 101 N.E.2d 45; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 200



October 4, 1951, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Jackson Circuit Court, Fred S. Matthews, Special Judge.

Ralph D. Todd was convicted of automobile banditry, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of automobile banditry by the Jackson Circuit Court (Indiana). Defendant appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the State's instruction regarding the weight to be given to an accomplice's testimony did not inform the jury that the State was required to prove defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt in order to convict him. The court agreed. The instruction given by the trial court did not define what was intended by the words "if her testimony should be found sufficiently satisfactory to the jury," and the jury could easily have had the impression that a conviction would be authorized on the uncorroborated testimony of an accomplice even though the testimony did not convince the jury of defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The instruction purported to be complete on the subject of accomplices, and its giving to the jury was prejudicial error. The court also noted that the trial court erroneously admitted evidence that defendant's wife had given forged checks to other people. However, none of the recipients of the checks, nor any officer of the drawee bank testified that the checks were forged or fraudulent. The admission of the evidence of similar crimes was error because it did not make out a prima facie case of uttering forged documents.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment with instructions to the trial court to sustain defendant's motion for a new trial.

 

768 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Public Service Com. v. Marion Circuit Court


No. 28,819


Supreme Court of Indiana


230 Ind. 277; 100 N.E.2d 888; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 235



October 1, 1951, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Dissenting Opinion Filed January 25, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original action by the State of Indiana on the relation of the Public Service Commission of Indiana against the Marion Circuit Court and Lloyd D. Claycombe, sole Judge of the Marion Circuit Court, for a writ of prohibition and mandate to compel respondents to withdraw and set aside an order granting a temporary injunction and to prohibit respondents from any further proceedings therein. A temporary writ issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ dissolved and permanent writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator Indiana Public Service Commission filed a petition for a writ of prohibition and mandate to compel respondents, a trial court (Indiana) and a trial court judge, to set aside an order granting a temporary injunction to a telephone company to enjoin the Commission from interfering with the rates charged by the telephone company and to prohibit any further proceedings by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The telephone company filed a petition with the Commission requesting an increase in rates. Due to its dissatisfaction with the Commission's order prescribing new rates, the telephone company filed an action in the trial court under Ind. Code Ann. § 54-429 (1951) to set aside the order on the ground that it was insufficient, unreasonable, and unlawful. The trial court granted the telephone company's request for a temporary injunction. The Commission sought a writ of prohibition against the trial court. The court denied the Commission's request for a permanent writ, concluding that the trial court had the authority to review the Commission's order and to issue injunctions. The trial court's order did not attempt to fix rates but merely permitted the telephone company to charge certain rates to maintain the status quo or to preserve the telephone company's solvency until a final determination could be made due to the unenforceability of the Commission's insufficient order. The injunction was just an interlocutory order, not a decision on the final merits, and thus special findings were not required. The trial court did not exceed its jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved its temporary writ and denied the Commission's request for a permanent writ.

 

769 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Evansville City Coach Lines, Inc. v. Rawlings


Nos. 28,779, 28,780


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 552; 99 N.E.2d 597; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 191



June 25, 1951, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 18, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original actions by the State of Indiana on the relation of the Evansville City Coach Lines, Inc., against The Honorable John D. Rawlings, Judge of the Superior Court of Vanderburgh County, Indiana, and that court for a writ of mandate and prohibition to restrain respondents from exercising further jurisdiction in two proceedings therein pending. A temporary writ of prohibition and an alternative writ of mandamus were issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ of prohibition made permanent; alternative writ of mandamus made absolute.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator common carrier sought a writ of mandate and prohibition against respondent trial court judge to restrain the judge from exercising further jurisdiction in two consolidated actions filed by two unions that challenged the Indiana Public Service Commission's approval of a tariff and bus fares for the common carrier.


OVERVIEW: The common carrier filed a schedule of a proposed new tariff and bus fares, and the Commission suspended the operation of the new tariff for 90 days based on protests by the unions. The Commission subsequently approved a new proposed tariff without notice to the unions' attorneys. The unions filed two actions, which were consolidated, challenging the Commission's orders. The trial court issued a restraining order without notice, enjoining the common carrier from collecting the new bus fares. The common carrier sought a writ of mandate and prohibition against the trial court judge. The court issued a temporary writ of prohibition and an alternative writ of mandamus. The court subsequently made the writs permanent, concluding that: (1) the unions had an adequate remedy at law by petitioning the Commission, which prevented the trial court judge from issuing an injunction; (2) the unions were not denied due process of law because neither the Commission nor the common carrier was required to give notice to the public generally or to those who used the service; and (3) the trial court judge improperly attempted to fix the rates and invaded the province of the Commission.


OUTCOME: The court made its temporary writ of prohibition against the trial court judge permanent and its alternative writ of mandamus absolute and ordered the trial court judge to set aside his orders in the unions' actions.

Lucas v. State


No. 28,686


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 633; 99 N.E.2d 419; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 197



June 21, 1951, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 2, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Allen Circuit Court, William H. Schannen, Judge.

Action by the State of Indiana on the relation of the Board of Medical Registration and Examination of Indiana against Paul F. Lucas to enjoin defendant from practicing medicine without a license. From a judgment granting a permanent injunction, defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual challenged the decision from the Allen Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted a permanent injunction to the state on the relation of the Board of Medical Registration and Examination to enjoin the individual from practicing medicine without a license.


OVERVIEW: The individual was permanently enjoined from practicing medicine without a license and he appealed, arguing that the Medical Practice Act, Ind. Code Ann. § 63-1305 was unconstitutional. On appeal the court noted that the state's right to regulate chiropractors was constitutional. Therefore the individual had to have a license before he could practice. The court noted that the individual made no attempt to comply with the rules and statutes set out for chiropractic regulation. The court held that even though there was the potential for the board members to have a pecuniary interest in the licensing of chiropractors, in the individual's case, none of the members had such an interest; therefore they did not have to be recused. Finding no error, the court affirmed the permanent injunction.


OUTCOME: The permanent injunction granted to enjoin the individual from practicing medicine without a license was affirmed.

State ex rel. Indiana Alcoholic Beverage Com. v. Superior Court of Vanderburgh County


No. 28,776


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 483; 99 N.E.2d 247; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 176



June 8, 1951, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by the State of Indiana on the relation of the Indiana Alcoholic Beverage Commission against the Superior Court of Vanderburgh County and John D. Rawlings, as Judge thereof, to prohibit respondents from exercising further jurisdiction in a suit, pending in respondent court, to enjoin the relator from enforcing its order suspending a beer and wine permit. A temporary writ of prohibition was issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ of prohibition made permanent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator Indiana Alcoholic Beverage Commission brought an action to prohibit respondent Vanderburgh Superior Court from exercising jurisdiction in a suit pending in that court in which individual permittees sought to enjoin the Commission from enforcing its order suspending a beer and wine permit. The Commission urged that the Superior Court had no jurisdiction to act under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 12-443(B) (Supp. 1949).


OVERVIEW: The permittees were charged with selling alcohol to a minor and their permit was suspended. They brought the suit in the superior court to enjoin the Commission from enforcing its suspension order and to have Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 12-443(a) and (b) (Supp. 1949) declared unconstitutional. The superior court dissolved a restraining order issued against the Commission but granted a stay of judgment pending appeal. The Superior Court refused to discharge a rule brought against the Commission for failing to return the permit pending the appeal. On consideration of whether to make a temporary writ of prohibition permanent, the court held that (1) a restraining order and injunction would only be granted when property rights were involved, and § 12-443(b) specifically provided that there was no property right in a beer and wine permit; (2) the superior court might have had jurisdiction of the parties and the subject matter, but it had no jurisdiction over the class of case involved and so could not act; and (3) the superior court had no jurisdiction to issue a citation for contempt where it had no jurisdiction to issue the injunction in the first place.


OUTCOME: The court made the temporary writ permanent.

 

772 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Indianapolis Rys., Inc. v. Indianapolis


No. 28,698


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 487; 98 N.E.2d 505; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 177



May 4, 1951, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 11, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Hancock Circuit Court, Samuel J. Offutt, Judge.

Action by the City of Indianapolis against Indianapolis Railways, Incorporated, and another for a declaratory judgment to have determined the rights of the parties under the grade separation statutes. From an adverse judgment, the named defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city sought a declaratory judgment against appellant railway to determine the parties' rights under the grade separation statutes, Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 48-3401 to 48-3410 (1950) and §§ 55-1810 to 55-1812 (1951). The railway sought to have the statutes declared unconstitutional as applied to it. The Hancock Circuit Court (Indiana) declared the rights of the parties and held the statutes to be constitutional. The railway appealed.


OVERVIEW: The railway refused to pay its share of the cost of a grade separation project. The railway argued that the Legislature did not grant to the city the right to apportion costs in grade separations, and that if the city's board of public works apportioned the costs its action was void because it did not have jurisdiction to do so, and the action was therefore unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Ind. Const. art. 1. The court noted that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 55-1810 set out formulas for the division of costs of grade separation, but made no attempt to apportion the division, while Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-3402 (1950) provided for apportionment of the costs. The Legislature in setting up the division of costs did not attempt to apportion the costs and thus did not repeal the right of the board of public works to apportion the costs of the grade separation as provided in the division of costs. In both Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 48-3402 and 55-1810, a street railway company, where the highway was occupied by its tracks, was responsible for five per cent of the costs. The Legislature divided the costs, and left to the board of public works the apportionment of the costs as divided.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

773 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Board of Medical Registration & Examination v. Frasure


No. 28,749


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 315; 98 N.E.2d 365; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 156



April 26, 1951, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Fulton Circuit Court, Kline D. Reed, Judge.

Action by the State of Indiana on the relation of the Board of Medical Registration and Examination of Indiana against A. L. Frasure to enjoin defendant from engaging in the practice of medicine without a license. From an order denying a temporary injunction, plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Board of Medical Registration and Examination of Indiana sought review of an order of the Fulton Circuit Court (Indiana), which denied its motion to enjoin appellee from engaging in the practice of medicine without a license under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 63-1311 (1943).


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that appellee had an office, where he held himself out as a practicing chiropractor and administered chiropractic treatments for pay for which he had no license. Under such circumstances, the trial court had no discretion in the matter and had to grant a temporary injunction as a matter of law. Appellee argued that the trial court could not have issued a temporary injunction against him because he had not entered a general appearance to the action. The court found that the jurisdiction of the trial court did not depend upon an appearance by appellee, nor could appellee, by failing or refusing to "submit" to the jurisdiction of the trial court, forestall action on its part. The trial court had full jurisdiction to decide whether a temporary injunction should have issued. The court concluded that if appellee's answer would not have availed appellee on the issue of the granting of a permanent injunction, when raised by answer, it could not have availed him on the issue of a temporary injunction, when raised by plea in abatement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment with directions to enter an order temporarily enjoining appellee from engaging in the practice of medicine without a license.

Department of Public Sanitation v. Solan


No. 28,680


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 228; 97 N.E.2d 495; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 140



March 22, 1951, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Lake Superior Court, Room No. 1, Joseph V. Stodola, Judge.

Action by Joseph E. Solan, as a citizen and taxpayer of the City of Hammond on behalf of himself and all other persons similarly situated, against the Department of Public Sanitation of the City of Hammond, Indiana, and others to enjoin defendants from executing and issuing or selling bonds to secure proceeds for the construction of a sewage disposal system. From a judgment for plaintiff, defendants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city Department of Public Sanitation and others, appealed a judgment from the Lake Superior Court, Room No. 1 (Indiana), which was entered in favor of plaintiff city taxpayer in his suit to enjoin defendants from executing and issuing or selling bonds to secure proceeds for the construction of a sewage disposal system.


OVERVIEW: The city sanitary district was created by a city ordinance that adopted Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 48-4201 to 48-4228 (1950). Later, the town was incorporated into the city sanitary district. The district then adopted a resolution to sell 30-year bonds of the district payable from a tax levy to be made annually by the board of sanitary commissioners on the taxable real and personal property in the district. The proceeds were to be used for the construction of sewers, pumps, and buildings. The taxpayer argued that the bonds were unconstitutional because they would create a city indebtedness beyond the two percent limitation in Ind. Const. art. XIII, § 1. The court agreed with the Department that the bonds were not payable out of the general fund of the municipalities in question, but out of a special fund to be raised by a special tax. Because such debts were not debts of the government subdivisions, they could not infringe Ind. Const. art. XIII, § 1. As a "local public improvement," the sewage system justified the creation of a separate taxing district from which to raise funds to accomplish the extension and improvement of the sewers, pumps, and buildings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the taxpayer and instructed the trial court to sustain defendants' motion for a new trial.

Dowd v. Harmon


No. 28,606


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 254; 96 N.E.2d 902; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 146



March 1, 1951, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 4, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the LaPorte Circuit Court, Lee L. Osborn, Judge.

Action by Herbert E. Harmon against Alfred F. Dowd for a writ of habeas corpus. From a judgment for petitioner ordering his release from the Indiana Hospital for Insane Criminals and delivery to the custody of the Superintendent of the Indiana Village for Epileptics, defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the warden of the Indiana Hospital for Insane Criminals, sought review of a decision of the LaPorte Circuit Court (Indiana), which granted petitioner mental patient's request for habeas corpus relief and ordered the release of the patient from the Indiana Hospital for Insane Criminals and his delivery to the custody of the Superintendent of the Indiana Village for Epileptics.


OVERVIEW: The patient was committed to the Indiana Village for Epileptics and three years later, he was transferred to the Indiana Hospital for Insane Criminals. He asserted that he was not a criminal, had never been convicted of a crime, was not an insane person, and that no court of competent jurisdiction had ever committed him to the Indiana Hospital for Insane Criminals. On appeal from the judgment granting the petition, the court reversed. It was prejudicial error for the trial court to refuse to grant the warden's motion for a change of judge as a petition for a writ of habeas corpus was a civil proceeding from which change of venue from the judge could be had under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 2-1402 (1946). Ind. Stat. Ann. § 22-4201 (1950) vested in the Indiana Council for Mental Health the right to transfer the patient. On its face, this transfer met the requirements of the statute. The Indiana Hospital for Insane Criminals was held not to be a penal institution. The transfer was not a violation of either the Constitution of Indiana or the Federal Constitution as due process was afforded to the patient at the time he was originally committed to the Indiana Village for Epileptics.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting the patient's petition for habeas corpus relief and ordering his release from the Indiana Hospital for Insane Criminals was reversed and remanded.

State ex rel. Beaman v. Circuit Court of Pike County


Nos. 28,742, 28,743


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 190; 96 N.E.2d 671; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 134



February 14, 1951, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Two original actions by the State of Indiana on the relation of Edwin W. Beaman against the Circuit Court of Pike County and Lester Nixon, as Judge thereof, and the Circuit Court of Gibson County and A. Dale Eby, as Judge thereof, for writs of mandate and prohibition to restrain further action in recount proceedings pending in respondent courts. Temporary writs of prohibition and alternative writs of mandamus were issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writs of prohibition made permanent; alternative writs of mandamus made absolute.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator State filed an original action against respondents, Circuit Court of Pike County (Indiana) and its judge, and the Circuit Court of Gibson County (Indiana) and its judge, for writs of mandate and prohibition to restrain further action in recount proceedings pending in respondent courts.


OVERVIEW: A losing candidate in a senatorial race requested a recount after an election for the senatorial district under Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 29-5401, 29-5417. The circuit courts granted the recount. The State was granted a temporary writ of prohibition to prevent the recount. The court held that the statute was unconstitutional and void. Thus, the circuit courts did not have jurisdiction to perform judicial or ministerial acts. The circuit courts exceeded their authority by proceeding with the recount. The court therefore had jurisdiction to issue a writ of mandate and prohibition. The court found that the statute was an adjudication of the election rather than a tool for discovery. Accordingly, the court made the temporary wits of prohibition permanent and made absolute the alternative writs of mandate.


OUTCOME: The court made the temporary writs of prohibition permanent, and the alternative writs of mandate were made absolute.

W. A. Barber Grocery Co. v. Fleming


No. 28,664


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 140; 96 N.E.2d 108; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 127



January 11, 1951, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 5, Ralph Hamill, Judge.

Action by W. A. Barber Grocery Co., Inc., and others against Charles F. Fleming, as Secretary of State of the State of Indiana, and as Commissioner of the Department of the Bureau of Motor Vehicles, and others, for a declaratory judgment that chapter 258 of the Acts of 1949 be declared unconstitutional, for an injunction against the enforcement thereof and for a declaration of the validity of chapter 169 of the Acts of 1949. From a judgment declaring the latter act valid, section one of chapter 258, Acts of 1949, invalid, the remainder of chapter 258 valid, and denying an injunction, plaintiffs appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commercial taxpayers sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which was entered in favor of appellees, the Secretary of State and the Commissioner of the Department of the Bureau of Motor Vehicles, in the taxpayers' suit for a declaratory judgment. The taxpayers argued that 1949 Ind. Acts 258 was unconstitutional and sought an injunction against its enforcement.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted the taxpayers' request insofar as it declared the validity of 1949 Ind. Acts 169 and declared 1949 Ind. Acts 258(1) invalid. However, the taxpayers appealed the portion of the trial court's judgment declaring the remainder of 1949 Ind. Acts 258 valid and denying the taxpayers' requested injunction. The challenged act provided for the registration and licensing of motor vehicles, trailers, and semi-trailers. The taxpayers argued that the act made the licensing and regulation a tax measure, in violation of Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. The court disagreed and held that the challenged act was general and embracing one subject and, therefore, did not violate either state or federal constitutions. As to the severability of the portion of the act declared unconstitutional, the court held that the remaining portions were workable and severable. Finally, the court held that the classifications set forth in the challenged act, which required taxpayers to estimate their gross weight for taxation classification purposes, did not subject taxpayers to a shockingly disproportionate punishment, should their declared weight be different from their estimated weight.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State ex rel. Acker v. Reeves


No. 28,741


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 126; 95 N.E.2d 838; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 125



January 8, 1951, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by the State of Indiana on the relation of Walter Acker and others against the Honorable Ollie C. Reeves, as Judge of the Vanderburgh Circuit Court, and the Vanderburgh Circuit Court for a writ of prohibition and a writ of mandate to prevent respondents from ordering a recount of votes cast in an election for state representatives. A temporary writ of prohibition and an alternative writ of mandate were issued.



DISPOSITION: Temporary writ of prohibition made permanent; alternative writ of mandate made absolute.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner political candidates filed an original action against respondents, a circuit court and its judge, seeking a writ of prohibition and a writ of mandate to prevent the circuit court from ordering a recount of votes cast in an election for state representatives. A temporary writ of prohibition and an alternative writ of mandate were issued.


OVERVIEW: Unsuccessful political candidates for Indiana State Representative challenged the election of the successful candidates. The successful candidates argued that the circuit court was without jurisdiction of the subject matter of the action. That in ordering a recount of the ballots for the offices, the circuit court had exceeded its lawful jurisdiction, and that it would continue to act beyond its jurisdiction unless prohibited from so doing by the court. The court agreed. The court noted that Ind. Const. art. 4, § 10, provided that the Indiana House of Representatives had sole and exclusive jurisdiction to judge the election, qualifications, and returns of its own members. The circuit court asserted that they assumed jurisdiction in the cases because of the authority granted by the Indiana Election Code art. 27, §§ 324, 325. The court noted that the constitution was the supreme law that effectively controlled legislatures, congresses, executives, courts and the people. To the extent the statute in question sought to grant the power to review legislative elections to the courts, it was necessarily unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: The court made the temporary writ of prohibition permanent and the alternative writ of mandate absolute.

State ex rel. McCormick v. Superior Court of Knox County


No. 28,745


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 118; 95 N.E.2d 829; 1951 Ind. LEXIS 124



January 5, 1951, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Action by the State of Indiana on the relation of Robert S. McCormick against the Superior Court of Knox County and the Honorable Sidney Gelb, as Judge thereof, for an alternative writ of mandamus and a temporary writ of prohibition to stay recount proceedings in the respondent court. The writs were issued.



DISPOSITION: Alternative writ of mandamus and temporary writ of prohibition vacated and annulled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Knox County (Indiana) issued a writ of mandamus and a temporary writ of prohibition to stay recount proceedings in respondent court. Relator contestee argued that if the contestor was issued a second certificate as a result of a recount then the contestee would have been denied the benefit of the statutory election contest.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered a recount of the ballots for the office of county prosecutor and trustee of two counties. The trial court appointed recount commissioners. At the time of recount an action for an alternative writ of mandamus and temporary writ of prohibition was granted, which stayed the recount. The contestee, who had received the majority of the votes in the election, alleged that Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 29-5401 to 29-5417 (1949) was unconstitutional because it provided no provision for the contestee to contest a second certificate of election issued to a contestor. The court found that under Ind. Stat. Ann. § 29-5413 (1949) when a recount was invoked, every candidate was protected because it required a court order to impound and protect all ballots, voting machines, tally sheets, and names and addresses of registered voters. The contestee also had the benefit of a recount in the presence of his watcher. The court further found that the contestee had a remedy by way of a quo warranto. Accordingly, the court vacated and remanded the mandamus and writ.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and annulled the alternative writ of mandamus and temporary writ of prohibition.

State ex rel. McManamon v. Blackford Circuit Court


No. 28,717


Supreme Court of Indiana


229 Ind. 3; 95 N.E.2d 556; 1950 Ind. LEXIS 96



December 1, 1950, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action by the State of Indiana on the relation of J. Emmett McManamon and J. Alfred Hollander, as Prosecuting Attorney of the 71st Judicial Circuit, against the Blackford Circuit Court and Max C. Peterson, as Judge thereof, for a writ of prohibition to prevent respondents from entertaining a prisoner's motion, filed more than five years after his conviction, to vacate the judgment of conviction. A temporary writ of prohibition issued.



DISPOSITION: Petition denied; temporary writ vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Based upon Ind. Stat. Ann. § 9-3301 (Supp. 1949), petitioner, the State of Indiana, commenced an original action for a writ of prohibition to issue against respondents, the Blackford Circuit Court and the Circuit Court judge, to prevent respondents from hearing defendant's motion to vacate his judgment of conviction more than five years after the conviction. A temporary writ issued.


OVERVIEW: On the same day that he was charged by affidavit with the crime of larceny, he pled guilty to crime without counsel present, and he was convicted on his plea. Several years later, while in the state reformatory, defendant moved to vacate the judgment of conviction. The State based a demurrer to defendant's motion on § 9-3301, and argued that because more than five years had expired since defendant's conviction, the circuit court no longer had jurisdiction over the matter. The demurrer was overruled, as was the State's motion for a rehearing. The State then commenced an original action for a writ of prohibition against respondents. The court held that the State's petition should be denied. The court determined first that defendant's motion to vacate was in effect a motion for a writ of error coram nobis. The court then held that defendant should be allowed to present its case and the circuit court should be allowed to determine if defendant acted with due diligence in bringing the petition. Further, the court found that defendant's case was proper for the writ of error coram nobis because the issue of defendant's constitutional right to counsel was involved.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the temporary writ and denied the State's petition.

Prunk v. Indianapolis Redevelopment Com. of Dep't of Redevelopment


No. 28,509


Supreme Court of Indiana


228 Ind. 579; 93 N.E.2d 171; 1950 Ind. LEXIS 172



June 27, 1950, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 31, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Superior Court of Marion County, John L. Niblack, Hezzie B. Pike, William R. Higgins, Jr., Walter Pritchard and Ralph Hamill, Judges.

Proceeding by Pauline and Byron F. Prunk against the Indianapolis Redevelopment Commission of the Department of Redevelopment of the City of Indianapolis and others to review the action of the Commission in overruling plaintiffs' remonstrances and confirming a resolution declaring real estate owned by plaintiffs to be a blighted area. From an adverse judgment, plaintiffs appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which overruled the owners' remonstrances to appellee Indianapolis Redevelopment Commission's declaratory resolution that the owner's real estate was a blighted area. The Commission filed a motion to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The Commission adopted a resolution declaring that the owners' real estate was a blighted area and that it would be of public utility and benefit to acquire and redevelop it. The owners filed remonstrances, alleging that the action was unconstitutional. The remonstrances were overruled and the resolution was approved. The owners appealed to the trial court, where they moved to dismiss their remonstrances but not their appeal. The trial court held that the appeal was not dismissed and ruled in favor of the Commission. The Commission moved to dismiss a further appeal, insisting that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-8515 (1950) limited the right to appeal in the trial court to the question of public utility and benefit and further provided that there was no appeal from the trial court's judgment. The court held this provision unconstitutional. However, the court also noted that the owners' constitutional questions were not properly presented to the trial court. The remonstrances did not specify any constitutional provision that was violated, and they were in any case dismissed on the owners' motion so that there was nothing of record before the trial court presenting any constitutional issue.


OUTCOME: The court overruled the Commission's motion to dismiss the appeal, and the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

782 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Gross Income Tax Div. v. Bartlett


Nos. 28,609, 28,610, 28,611


Supreme Court of Indiana


228 Ind. 505; 93 N.E.2d 174; 1950 Ind. LEXIS 162



June 19, 1950, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 4, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Marion Circuit Court, Lloyd D. Claycombe, Judge. Actions by Robert Bartlett, both individually and as trustee, against the Gross Income Tax Division, State of Indiana, and others to recover taxes paid under the Gross Income Tax Act of 1933. From judgments for the plaintiff, defendants appeal. The appeals have been consolidated.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Gross Income Tax Division, State of Indiana, and others, sought review of certain judgments of the Marion Circuit Court (Indiana), which were entered in favor of appellee subdivision developer. The developer had filed actions against appellants to recover taxes paid under the Indiana Gross Income Tax Act of 1933 (Act).


OVERVIEW: The developer had acquired real property in Indiana for purposes of resale. The developer argued that because his organization's efforts to successfully sell the property took place in Illinois, not Indiana, he was entitled to a correction of taxes paid on the property under the Act. Appellants filed an answer denying the correctness of the developer's assertions. The trial court ruled in favor of the developer. The court reversed. The court held that the developer's contention that the receipts involved were derived from and attributable to activities or sources outside the State of Indiana, which the State of Indiana could not have properly or legally taxed, was without merit. Under the Act, the word "gross income" meant total receipts. With respect to the developer's situation, the taxable event was the receipt of income from the sale of lots in Indiana ,and the taxable income consisted entirely of such receipts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court with instructions to render judgment for and in behalf of appellants.

 

783 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sutherlin


No. 28,631


Supreme Court of Indiana


228 Ind. 587; 92 N.E.2d 923; 1950 Ind. LEXIS 173



June 16, 1950, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 31, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Putnam Circuit Court, Horace L. Hanna, Special Judge.

Proceeding for the removal of John Sutherlin from the office of Sheriff of Putnam County. From a judgment sustaining defendant's objections to the accusation of the grand jury, the State appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a judgment of the Putnam Circuit Court (Indiana), which sustained defendant sheriff's objections to a grand jury accusation on the basis that the accusation did not state facts sufficient to constitute cause for the sheriff's removal from office.


OVERVIEW: The grand jury accusation charged that there was cause to remove the sheriff based on incidents involving punchboards and an incident in which the sheriff allegedly told a lodge officer to allow the installation of a slot machine if he wanted the sheriff's help. The sheriff moved to dismiss the State's appeal on the ground that the State had no statutory authority to appeal. The court held that Ind. Stat. Ann. § 2-3201 (1946) provided for an appeal by the State from a final adverse judgment in proceedings for the removal of a county officer. Disregarding the evidentiary allegations as surplusage, and considering the averments of fact, the accusation stated sufficient cause for removal. While the sheriff correctly insisted that there was no statutory crime of conspiracy to commit a misdemeanor in Indiana, all persons concerned in the commission of a misdemeanor were liable as principals. As to the punchboard charge, the keeping or exhibiting of such devices was prohibited, but no laws prohibited an attempt to do the prohibited acts. The charges concerning punchboards did not charge that any completed offense had been committed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment with instructions to overrule the objections to the accusation.

Department of Financial Institutions v. Johnson Chevrolet Co.


No. 28,615


Supreme Court of Indiana


228 Ind. 397; 92 N.E.2d 714; 1950 Ind. LEXIS 149



June 8, 1950, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 5, Ralph Hamill, Judge.

Action by Johnson Chevrolet Company against the Department of Financial Institutions to enjoin the enforcement of a general order adopted by defendant. From a judgment perpetually enjoining enforcement of the order, defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Financial Institutions appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana) overruling defendant's demurrer to plaintiff's action to enjoin the enforcement of new rules promulgated by defendant limiting the commissions paid to insurance agents.


OVERVIEW: Defendant Department of Financial Institutions enacted a rule limiting the ability of a retail seller to collect commissions for selling insurance. Plaintiff car dealership was not licensed to sell insurance, but did so and collected commissions from the sales. As a result, plaintiff filed an action to prevent enforcement of the rule and defendant filed a demurrer. The court overruled the demurrer and defendant appealed. On appeal, the court found that in order for plaintiff to sell insurance, plaintiff was required to file for a license. Furthermore, the court found that since plaintiff was not licensed to sell insurance, plaintiff could not collect commissions. Therefore, the court found that plaintiff came into court without clean hands since plaintiff was in violation of the law, and the court reversed the decision overruling defendant's demurrer.


OUTCOME: The judgment overruling defendant's demurrer was reversed since plaintiff was not an insurance agent and was selling insurance without being licensed by the state.

786 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. 28,515


Supreme Court of Indiana


227 Ind. 672; 87 N.E.2d 881; 1949 Ind. LEXIS 179



October 7, 1949, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 8, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Vigo Circuit Court, Ernest M. Wright, Judge Pro tem.

Forrest Eugene Smith was convicted of the offense of vehicle taking and sentenced to life imprisonment under the habitual criminal act, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the life imprisonment sentence that he received following his conviction by the Vigo Circuit Court (Indiana) for vehicle taking. The application of the habitual criminal act, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 9-2207 (1942), was central to the dispute between the parties.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's first trial on vehicle taking charges, there was a hung jury. The State then filed a second count for the offense of vehicle taking, and it alleged pursuant to § 9-2207 that defendant was an habitual criminal. At his second trial, defendant was found guilty of vehicle taking, and he was found to have had two previous felony convictions. Thus, defendant was sentenced to life in prison. Upon appeal, the trial court's judgment was affirmed. The court held that § 9-2207 did not charge a crime, but it only classified defendant as an habitual criminal. Thus, it did not make bad character a part of defendant's original case, and it was not impeaching. Further, § 9-2207 did not impose an additional penalty on crimes for which defendant had already been convicted. Rather, it imposed a heavier penalty for the commission of a felony by one who had been previously twice convicted and imprisoned for the commission of a felony. Thus, § 9-2207 was not an ex post facto law and did not violate U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 or Ind. Const. art. 1, § 24. The court also ruled that neither Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-3010 (1942) nor Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-3011 (1942) repealed the habitual criminal act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Rappaport v. Department of Public Health & Hospitals


No. 28,534


Supreme Court of Indiana


227 Ind. 508; 87 N.E.2d 77; 1949 Ind. LEXIS 161



July 5, 1949, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 5, Ralph Hamill, Judge.

Action by Leo M. Rappaport, a taxpayer, for himself and others similarly situated, against the Department of Public Health and Hospitals of the City of Indianapolis, and others, to enjoin defendants from letting contracts for, or issuing bonds to defray the cost of, additions to the City Hospital on the grounds that it would constitute an evasion of the municipal debt limitation imposed by the Constitution. From a judgment for defendants, plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instruction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which found in favor of defendants, the Department of Public Heath and Hospitals of the City of Indianapolis and related parties, in the taxpayer's action to enjoin the Department from letting contracts for, or issuing bonds to defray costs of, additions to a hospital on the grounds that it constituted an evasion of the municipal debt limitation.


OVERVIEW: The Department took preliminary steps to build additions and improvements to a city hospital and to issue a large sum of bonds to defray the costs of the new facilities. The taxpayer filed an action to enjoin the Department, but the trial court found in favor of the Department. The taxpayer appealed and contended that the issuance of the bonds would constitute an evasion of the debt limitation imposed upon the city by the Ind. Const. art. 13. The court agreed and held that hospitals were not local improvements for which special assessments could be levied. The court held that the Acts of 1945, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 200, as amended by the Acts of 1947, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 48-8401, et seq., to the extent that the Acts permitted indebtedness beyond the two percent debt limitation of the city, were an evasion of the Indiana Constitution. The fact that the new bonds sought to be issued would not, if charged against the city, increase the city's indebtedness beyond two percent did not render the issuance of such bonds free from attack. They were issued according to procedure set up in the part of the Acts of 1945 and 1947, which the court found to be repugnant to the Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and ordered a new trial.

 

788 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Department of Financial Institutions v. General Finance Corp.


No. 28,397


Supreme Court of Indiana


227 Ind. 373; 86 N.E.2d 444; 1949 Ind. LEXIS 145; 10 A.L.R.2d 436



June 9, 1949, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Superior Court of Marion County, Room No. 5, Ralph Hamill, Judge.

Action by General Finance Corporation against Department of Financial Institutions, and others, for a declaratory judgment to test the constitutionality of an amendment to the Retail Instalment Sales Act, and for an injunction.

From judgment for the plaintiff, defendants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee state department of financial institutions sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Marion County (Indiana), which granted judgment in favor of appellant finance company in the finance company's action which sought to declare an amendment to Section 9 of the Indiana Retail Installment Sales Act, as amended by 1947 Ind. Acts ch. 238, Ind. Code § 58-909 (1947 Supp.), unconstitutional and enjoin its enforcement.


OVERVIEW: The finance company was engaged in the business of buying retail sales contracts within the state and selling them to out-of-state financial institutions. Section 9 of the Indiana Retail Installment Sales Act, Ind. Code § 58-909 (1947 Supp.), was amended to provide that installment contracts could only be sold to entities that were licensed under the act. Subsequently, the finance company filed an action which sought to declare the amendment unconstitutional and sought to enjoin the department from enforcing the amendment. The trial court granted judgment in favor of the finance company. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the finance company had standing to challenge the amendment, despite the facts that it was a licensee under the act and the amendment had not gone into effect. The court concluded that although the amendment may have had a valid state purpose, the prohibition of a right to contract within another state concerning the property of the finance company within the state was a denial of due process of law and violated the Commerce Clause by restricting the market for contract sales and credit within the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, which granted judgment in favor of finance company in the finance company's action which sought to declare an amendment to Section 9 of the Indiana Retail Installment Sales Act unconstitutional and enjoin its enforcement.

Kirtley v. State


No. 28,479


Supreme Court of Indiana


227 Ind. 175; 84 N.E.2d 712; 1949 Ind. LEXIS 124



March 29, 1949, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Marion Criminal Court, Division Two, Saul I. Rabb, Judge.

Action by the State of Indiana against Ottis F. Kirtley for allegedly having unlawfully offered for sale tickets to State High School Basketball Finals at a price greater than the original price. Defendant's motions to quash and in arrest of judgment were overruled, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions to sustain defendant's motion to quash the affidavit.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Marion Criminal Court, Division Two, (Indiana), which overruled defendant's motion to quash and motion in arrest of judgment. Defendant had been convicted of having unlawfully offered for sale tickets to a basketball game at a price greater than the original price.


OVERVIEW: Defendant offered to sell $ 3 tickets to the Indiana State High School Basketball Finals for $ 25. He was convicted of having unlawfully offered for sale tickets at a price greater than the original price under Ind. Code Ann. § 10-4913 (Repl. 1942). The judgment was affirmed on appeal. On further appeal, the court reversed the decision of the lower courts and held that the statute was void. The court found that § 10-4913 interfered with the liberties, the personal and property rights of defendant and had no relation whatever to the protection of the public health, morals, safety or welfare. It could not be justified as a proper exercise of police power. The statute did not seek to regulate the resale of tickets to entertainment, but to prevent the resale by removing the element of profit.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for offering to sell basketball tickets at a price higher than the original price was reversed and the statute under which defendant was convicted was declared void.

Curry v. Maynard


No. 28,481


Supreme Court of Indiana


227 Ind. 46; 83 N.E.2d 782; 1949 Ind. LEXIS 110



February 8, 1949, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Vigo Circuit Court, Juvenile Division; Ernest M. Wright, Judge pro tem.

George Curry was found guilty of indirect contempt of court for failure to comply with court's order to support a child after court had established defendant as the father of a child born out of wedlock to Gertrude Maynard, and the defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed from the judgment of the Vigo Circuit Court, Juvenile Division (Indiana), which found the father guilty of indirect contempt of court for failure to comply with the trial court's order to support a child after the trial court had established the father as the father of a child born out of wedlock.


OVERVIEW: In the original action, the father was found to be the father of the child born to the plaintiff mother and was ordered to pay to the clerk of the court the sum of $ 30 per month. On the father's failure to comply with the support order, the juvenile court found the father guilty of indirect contempt. On appeal the father contended that the original petition failed to confer jurisdiction of the person and subject matter and that the original judgment violated the Fifth Amendment on the ground that it was entered in the father's absence. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) the petition did not deprive the juvenile court of jurisdiction because the petition complied substantially with Ind. Stat. Ann. § 3-633 (Burns' 1946), and the fact that the verified petition in the original action contained the words "bastard child," instead of "child born out of wedlock," did not make the petition faulty; (2) the original judgment was not in conflict with the Fifth Amendment because the Fifth Amendment operated exclusively in restriction of federal power; and (3) the juvenile court had jurisdiction of the paternity proceedings under Ind. Stat. Ann. §§ 9-3102, -3103 (Burns' 1947 Supp.).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding the father guilty of indirect contempt of court for failure to comply with the support order.

Gingerich v. State


No. 28,455


Supreme Court of Indiana


226 Ind. 678; 83 N.E.2d 47; 1948 Ind. LEXIS 211



December 30, 1948, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Jay Circuit Court, Byron G. Jenkins, Judge.

Chester Gingerich was convicted of violation of the Compulsory School Attendance Law for permitting, compelling or encouraging his 14 year old son to remain absent from public high school, contrary to the statute, and he appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Circuit Court of Jay County (Indiana), which convicted him of violation of the Compulsory School Attendance Law for permitting, compelling, or encouraging his 14 year old son to remain absent from public high school.


OVERVIEW: The school district where defendant lived with his family was closed because of lack of attendance and the student population was consolidated with another school district. Defendant maintained religious beliefs that discouraged attendance in public school at the end of elementary school. When defendant's son discontinued school defendant was convicted for encouraging the son's failure to attend high school. Defendant asserted that: (a) there was no school in his township for his son to attend; (b) the mandatory attendance law was unconstitutional; and (c) the sentence assessed was excessive. The court affirmed the conviction because it determined that: (1) the mandatory attendance requirement did not specify that the student attend a particular school so that the failure of the township to maintain a school did not prevent defendant's son from attending another qualified school in another district; (2) defendant could not present a constitutional challenge on appeal that had not been presented to the trial court by a motion to quash or a motion in arrest of judgment; and (3) the sentence was within the terms of the statute and could not be challenged on appeal as too severe.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

792 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Board of Comm'rs v. State


No. 28,424


Supreme Court of Indiana


226 Ind. 633; 82 N.E.2d 891; 1948 Ind. LEXIS 207



December 23, 1948, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Adams Circuit Court; Earl B. Adams, Special Judge.

Action by the State of Indiana on the relation of Elmer Gibson and others against the Board of Commissioners of Adams County and others to compel the defendants to issue bonds for the construction of the Fenning Drain. From the judgment mandating defendants to issue such bonds, the defendants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions to enter judgment for appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Board of Commissioners of Adams County, Indiana, and others, sought review of a decision from the Adams Circuit Court (Indiana), which entered an order to issue bonds for the construction of a drain in an action brought by plaintiffs, a ditch commission and the owners of the land which was assessed for the construction of the drain.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered an order for the Board to issue bonds for the construction of a drain. The action was preceded by another case, with different participants, which resulted in a denial of the same mandatory relief and held that the proceeding was terminated by virtue of the Contractors Relief Act of 1919, 1919 Ind. Acts 93. On appeal, the court set the judgment aside, holding that the prior case barred relitigation of the same issues. The fact that the contractor named as relator in the first action was not the one named in the second action was immaterial. It was also immaterial that the statute upon which the trial court based its first finding and judgment was afterward declared unconstitutional. Jurisdiction in the trial court was not lost when the trial court entered a judgment that denied the relief sought. The trial court may have erred, but that error could have been corrected on appeal. The ditch commissioner and landowners could not relitigate the same matter that was concluded by a decision that was never questioned by an appeal, which stood as a final judgment governing the rights of the parties in the drain proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment with instructions to enter judgment for the Board.

State v. Griffin


No. 28,391


Supreme Court of Indiana


226 Ind. 279; 79 N.E.2d 537; 1948 Ind. LEXIS 161



May 27, 1948, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] From the Lawrence Circuit Court; Chester A. Davis, Judge.

Bert Griffin was charged by affidavit with visiting a gambling house, to which he filed a motion to quash, which was sustained, and the State of Indiana appealed.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Indiana appealed from the judgment of the Lawrence County Circuit Court (Indiana) sustaining defendant's motion to quash an affidavit charging him with visiting a gambling house on grounds that the affidavit did not state a public offense, in that the applicable statute, Ind. Stat. Ann. § 10-4219 (1942), was unconstitutional and void under U.S. Const. amend. XIV; Ind. Const. art. I, § 23; and Ind. Const. art. IV, §§ 19, 22, and 23.


OVERVIEW: The statute prohibited "male persons" from, inter alia, visiting houses of ill fame or gambling houses. The affidavit was quashed, and defendant was discharged, on his claim that the statute contained an unconstitutional classification and violated his privileges and immunities. In reversing on appeal, the court ruled that the title of the act at issue gave fair notice of its contents so as not to mislead those to be bound, as required by Ind. Const. art. IV, § 19. The statute did not grant a privilege or immunity to anyone and its limitation to male persons was a reasonable classification founded on substantial distinctions in the subject matter and designed to protect the morals and welfare of the public, consistent with Ind. Const. art. I, § 23. The statute applied to all who came within its provisions and did not violate the special law and general law provisions of Ind. Const. art. IV, §§ 22 and 23. Finally, defendant could not claim a privilege to visit a gambling house or be immune from regulation under the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded with instructions to overrule the motion to quash and for further proceedings.

 

794 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stabb


No. 28,360


Supreme Court of Indiana


226 Ind. 319; 79 N.E.2d 392; 1948 Ind. LEXIS 169



May 21, 1948, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 21, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the Marion Circuit Court; Lloyd D. Claycombe, Judge.

Condemnation proceedings by the State of Indiana, on behalf of the State Highway Commission, to appropriate lands of the defendants. From a judgment for $ 18,000 for defendants, the plaintiff appealed.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the State of Indiana on behalf of the State Highway Commission (Indiana), brought appropriation proceedings against appellee property owners. Appraisers were appointed, and they assessed an amount of damages. The owners filed exceptions, and they were awarded a jury trial. The Marion Circuit Court (Indiana) entered judgment in favor of the owners, and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Commission sought the owners' property for the construction of a highway. On their property, the owners operated a retail store and gasoline station. At the jury trial before the circuit court, the owners presented evidence as to the store's annual business and the station's annual sales of gasoline. The State requested that the circuit court instruct the jury that, among other things, the owners were not entitled to recover for any loss of business or profits; the circuit court refused the State's request. On appeal from the owners' judgment, the court held that the evidence pertaining to the store's business and the station's gasoline sales was properly admitted to prove that the appropriated property was suitable for business purposes. The court also held that the circuit court properly refused the State's tendered instruction regarding losses of business or profits because Ind. Stat. Ann. § 3-1706 (1946) authorized such damages in an appropriation case. Specifically, because the first three clauses of § 3-1706 provided damages sustained by property taken, the fourth clause of § 3-1706 necessarily referred to damages other than damages to the property involved.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

795 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 82A04-9812-CR-620


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FOURTH DISTRICT


721 N.E.2d 327; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2209



December 29, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Carl A. Heldt, Judge. Cause No. 82C01-9808-CF-762.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction after jury trial by the Vanderburgh Circuit Court (Indiana) for stalking as a Class C felony under Indiana Law, Ind. Code § 35-45-5(b)(3) (1998).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for stalking under Ind. Code § 35-45-10-5(b)(3), since he came to the victim's house several times within a few hours, calling her names and threatening her. Because he was previously charged with stalking, defendant's second count was enhanced, even though defendant was acquitted of the first charge. The court held the evidence supported a finding that defendant was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. It did not matter that the harassment occurred over a period of only several hours. Defendant's harassing behavior occurred more than once, and was thus deemed "repeated" under the statute. The evidence supported a finding that the victim actually felt terrorized. The enhancement of defendant's penalty based on the prior stalking charge was constitutional since the pending stalking charge was proved beyond a reasonable doubt, defendant was not deprived of a jury trial and the enhancement was related to the characteristics of stalkers.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed because evidence supported finding that defendant was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt and that the victim was actually felt terrorized by defendant's actions; enhancement of defendant's penalty constitutional and thus affirmed.

 

796 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Geiger v. State


No. 57A03-9809-CR-417


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


721 N.E.2d 891; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2218



December 28, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE NOBLE COUNTY CIRCUIT COURT. The Honorable Kevin P. Wallace, Special Judge. Cause No. 57C01-9705-CF-50.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed from a jury decision in the Noble County Circuit Court (Indiana), which convicted him of bribery and official misconduct, asserting that the court improperly instructed the jury, improperly excluded extrinsic impeachment evidence, and denied defendant his constitutional right of confrontation.


OVERVIEW: The jury in the lower court convicted defendant of bribery and official misconduct. The reviewing court reversed, holding that, without sufficient explanation, infirm language in a jury instruction on intent, where intent was an element of the crimes charged, unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof and was fundamental error that could not be waived by defendant's failure to object. The court next weighed and assessed the sufficiency of the evidence in support of the convictions, in order to ensure that any retrial would not be barred by principles of double jeopardy. When the jury instructions were considered together, the court determined that the jury was adequately instructed that the "property" defendant was accused of accepting was money. When defendant did not meet his burden of showing the relevance of the information he claimed was erroneous to exclude, there was no abuse of discretion in its exclusion.


OUTCOME: Convictions reversed, because a fundamental infirmity in a jury instruction, unconstitutionally shifting the burden of proof on the element of intent, could not be waived by defendant's failure to object.

 

797 of 1699 DOCUMENTS


Lockett v. State


No. 02A03-9905-CR-184


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


720 N.E.2d 762; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2190



December 20, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 26, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 2235.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE ALLEN SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Francis C. Gull, Judge. Cause No. 02D04-9810-CF-551.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Allen Superior Court (Indiana) denying his motion to suppress evidence obtained by a warrantless search of the vehicle in which he was driving. The trial court certified the issue as to whether law enforcement officers may routinely ask a driver stopped for a traffic infraction if he has a weapon in the vehicle.


OVERVIEW: At 2:20 a.m., two police officers on patrol stopped a car being driven erratically. Defendant rolled down the window, and the officer detected a smell of alcohol emanating from the vehicle. The officer asked defendant whether he had any weapons in the vehicle. After exiting the car, defendant responded that he had a weapon under the front driver's seat. The officer looked and could see the gun sticking out underneath the seat. Defendant was charged with carrying a handgun without a license. The court held that prior to making an inquiry about the presence of weapons an officer must: (1) either be warranted in believing that his safety was threatened; or (2) the question must reasonably relate to the basis for the traffic stop, such as stopping a suspected armed burglar or bank robber. Because neither was present, the gun must be suppressed as a fruit of the illegal question.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded. The gun must be suppressed as a fruit of the illegal question about the presence of weapons because an officer was not warranted in believing that his safety was threatened, nor did his question reasonably relate to the basis for the traffic stop.

Reed v. State


No. 20A03-9902-CR-72


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


720 N.E.2d 431; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2106



December 6, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE ELKHART SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Stephen Platt, Judge. Cause No. 20D02-9902-CF-85.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Elkhart Superior Court (Indiana), following a jury trial, convicting him of a class A felony under Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6(b)(3)(B), the possession of at least three grams of cocaine or narcotic drug within one thousand feet of a public park.


OVERVIEW: Defendant violated a restraining order by going to his former wife's residence and was arrested for invasion of privacy. During the booking process at the jail, some rock-like items were found in the toe of defendant's shoe. The rocks subsequently tested positive for cocaine. The weight of the rock cocaine was 8.9 grams. The court held that: (1) because defendant failed to file a motion to dismiss raising a constitutional challenge to Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6, the claim was waived; (2) the argument that Ind. Code § 35-48-4-6 was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to set forth a specific method for measuring the 1,000 foot "drug-free zone" failed on its own merits, waiver notwithstanding, because there is nothing indefinite or uncertain in its language; and (3) the jury instruction that stated a surveyor's line-of-sight technique was an appropriate method of measurement was proper.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed. The constitutional challenge to the statute was waived by failing to file a motion to dismiss. Nevertheless, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it failed to set forth a method for measuring a drug-free zone; and the jury instruction stating that surveyor's line-of-sight technique was an appropriate method of measurement was proper.

Area Plan Comm'n of Evansville & Vanderburgh County v. Major


No. 82A01-9812-CV-472


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, FIRST DISTRICT


720 N.E.2d 391; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2040



November 30, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 1, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ind. App. LEXIS 2233.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE VANDERBURGH SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable Robert J. Tornatta, Judge. Cause No. 82D03-9601-CP-72.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant area plan commission and county challenged a Vanderburgh Superior Court (Indiana) judgment which awarded plaintiff temporary and permanent damages for the taking of his property.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an area plan commission and county, appealed a judgment awarding plaintiff temporary and permanent damages for defendant's taking of plaintiff's property in plaintiff's suit alleging that defendant had improperly revoked plaintiff's first improvement location permit, constituting a temporary and permanent taking of his property without just compensation in contravention of the United States and Indiana Constitutions. The court reversed and remanded, holding that, although the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction to consider at least a portion of the plaintiff's taking question, under the doctrine of primary jurisdiction, the trial court erred by deciding that the permit had been improperly revoked, as this question should have been reserved for the local board of zoning appeals' (board) determination in the first instance. The trial court was required to stay its proceedings while plaintiff appealed the propriety of the initial permit revocation to the board.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded; under the doctrine of primary jurisdiction, the trial court erred by deciding that plaintiff's first improvement location permit was improperly revoked. The trial court was required to stay its proceedings while plaintiff appealed the propriety of the permit revocation to the zoning appeals board.

Holmes v. Jones


No. 50A03-9901-CV-33


COURT OF APPEALS OF INDIANA, THIRD DISTRICT


719 N.E.2d 843; 1999 Ind. App. LEXIS 2032



November 22, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE MARSHALL SUPERIOR COURT. The Honorable R. W. Chamblee, Jr., Judge. Cause No. 50D01-9802-PO-13.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent appealed from the permanent protective order entered against him in the Marshall Superior Court (Indiana), challenging the trial court's denial of his motion for appointed counsel under Ind. Code § 34-1-1-3, now Ind. Code §§ 34-10-1-1 and -2, the state pauper counsel statute.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, the adoptive parents of respondent's son, petitioned for a permanent protective order seeking to stop respondent's continuing efforts to challenge the adoption and contact their son. Acting pro se respondent moved the court for appointment of pauper counsel to represent him in the protective order hearing. In support of his motion respondent made uncontroverted representations that he was incarcerated, had no income, property, or assets, and that he could not afford to hire counsel. On appeal, respondent asserted the trial court erred in denying him pauper counsel in the hearing on the permanent protective order. Holding that respondent's uncontroverted representations of indigency could not be reconciled with Ind. Code § 34-1-1-3, now Ind. Code §§ 34-10-1-1 and -2, the State pauper statute, the court reversed and remanded with instructions to appoint counsel, or, in the alternative, to conduct a hearing to determine whether respondent was indigent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded, holding that, given respondent's uncontroverted representations of his own indigency, the State's pauper counsel statute required the trial court to appoint respondent counsel or hold a hearing to determine respondent's indigency.
